Nikah — Marriage

Mahr al-Mithl in a Fasid Marriage After Consummation
Ruling on compensation mahr in fasid marriage after consummation with cap.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr in a fasid marriage after consummation and apply the cap to the agreed amount.

Core Idea
In a fasid marriage, mahr al-mithl is wajib due to intercourse, but is capped at the agreed amount.

In this lesson, we examine a specific rule from Hanafi fiqh: what mahr is owed when a fasid marriage has been consummated? The source passage provides a clear ruling: the woman receives mahr al-mithl, but limited to the amount they agreed upon. This balances compensation for intercourse with honoring the mutual agreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage addresses a fasid marriage that has been consummated. The ruling is that the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl, but this amount cannot exceed the mahr specified in the contract (musamma).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites an athar from 'Ata: 'Whoever marries not according to the proper way of marriage and then divorces, it is not counted as anything; he only divorced someone not his wife.' This shows that a fasid marriage does not create full contractual rights.
The athar is from Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The athar implies that the marriage is invalid; thus only actual intercourse triggers compensation (mahr al-mithl), not the contract itself. The cap on the agreed amount honors the parties' mutual consent.
The ruling uses qawl sahabi as proof, which is a secondary source.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may hold that the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl without the cap, since the tasmiyah (specification) is void in a fasid contract.
Hanafis give weight to the parties' agreement even in a fasid contract.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi and is based on the principle that although the marriage is defective, compensation for intercourse is limited by what was mutually agreed, as a measure of fairness.
This ruling is part of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۸۱۲] (۸۷) واذا دخل بها فلها مهر مثلها ولا يزاد على المسمى ۔ نکاح فاسد میں عورت سے صحبت کرے تو عورت کے لئے مهر مثل ہوگا۔ لیکن یہ مهر مثل آپس میں جتنا مہر طے کیا ہے اس سے زیادہ نہ ہو۔ مثلا آپس میں پانچ سو درہم مہر طے کیا ہے اور مهر مثل چھ سو درہم ہے تو پانچ سو درہم ہی دیئے جائیں گے چھ سو درہم نہیں دیئے جائیں گے۔ نکاح فاسد اصل میں نکاح ہی نہیں ہے لیکن چونکہ صحبت کر چکا ہے اس لئے مجبورا مهر مثل کا فیصلہ کیا جائے گا۔ اور چونکہ دونوں کم پر راضی ہو گئے ہیں اس لئے کم دیا جائے گا (۲) نکاح فاسد نکاح نہیں ہے اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ عن عطاء قال من نكح على غير وجه النكاح ثم طلق فلا يحسب شيئا انما طلق غير امرأته (ج) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب النکاح علی غیر وجہ النکاح ج سادس ص ۲۰۳ نمبر ۱۰۵۱۰) اس اثر میں ہے کہ نکاح کے طریقے کے علاوہ جو نکاح کیا اس کا اعتبار نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے نکاح فاسد کا اعتبار نہیں ہے۔
[1812] (87) And if he consummates with her, then she gets mahr al-mithl of her peers, and it is not increased beyond the named (agreed) amount. In a fasid marriage, if he has intercourse with the woman, then she is entitled to mahr al-mithl. But this mahr al-mithl should not exceed the amount that was mutually agreed upon. For example, if they agreed on five hundred dirhams and the mahr al-mithl is six hundred dirhams, then only five hundred dirhams will be given, not six hundred. The fasid marriage is not a valid marriage in essence, but since intercourse has occurred, mahr al-mithl is compelled. And since both parties agreed on a lower amount, the lower amount is given. (2) The proof that a fasid marriage is not a valid marriage is this athar: From Ata: 'Whoever marries not according to the proper way of marriage and then divorces, it is not counted as anything; he only divorced someone not his wife.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Nikah 'ala Ghayr Wajh al-Nikah, vol. 6, p. 203, no. 10510) This athar indicates that a marriage conducted otherwise than the proper way of marriage is not recognized. Therefore, a fasid marriage has no validity.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for a fasid marriage after consummation. The ruling states that if the husband has had intercourse with the wife in a fasid marriage, she is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the proper mahr of her female peers). However, this mahr al-mithl is capped at the amount that was specified (musamma) in the contract; if the specified amount is lower than mahr al-mithl, only the lower amount is paid. The commentary illustrates with an example: if the agreed mahr was 500 dirhams and the mahr al-mithl is 600, only 500 is given. The reason is that although the marriage is defective and not valid as a proper marriage, intercourse necessitates mahr. But since both parties agreed to a lower sum, that agreement is honored. The proof is an athar from Ata stating that a marriage not done in the proper way is invalid, so the fasid marriage has no legal effect except for consequences of intercourse.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The mahr that is determined by the mahr of the woman's female peers (e.g., her paternal cousins, social status).
مسى (musamma): The mahr that was explicitly named or agreed upon in the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a fasid marriage where the agreed mahr is 300 dirhams and the mahr al-mithl is 400 dirhams, what does the wife receive?
A) 400 dirhams
B) 300 dirhams
C) Nothing because the marriage is invalid
D) 500 dirhams

Key Takeaway
In a fasid marriage after consummation, the wife receives mahr al-mithl, but not exceeding the agreed mahr.

Iddah and Lineage in Fasid Nikah
Ruling on obligatory iddah and established lineage in fasid marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two legal effects of a consummated fasid marriage after separation and cite the proof from the action of Ali ibn Abi Talib.

Core Idea
A fasid marriage, though invalid, still triggers iddah and establishes lineage if consummated.

In this lesson, we examine two important consequences of a fasid (defective) marriage after the qadi separates the couple. Even though the marriage is invalid, certain rights and obligations arise from consummation, protecting the woman and the child. The Hanafi school relies on a tradition from Ali ibn Abi Talib to support this position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage states two legal effects of a fasid marriage after separation: 1) the woman must observe iddah, 2) the child's lineage is established to the husband.
These are separate but related consequences.
2
Determine the condition for these rulings
These rulings apply only if the fasid marriage was consummated (either actual intercourse or valid seclusion). The proof from Ali mentions a consummated marriage.
Consummation is the key factor that triggers legal effects.
3
Examine the proof
The author cites an athar from Ali ibn Abi Talib through Ata: Ali separated a couple who married during the woman's iddah (a fasid marriage) and consummated, and he ordered her to complete her iddah.
This shows that even a defective marriage generates the obligation of iddah.
4
Derive the legal principle
From Ali's judgment, Hanafi jurists conclude that any consummated fasid marriage triggers iddah upon separation and establishes nasab for the child born during the marriage.
The principle is that fasid is not void ab initio; it has effects after consummation.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may not require iddah in a fasid marriage because they consider it void with no effects. The Hanafi view distinguishes fasid from batil.
The cross-madhhab dispute is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۸۱۳] (۸۸) وعليها العدة ويثبت نسب ولدها منه ۔ التي نکاح فاسد میں تفریق کے بعد عورت پر عدت بھی لازم ہوگی۔ اور اس درمیان بچہ پیدا ہوا تو اس بچے کا نسب اس شوہر سے ثابت ہوگا۔ اخبرني عطاء ان على بن ابى طالب اتى بامرأة نكحت في عدتها وبنى فيها ففرق بينهما وامرها ان تعتد بما
[1813] (88) And upon her is iddah, and the lineage of her child is established from him (the husband). Commentary: In a fasid marriage after separation, the woman is obligated to observe iddah. And if a child is born during that period, the child's lineage is established from this husband. Ata informed me that Ali ibn Abi Talib brought a woman who married during her iddah and consummated, so he separated them and ordered her to complete the iddah...
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage provides two consequences of a fasid marriage after the qadi separates the couple. First, the woman must observe an iddah (waiting period) as required. Second, if a child is born during the period of the fasid marriage, the child's lineage (nasab) is attributed to the husband. The commentary cites an athar from Ali ibn Abi Talib (through Ata) as proof: Ali separated a couple who married during iddah and ordered the woman to complete her iddah. This establishes that iddah and lineage are recognized despite the marriage being defective. The ruling emphasizes that the fasid marriage, though invalid, still produces some legal effects like iddah and paternity.

Key Terms
عدة (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after separation or death of husband before remarrying, to ensure no pregnancy from previous marriage.
نسب (nasab): Lineage; legal parentage of a child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After a qadi separates a couple in a consummated fasid marriage, what must the woman observe?
A) Nothing, since the marriage was invalid
B) Iddah of three menstrual cycles
C) Iddah only if she is pregnant
D) She must re-marry immediately

Key Takeaway
A consummated fasid marriage, though defective, obligates the woman to observe iddah and establishes the child's lineage to the husband.

Nikah — Marriage

Consequences of Fasid Nikah: Mahr, Iddah, and Lineage
Rulings on mahr, iddah, and nasab in invalid marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on mahr, iddah, and lineage in a fasid nikah after consummation, and identify the evidence from the athar.

Core Idea
In a fasid nikah, mahr al-mithl is wajib only after consummation, iddah is required, and lineage is established.

This passage presents the Hanafi rulings on the legal effects of a fasid (invalid) marriage after consummation. While a fasid nikah is not a valid contract in itself, certain consequences follow if the marriage was consummated, including the obligation of mahr al-mithl, the waiting period (iddah), and the establishment of the child's lineage. The text also provides proofs from the sayings of early authorities (athar) supporting these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage deals with fasid nikah after consummation. The rulings are: mahr al-mithl (not exceeding the specified amount), iddah, and lineage.
2
Locate the condition
The key condition for mahr is actual consummation (dakhul). Without it, no mahr is due.
Seclusion (khalwa) is not equivalent to consummation in fasid nikah.
3
Examine the evidence
The passage cites athar from Ibrahim and Ata, and the principle 'al-walad li al-firash'.
The athar are from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'i school holds that mahr al-mithl is due without the cap; Hanafi caps at the specified amount.
5
Apply the ruling
For iddah and lineage, the woman is considered under the man's bed (firash) due to the nikah, so iddah is wajib and lineage established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا دخل بها فلها مهر مثلها ولا يزاد على المسمى (۸۷) وعليها العدة ويثبت نسب ولدها منه (۸۸) .
نكاح فاسد مجبوری کے درجہ میں نکاح ہے۔ اس لئے باضابطہ محبت سے پہلے نکاح کا انعقاد نہیں ہو گا۔ اس لئے اس سے پہلے مہر بھی لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ اور چونکہ نکاح صحیح نہیں ہے اس لئے خلوت کرنا صحبت کے درجے میں نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے قاضی نے صحبت سے پہلے یا خلوت سے پہلے تفریق کر دی تو مہر لازم نہیں ہو گا (۲) اس اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابراهيم قال کل نکاح فاسد نحو الذي تزوج في عدتها واشباهه ماذا من النكاح الفاسد اذا كان قد دخل بها؟ فلها الصداق ويفرق بينهما (الف) (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ۱۶۱ ما قالوافي المرأة تزوج في عدتها الها الصداق ام لا؟ ج رابع ، ص ۴ نمبر ۱۷۱۹۰) اور مصنف عبد الرزاق میں ہے۔وقال عطاء لها صداقها بما اصاب منها (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب نکا تھافی عد تھاج سادس ص ۲۰۹ نمبر ۱۰۵۳۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ صحبت کرے گا تب عورت کو مہر ملے گا ورنہ نہیں۔
نوت عورت عدت گزار رہی ہو اسی درمیان نکاح کرنا نکاح فاسد کی شکل ہے۔
[۱۸۱۲] (۸۷) اور اگر اس سے محبت کرلے تو عورت کے لئے مہر مثل ہوگا اور متعین مہر پر زیادہ نہیں کیا جائے گا۔
نکاح فاسد میں عورت سے صحبت کرے تو عورت کے لئے مہر مثل ہوگا۔ لیکن یہ مہر مثل آپس میں جتنا مہر طے کیا ہے اس سے زیادہ نہ ہو۔ مثلا آپس میں پانچ سو درہم مہر طے کیا ہے اور مہر مثل چھ سو درہم ہے تو پانچ سو درہم ہی دیئے جائیں گے چھ سو درہم نہیں دیئے جائیں گے۔ نکاح فاسد اصل میں نکاح ہی نہیں ہے لیکن چونکہ صحبت کر چکا ہے اس لئے مجبورا مہر مثل کا فیصلہ کیا جائے گا۔ اور چونکہ دونوں کم پر راضی ہو گئے ہیں اس لئے کم دیا جائے گا (۲) نکاح فاسد نکاح نہیں ہے اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ عن عطاء قال من نكح على غير وجه النكاح ثم طلق فلا يحسب شيئا انما طلق غير امرأته (ج) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب النکاح علی غیر وجہ النکاح ج سادس ص ۲۰۳ نمبر ۱۰۵۱۰) اس اثر میں ہے کہ نکاح کے طریقے کے علاوہ جو نکاح کیا اس کا اعتبار نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے نکاح فاسد کا اعتبار نہیں ہے۔
(۱۸۱۳] (۸۸) اور عورت پر عدت ہے۔ اور عورت کے بچے کا نسب ثابت ہو گا اسی شوہر سے۔ التی نکاح فاسد میں تفریق کے بعد عورت پر عدت بھی لازم ہوگی۔ اور اس درمیان بچہ پیدا ہوا تو اس بچے کا نسب اس شوہر سے ثابت ہوگا۔ اخبرني عطاء ان على بن ابى طالب اتى بامرأة نكحت في عدتها وبنى فيها ففرق بينهما وامرها ان تعتد بما بقى من عدتها الأولى ثم تعتد من هذا عدة مستقبلة (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب نکاحھا فی عد تھاج سادس ص ۲۰۸ نمبر ۱۰۵۳۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ دوسرے کی عدت میں شادی کی تو یہ نکاح فاسد ہوا اس لئے پہلے نکاح کی عدت بھی پوری کرنی ہے اور دوسری شادی جو نکاح فاسد ہے اس کی عدت بھی پوری کرنی ہے۔ جس سے ثابت ہوا کہ نکاح فاسد کی فرقت میں عدت ہے (۲) عدت اس لئے گز روائی جائے گی تاکہ پتہ چل جائے کہ اس کے پیٹ میں کسی قسم کا بچہ نہ رہ جائے۔ اور نسب ثابت اس لئے کیا جائے گا تا کہ بچہ بغیر نسب کے نہ رہ جائے (۲) پہلے گزر چکا ہے الولد للفراش (مسلم شریف نمبر ۷ (۱۴۵) اور چونکہ نکاح فاسد کی وجہ سے عورت ناکح کی فراش ہے اس لئے اس وقت کے بچے کا نسب ناکح سے ثابت ہوگا۔
If he has consummated with her, then she gets her mahr al-mithl, and it is not increased beyond the specified amount (87). Upon her is the iddah, and the lineage of her child is established from him (88). A fasid (invalid) nikah is in the degree of compulsion. Therefore, before intentional consummation, the nikah does not take effect. Hence, before that, mahr is not obligatory. And since the nikah is not valid, khalwa (seclusion) is not equivalent to consummation. So if the judge separates them before consummation or before khalwa, mahr is not obligatory. (2) There is evidence for this in the athar: from Ibrahim who said, 'Every fasid nikah, such as the one who marries in her iddah and the like, if he has consummated with her, then she gets the mahr and they are separated.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) And in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq: 'Ata said: She has her mahr for what he had from her.' This athar indicates that only if consummation occurs does the woman get mahr, otherwise not. Note: marrying a woman while she is in iddah is a form of fasid nikah. [1812] (87) And if he has consummated with her, then for her is mahr al-mithl, and it is not increased beyond the specified amount. In a fasid nikah, if consummation occurs, the woman gets mahr al-mithl. But this mahr al-mithl does not exceed what was mutually agreed. For example, if they agreed on 500 dirhams but her mahr al-mithl is 600, then 500 is given, not 600. A fasid nikah is essentially not a nikah, but since consummation occurred, mahr al-mithl is compelled. And because both were satisfied with a lower amount, the lower is given. (2) The proof that fasid nikah is not a nikah is the athar from Ata: 'Whoever marries in an improper manner and then divorces, it is not counted as anything; he only divorced a non-wife.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) This athar shows that the nikah done outside the proper manner has no recognition. Therefore, a fasid nikah has no recognition. [1813] (88) Upon her is the iddah, and the lineage of her child is established from this husband. That is, after separation in a fasid nikah, the woman must observe iddah. And if a child is born during that time, the child's lineage is established from that husband. It is narrated from Ata that Ali ibn Abi Talib had a woman who married in her iddah and then had her marriage consummated; he separated them and ordered her to observe the remainder of her first iddah and then observe another iddah for this (marriage). (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) This athar shows that if someone marries during another's iddah, it is a fasid nikah; therefore, she must complete the iddah of the first marriage and also observe iddah for the second (fasid) marriage. This proves that in a fasid nikah, separation requires iddah. (2) The iddah is observed to ascertain whether the womb contains a child. And the lineage is established so that the child does not remain without lineage. (2) It has already been mentioned that 'the child belongs to the bed' (Muslim, no. 7/145). Since due to the fasid nikah the woman is considered under the bed of the husband, the child born at that time is attributed to him.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the consequences of a fasid (invalid) nikah. The text explains two key rulings: (1) the entitlement to mahr and (2) the obligation of iddah and establishment of lineage. The author begins by stating that if consummation occurs in a fasid nikah, the woman is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the mahr of her equals) but not exceeding the amount specified by the parties. This is because the nikah is invalid ab initio, so no mahr is due without consummation; however, after consummation, mahr al-mithl is wajib to compensate for sexual relations. The rule 'no increase over the specified amount' reflects the principle that the parties' consent to a lower amount should be honored. Proof is provided from athar of Ibrahim and Ata indicating that only upon consummation does mahr become due. (2) The second ruling states that the woman must observe iddah and that the child's lineage is established from the husband. The iddah is for ensuring the womb is clear, and lineage is established to avoid the child being without a father. The athar from Ali illustrates that a woman who marries during her iddah must complete the first iddah and then observe a second iddah for the fasid marriage, confirming that iddah is required upon separation. The principle 'al-walad li al-firash' (the child belongs to the bed) applies because the woman is considered under the husband's bed (firash) due to the nikah, even if invalid, for the purpose of lineage.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The mahr equivalent to that given to women of similar status in the bride's family, used when no mahr is specified or in fasid nikah after consummation.
نكاح فاسد (nikah fasid): An invalid marriage due to a defect in one of its pillars or conditions; it does not produce legal effects unless consummated, and then only some effects follow.
عدة (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after separation from her husband, to confirm she is not pregnant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a fasid nikah, if the man has not consummated the marriage and the judge separates them, what is the ruling on mahr?
A) She gets mahr al-mithl
B) She gets the specified mahr
C) No mahr is due
D) She gets half of the specified mahr

Key Takeaway
In a fasid nikah, only after consummation do the effects of mahr al-mithl (capped), iddah, and lineage take effect; without consummation, no such effects.

beginner
6 min
Who Determines Mahr al-Mithl?
Definition and delimitation of mahr al-mithl relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which female relatives determine mahr al-mithl according to the Hanafi school and explain why the maternal side is excluded, using the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Mahr al-mithl is based on paternal female relatives only; mother and maternal aunt are excluded unless from the same tribe.

When a marriage contract does not specify a dower (mahr), or in certain invalid marriages after consummation, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the equitable dower). But how is this amount determined? The Hanafi school, relying on a hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, identifies specific female relatives whose mahr serves as the benchmark. In this lesson, we will examine which relatives are considered and why the default excludes the maternal side.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal context
Recall when mahr al-mithl is used: when no mahr is specified in the contract or in a fasid nikah after consummation. The ruling is wajib payment.
2
List the considered relatives
From the passage, the relatives are: the woman's sisters, her paternal aunts, and her female paternal cousins (daughters of paternal uncles).
These are all from the father's lineage.
3
Note the exclusion
The mother and maternal aunt are explicitly excluded unless they belong to the same paternal tribe as the woman.
This is a default rule; exception if the mother or aunt is from the father's family.
4
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'For her is the like of the dower of her women, without reduction or increase.' The key phrase is 'mithla sadaqi nisaiha'.
The hadith is narrated in Tirmidhi and Abu Dawood.
5
Understand the Hanafi interpretation
The term 'nisaiha' (her women) is interpreted by the Hanafi school as referring to paternal female relatives based on customary usage (urf), as they determine the family's standard.
This interpretation leads to the exclusion of mother and maternal aunt by default.

مهر مثل کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اس خاندان کی قریبی عورتوں مثلا بہن، پھوپی، چچازاد بہن کا جو مہر ہے ان مہروں کے مثل ان کا مہر ہو اس کو مہر مثل کہتے ہیں۔ مہر کا اعتبار خاندان کی عورتوں کے ساتھ ہے (۲) حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ لمبی حدیث جس میں عبد اللہ بن مسعود نے عورت کے لئے مہر مثل کا فیصلہ کیا اس کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ عن ابن مسعود انه سئل عن رجل تزوج امرأة ولم يفرض لها صداقا ولم يدخل بها حتى مات فقال ابن مسعود لها مثل صداق نسائها لا وكس ولا شطط (الف) (ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الرجل يتزوج المرأة فيموت عنها قبل ان يفرض لها ص ۲۱۷ نمبر ۱۱۴۵ را بو د ا د د د شریف، باب فیمن تزوج ولم يسم لها صدا قامتی مات ص ۲۹۵ نمبر ۲۱۱۶) اس حدیث میں ہے لها مثل صداق نسائها لا وكس ولا شطط جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ خاندان کی عورت کا جو مہر ہے وہ مہر مثل ہے۔ نہ اس سے کم ہو اور نہ زیادہ ہو۔ اور خاندان کی عورتیں بہن، پھوپیاں اور چازاد بہن ہوتی ہیں۔ اس لئے انہیں عورتوں کے مہر کو مہر مثل کہتے ہیں۔
[۱۸۱۵ (۹۰) مہر مثل کا اعتبار نہیں کیا جائے گا اس کی ماں کے ساتھ اور اس کی خالہ کے ساتھ اگر وہ عورت کے قبیلے سے نہ ہوں۔ ماں کا مہر اور خالہ کا مہر عورت کے لئے مہر مثل نہیں ہوگا۔ ہاں اگر عورت کے خاندان سے ہی ماں اور خالہ ہو تو ان کے مہر کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا۔

Her mahr al-mithl is considered based on her sisters, her paternal aunts, and her female cousins (89). It is not considered based on her mother nor her maternal aunt if they are from other than her tribe (90). The meaning of mahr al-mithl is that the mahr of the close women of her family, such as sister, paternal aunt, and cousin, is taken as the equivalent. Mahr is determined by the women of the family. (2) There is proof of this in the hadith: a long hadith in which Abdullah ibn Mas'ud decided mahr al-mithl for a woman. Its excerpt: from Ibn Mas'ud that he was asked about a man who married a woman without fixing a dower and died before consummation; he said: 'For her is the like of the dower of her women without reduction or increase.' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawood). This hadith says: 'For her is the like of the dower of her women, without reduction or increase.' The meaning is that the mahr of the women of the family is mahr al-mithl. [1815] (90) Mahr al-mithl will not be considered based on her mother nor her maternal aunt if they are not from her tribe. The mahr of the mother and maternal aunt will not be mahr al-mithl for the woman. Yes, if the mother and maternal aunt are from her family, then their mahr will be considered. The above hadith 'mithla sadaqi nisaiha' (like the dower of her women) makes it clear that it is the women of her family. And mother and maternal aunt are generally not from the family, so their mahr is not considered. However, if they are from her own family, then their mahr is considered. For example, the father married a cousin? Footnote: (from previous page) then she completes the next iddah. (A) When Abdullah ibn Mas'ud was asked about a man who married a woman without fixing a dower and died without consummation, he said: 'For her is the like of the dower of the women of her family, neither less nor more.'

Commentary
This passage defines mahr al-mithl (the equitable dower) and specifies which female relatives are considered in its calculation. The text states that mahr al-mithl is assessed based on the woman's sisters, paternal aunts (father's sisters), and female paternal cousins (father's brother's daughters). It is not assessed based on the mother or maternal aunt unless they belong to the same tribe as the woman. The key point is that mahr al-mithl uses the mahr of paternal-side relatives, reflecting the Hanafi view that the family's standard dower is determined by the father's lineage. The maternal side is excluded because mother and maternal aunt are typically from a different tribe. The proof is from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud who ruled in a case of a man who died before fixing a dower and before consummation; he said: 'For her is the like of the dower of her women (sisters, aunts, cousins), without reduction or increase.' This establishes that mahr al-mithl is based on the women of her own family (paternal side). The commentary emphasizes that if the mother or maternal aunt happens to be from the same tribe (i.e., she married within the tribe), then their mahr could be considered, but the default is to consider only paternal relatives.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower equivalent to that of the woman's paternal female relatives (sisters, paternal aunts, paternal cousins), used when no mahr is specified or in certain invalid marriages.
عمة (ammah): Paternal aunt (father's sister); a key relative for determining mahr al-mithl.
خالة (khalah): Maternal aunt (mother's sister); generally not considered in mahr al-mithl unless from the same tribe.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The woman's mother
B) The woman's maternal aunt
C) The woman's paternal aunt
D) Both mother and maternal aunt

Key Takeaway
Mahr al-mithl is determined solely by the mahr of the wife's paternal female relatives (sisters, paternal aunts, and female paternal cousins), not by mother or maternal aunt unless they belong to the same paternal tribe.

Iddah After a Fasid Marriage
Ruling that a woman who marries during iddah must complete both iddahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a woman who marries during iddah must complete both iddahs, and identify the proof (dalil) for this ruling.

Core Idea
A fasid marriage during iddah requires both iddahs to be completed.

In the Hanafi school, a fasid (defective) marriage still carries legal effects, including the obligation of iddah upon separation. This lesson examines a specific case: a woman who marries while already in iddah from a previous marriage. The text establishes that the second marriage is fasid and does not cancel the first iddah; she must observe both waiting periods. The proof is drawn from the principle ‘al-walad li al-firash’ and a tradition from the Musannaf of Abd al-Razzaq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a woman marrying during her existing iddah. The ruling is that the second marriage is fasid and she must complete both the first iddah and a separate iddah for the fasid marriage.
The text explicitly states: 'she must complete the iddah of the first marriage and also complete the iddah of the second marriage'.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two proofs: (1) a tradition from the Musannaf of Abd al-Razzaq on marriage during iddah, and (2) the hadith 'al-walad li al-firash' (Sahih Muslim).
The tradition establishes the ruling, while the hadith provides the underlying principle.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith 'al-walad li al-firash' means that the child belongs to the husband of the marriage bed. Since a fasid marriage creates a firash, any child born during the fasid marriage is attributed to the husband. To avoid confusion of lineage and to ensure no pregnancy from the previous husband remains, iddah is wajib after the fasid marriage.
The Hanafis apply the principle even to fasid marriages, while other schools may require a valid marriage.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no intra-Hanafi disagreement: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad all agree that iddah is required for a fasid marriage. However, it is mukhtalaf fih across madhabs; some schools may not mandate iddah for a fasid marriage.
Cross-madhhab status is legitimate ikhtilaf, and the Hanafi position is the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم تعتد من هذا عدة مستقبلة (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب نکاحھا فی عد تھاج سادس ص ۲۰۸ نمبر ۱۰۵۳۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ دوسرے کی عدت میں شادی کی تو یہ نکاح فاسد ہوا اس لئے پہلے نکاح کی عدت بھی پوری کرنی ہے اور دوسری شادی جو نکاح فاسد ہے اس کی عدت بھی پوری کرنی ہے۔ جس سے ثابت ہوا کہ نکاح فاسد کی فرقت میں عدت ہے (۲) عدت اس لئے گز روائی جائے گی تاکہ پتہ چل جائے کہ اس کے پیٹ میں کسی قسم کا بچہ نہ رہ جائے۔ اور نسب ثابت اس لئے کیا جائے گا تا کہ بچہ بغیر نسب کے نہ رہ جائے (۲) پہلے گزر چکا ہے الولد للفراش (مسلم شریف نمبر ۷ (۱۴۵) اور چونکہ نکاح فاسد کی وجہ سے عورت ناکح کی فراش ہے اس لئے اس وقت کے بچے کا نسب ناکح سے ثابت ہوگا۔
Then she must complete a separate iddah after this. (A) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on marriage during iddah, sixth volume, p. 208, no. 10532) In this tradition, it is mentioned that if a woman marries during her iddah, then this marriage is fasid. Therefore, she must complete the iddah of the first marriage and also complete the iddah of the second marriage which is fasid. This proves that separation from a fasid marriage requires an iddah. (2) The iddah is prescribed so that it becomes clear that there is no child in her womb. And lineage is established so that a child is not left without lineage. (2) It has already passed that 'the child belongs to the marriage bed' (Sahih Muslim no. 7 (145)). And because due to the fasid marriage, the woman is the bed of the husband, therefore the lineage of the child at that time is established from the husband.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding the iddah (waiting period) of a woman who enters into a fasid (defective) marriage during her iddah. The text establishes that the fasid marriage does not invalidate the original iddah; rather, she must complete the original iddah and then observe a separate iddah for the fasid marriage. The proof is drawn from a tradition in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq and the well-known hadith 'al-walad li al-firash' (the child belongs to the marriage bed). The purpose of iddah is to ensure no pregnancy from the first husband remains, and to establish lineage if a child is born. Since the fasid marriage places the woman under the husband's bed (firash), any child born during that time is attributed to him. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school, which holds that a fasid marriage, though invalid, still requires an iddah upon separation.

Key Terms
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after separation from a marriage or its termination, to determine pregnancy and establish lineage.
نكاح فاسد (nikah fasid): A defective marriage that is invalid due to a defect in its conditions or pillars, but still requires iddah upon separation.
فراش (firash): The marriage bed; the legal presumption that a child born during a marriage belongs to the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a woman do if she enters into a fasid marriage during her iddah from a previous marriage?
A) She must only complete the iddah of the first marriage.
B) She must complete the iddah of the first marriage and then observe a separate iddah for the fasid marriage.
C) The fasid marriage is considered valid, so she begins a new iddah immediately.
D) She does not need to observe any iddah at all.

Key Takeaway
A fasid marriage during iddah does not cancel the original iddah; both waiting periods must be completed.

Determining Mahr al-Mithl by Paternal Female Relatives
Ruling with proof on determining mahr al-mithl by specific female relatives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of mahr al-mithl and identify which female relatives are used to determine it.

Core Idea
Mahr al-mithl is determined by the dower of the woman's paternal female relatives — sisters, paternal aunts, and cousins.

When a marriage contract is concluded without specifying a dower, or in certain situations like the husband's death before consummation, a woman is entitled to mahr al-mithl — the dower equivalent to that of her female relatives. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on which relatives are considered, and the prophetic proof from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
Determine when mahr al-mithl is applied: when no dower is fixed, in an invalid (fasid) marriage, or when the husband dies before consummation without fixing a dower.
This lesson focuses on the definition, not the full list of scenarios.
2
State the Hanafi definition
Mahr al-mithl is the dower equivalent to that of the woman's close female relatives on her father's side: her sisters (real or half), paternal aunts (father's sisters), and female cousins (father's brother's daughters).
The Arabic term 'نساءها' is interpreted restrictively to paternal relatives.
3
Examine the dalil
The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'لها مثل صداق نسائها لا وكس ولا شطط' (For her is the like of the dower of her women, no reduction and no increase). This is the primary proof.
The hadith is narrated in Tirmidhi and Abu Dawood, classified as ahad (single-transmitter).
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'نسائها' (her women) is understood by Hanafis, based on custom (urf), to refer to the woman's paternal female relatives. The instruction 'لا وكس ولا شطط' ensures the mahr is exactly the typical amount.
Other schools may include maternal relatives, but Hanafis restrict to paternal.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may include maternal relatives in determining mahr al-mithl. The Hanafi position is based on the predominant custom (urf) of the community.
The practical difference can affect the calculated amount.

Source Text

ومهر مثلها يعتبر باخواتها وعماتها وبنات عمها ۱۸۱۴ (۸۹) اس کے مہر مثل کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا اس کی بہنوں، پھوپیوں اور چازاد بہنوں سے۔ ہر مثل کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اس خاندان کی قریبی عورتوں مثلا بہن، پھوپی، چچازاد بہن کا جو مہر ہے ان مہروں کے مثل ان کا مہر ہو اس کو مہر مثل کہتے ہیں۔ مہر کا اعتبار خاندان کی عورتوں کے ساتھ ہے (۲) حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ لمبی حدیث جس میں عبد اللہ بن مسعود نے عورت کے لئے مہر مثل کا فیصلہ کیا اس کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ عن ابن مسعود انه سئل عن رجل تزوج امرأة ولم يفرض لها صداقا ولم يدخل بها حتى مات فقال ابن مسعود لها مثل صداق نسائها لا وكس ولا شطط (الف) (ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الرجل يتزوج المرأة فيموت عنها قبل ان يفرض لها ص ۲۱۷ نمبر ۱۱۴۵ را بو د ا د د د شریف، باب فیمن تزوج ولم يسم لها صدا قامتی مات ص ۲۹۵ نمبر ۲۱۱۶) اس حدیث میں ہے لها مثل صداق نسائها لا وكس ولا شطط جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ خاندان کی عورت کا جو مہر ہے وہ مہر مثل ہے۔ نہ اس سے کم ہو اور نہ زیادہ ہو۔ اور خاندان کی عورتیں بہن، پھوپیاں اور چازاد بہن ہوتی ہیں۔ اس لئے انہیں عورتوں کے مہر کو مہر مثل کہتے ہیں۔
And her mahr al-mithl is considered with reference to her sisters, paternal aunts, and female cousins. 1814(89) Her mahr al-mithl will be determined by her sisters, paternal aunts, and cousins. The meaning of mithl is that the mahr of the close women of the family, such as sister, paternal aunt, and cousin, will be the mahr of this woman; this is called mahr al-mithl. The mahr is determined by the women of the family. (2) There is proof from hadith. A long hadith in which Abdullah ibn Mas'ud decided mahr al-mithl for a woman, its portion is: from Ibn Mas'ud that he was asked about a man who married a woman and did not fix a dower for her and did not consummate the marriage until he died. Ibn Mas'ud said: 'For her is the like of the dower of her women, no reduction and no increase.' (A) (Tirmidhi, chapter on the man who marries a woman and dies before fixing dower, p. 217, no. 1145; Abu Dawood, chapter on the one who marries and does not name dower and dies, p. 295, no. 2116) In this hadith it says 'for her is the like of the dower of her women, no reduction and no increase.' Its meaning is that the mahr of the women of the family is the mahr al-mithl. It should not be less or more. And the women of the family are sisters, paternal aunts, and cousins. Therefore, the mahr of these women is called mahr al-mithl.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling and proof for determining mahr al-mithl (dower of the like) in the Hanafi school. The matn states that the mahr al-mithl of a woman is calculated by looking at the dowers of her close female relatives on the father's side: her sisters (real or half), paternal aunts (father's sisters), and female cousins (father's brother's daughters). The commentary expands by explaining that 'mithl' means the dower equivalent to that of the family's women, as derived from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud. The hadith explicitly says 'for her is the like of the dower of her women', indicating that the mahr should be neither decreased nor increased. This hadith is from Tirmidhi and Abu Dawood. The Hanafi interpretation is that 'her women' refers specifically to the father's side of the family, not the mother's side, as clarified in the next lesson.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower equivalent to that of the women of the same family (father's side), used when no dower is fixed or in certain situations.
لا وكس ولا شطط (la waks wa la shatat): No reduction and no increase; meaning the mahr al-mithl should be exactly the typical amount, not varied.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT considered in determining mahr al-mithl?
A) The woman's sisters.
B) Her paternal aunts.
C) Her maternal aunts.
D) Her father's brother's daughters.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, mahr al-mithl is determined by the dowers of the woman's sisters, paternal aunts, and female cousins on her father's side.

Excluding Mother and Maternal Aunt from Mahr al-Mithl
Ruling that mother and maternal aunt are not considered for mahr al-mithl unless from the same paternal tribe.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for excluding the mother and maternal aunt from the reference group for mahr al-mithl, and identify the exception when they belong to the same paternal tribe.

Core Idea
Mahr al-mithl is based on paternal relatives; mother and maternal aunt are excluded unless they share the woman's paternal tribe.

This lesson examines a specific exclusion in determining mahr al-mithl: why the mother and maternal aunt are not automatically used as references. The Hanafi school, relying on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud ('mithl sadaq nisa'iha'), limits the reference group to the woman's paternal family. We will explore the reasoning, the exception, and the practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the general rule: the mahr of the mother and maternal aunt is not considered when determining the mahr al-mithl of a woman.
2
Recognize the exception
Note the exception: if the mother or maternal aunt is from the same paternal tribe as the woman, their mahr is considered.
The exception occurs when the father married within the family (e.g., a cousin).
3
Locate the proof
Identify the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'For her is the like of the dower of her women (mithl sadaq nisa'iha).' This is the primary dalil.
The hadith is quoted in the passage.
4
Analyze the linguistic reasoning
Understand that 'nisa'iha' ('her women') refers to the women of her paternal family, not all female relatives. Hence, maternal relatives are excluded by default.
Paternal lineage is the basis for mahr al-mithl in the Hanafi school.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a woman whose mother is from a different tribe, confirm that the mother's mahr is not a valid reference. Then consider the exception.
Example: a Qurayshi woman married to a man; her mother from Banu Hashim (same tribe) would be a valid reference if the mother was also a paternal relative.

And it is not considered with her mother and her maternal aunt when they are not from her tribe. 1815(90) Her mahr al-mithl will not be considered with her mother and with her maternal aunt if they are not from the woman's tribe. The mahr of the mother and the mahr of the maternal aunt will not be the mahr al-mithl for the woman. Yes, if the mother and maternal aunt are from the woman's own family, then their mahr will be considered. From the above hadith 'mithl sadaq nisa'iha' it is understood that it is the woman of the family whose mahr is considered. And the mother and maternal aunt are generally not from the family, so their mahr will not be considered. However, if they are women from her own family, then their mahr will be considered. For example, if the father married a cousin... Footnote: (continuation from previous page) She should also complete the next iddah. (A) Abdullah ibn Mas'ud was asked about a man who married a woman, did not fix a dower for her, did not consummate, and then died. Ibn Mas'ud said: 'For her is the like of the dower of her women, no reduction and no increase.'
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on mahr al-mithl by addressing a specific exclusion: the mother and maternal aunt are not automatically considered when determining the mahr al-mithl of a woman, unless they happen to be from the same tribe (i.e., the father's family). The reasoning is that the hadith uses 'nisa'iha' meaning 'her women'—typically referring to the paternal family. The mother comes from a different family (her own paternal line), and the maternal aunt also belongs to the mother's family, not the father's. Therefore, their mahr values are not the standard. However, if the mother or maternal aunt is actually from the same paternal tribe (e.g., the father married a cousin from his own family), then their mahr can be used. The footnote seems to be a carryover from the previous iddah discussion, which is a separate issue. The core ruling is clear: mahr al-mithl is based on the paternal relatives, not maternal, unless those maternal relatives happen to also be paternal relatives.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The standard dower for a woman in her family or locality, used when no dower is specified in the marriage contract.
قبیلہ (qabilah): Tribe or paternal family. The woman is considered to belong to her father's tribe.

The mother and maternal aunt are excluded from mahr al-mithl reference unless they belong to the woman's paternal tribe.

The Seven Conditions for Equality in Mahr al-Mithl
Seven conditions for equality in mahr al-mithl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven conditions for equality in mahr al-mithl and explain how each condition affects the dower amount.

Core Idea
Mahr al-mithl requires equality in seven attributes: age, beauty, wealth, intelligence, religion, city, and time.

When a dower is not specified in the marriage contract, the Hanafi school determines it by comparing the woman to other women with similar characteristics. This lesson clarifies the seven conditions that must be considered to ensure a fair mahr al-mithl, as derived from the foundational matn and commentary.

Guided Path
1
Recite the seven conditions
Memorize the list: age (سن), beauty (جمال), wealth (مال), intelligence (عقل), religion (دین), city (بلد), and time (عصر). These are the criteria for a fair comparison.
The order in the matn is: age, beauty, wealth, intelligence, religion, city, time.
2
Understand why each condition matters
Each attribute directly influences the dower amount. For example, a younger, more beautiful woman typically commands a higher mahr. Differences in city or time also affect local customs and economic conditions.
The commentary stresses that even slight differences can change the mahr value.
3
Apply to a hypothetical scenario
Consider two women: one is 20 years old, very beautiful, wealthy, intelligent, religious, from the same city, and married in the same year. The other is 40 years old, less wealthy, etc. Would they be considered equal for mahr al-mithl? No, because they differ in age and wealth.
This exercise helps internalize the need for all seven conditions.
4
Cite the supporting hadith
The hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (Tirmidhi) states: 'For her is the like of the dower of her women.' This hadith provides the basis for comparing women with similar traits.
The phrase 'her women' implies women sharing the same attributes as listed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعتبر فى مهر المثل ان يتساوى المرأتان في السن والجمال والمال والعقل والدين والبلد والعصر ۱۸۱٦ (۹۱) اعتبار کیا جائے گا مہر مثل میں یہ کہ برابر ہوں دونوں عورتیں عمر میں، خوبصورتی میں اور مال میں اور عقل میں اور دین میں اور شہر میں اور زمانہ میں۔ اس عورت کا دوسری عورت کے ساتھ مہر کے مثل ہونے کا اعتبار اس وقت کیا جائے گا جبکہ دونوں عورتیں اوپر کی سات چیزوں میں یکساں ہوں۔ ان چیزوں کے تفاوت سے مہر میں تفاوت ہوتا ہے۔ مثلا ایک عورت کی شادی تمہیں سال میں ہوئی تھی جس کا مہر پانچ سو درہم رکھا تھا۔ اور اس عورت کی عمر بیس سال ہے تو ظاہر ہے کہ اس کا مہر زیادہ ہوگا۔ اس لئے دونوں عورتوں کی عمر ، خوبصورتی ، مال، عقل، دین تقریبا یکساں ہوں۔ اسی طرح ایک عورت برطانیہ کی ہو تو اس کا مہر کچھ اور ہوگا اور دوسری عورت پاکستان کی ہے تو اس کا مہر کچھ اور ہوگا۔ اس لئے دونوں عورتیں ایک شہر کی ہوں۔ اور دونوں کا زمانہ بھی تقریبا ایک ہوں۔ عبداللہ ابن مسعود کی حدیث میں ہے- لها مثل صداق نسائها (ترندی شریف نمبر ۱۱۴۵) جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ دونوں عورتیں ایک طرح کی ہوں۔
And it is considered in mahr al-mithl that the two women are equal in age, beauty, wealth, intelligence, religion, city, and time. 1816(91) It will be considered in mahr al-mithl that both women are equal in age, beauty, wealth, intelligence, religion, city, and time. This woman's mahr being like that of another woman will be considered when the two women are equal in the above seven things. Differences in these things cause differences in mahr. For example, one woman was married in the same year with a dower of five hundred dirhams, and this woman is twenty years old; then obviously her mahr will be more. Therefore, the two women should be approximately equal in age, beauty, wealth, intelligence, and religion. Similarly, if one woman is from Britain, her mahr will be different; another woman is from Pakistan, so her mahr is different. Therefore, both women should be from the same city. And their time should also be approximately the same. In the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud it is: 'for her is the like of the dower of her women' (Tirmidhi no. 1145). Its meaning is that the two women are similar.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage lists seven conditions that must be considered when comparing two women for the purpose of determining mahr al-mithl. The matn states that equality is required in: age (سن), beauty (جمال), wealth (مال), intelligence (عقل), religion (دین), city (بلد), and time (عصر). The commentary explains that even slight differences can affect the dower amount. For instance, a younger woman may command a higher mahr than an older one, or a woman from a wealthy city may have a higher mahr than one from a poor region. The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud is again cited to support that the dower should be equal. These conditions ensure that the mahr al-mithl is truly representative of what the woman would have received if her dower had been fixed at the time of marriage. The Hanafi school emphasizes these details to ensure justice and avoid arbitrariness.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): Dower of the like, determined by comparison with women who are equal in age, beauty, wealth, intelligence, religion, city, and time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Religion

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires seven specific attributes for equality in mahr al-mithl: age, beauty, wealth, intelligence, religion, city, and time, ensuring justice in dower determination.

Permissibility of Marrying a Kitabiyyah Slave Woman: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Ruling that marrying a slave woman is permissible whether Muslim or Kitabiyyah, with Shafi'i opposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying a Kitabiyyah slave woman, explain the Shafi'i objection, and evaluate the Hanafi response using Quran 4:25 and qiyas.

Core Idea
The Quranic phrase 'believing slave girls' is interpreted broadly by Hanafis to include Kitabiyyah, by analogy with free Kitabiyyah women.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute regarding marriage to a Kitabiyyah (Jewish or Christian) slave woman. While the Hanafi school permits such a marriage under specific conditions, Imam al-Shafi'i prohibits it. We will trace the textual proof and reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the hukm and condition: a free man who cannot afford a free woman may marry a slave woman, whether Muslim or Kitabiyyah.
The condition of not affording a free woman is crucial.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that only Muslim slave women may be married; Kitabiyyah slave women are not permissible.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i rely on Quran 4:25's restriction to 'your believing slave girls' (fatayatikum al-mu'minat), arguing that 'mu'minat' means Muslim.
The Arabic word 'mu'minat' is the focus.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis interpret 'mu'minat' broadly to include Kitabiyyah, as they believe in God and the messengers. They also use qiyas to free Kitabiyyah women, who are unanimously permissible.
Qiyas is a key legal tool here.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a Hanafi may contract a valid marriage with a Kitabiyyah slave woman, while a Shafi'i must avoid it.
This affects actual marital contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز تزويج الامة مسلمة كانت او كتابية ۱۸۱۷ (۹۲) اور جائز ہے باندی سے نکاح کرنا مسلمان ہو یا کتابیں۔ آزاد عورت بیوی نہ ہو تو باندی سے نکاح کر سکتا ہے۔ چاہے باندی مسلمان ہو یا یہودیہ یا نصرانیہ ہو۔ آیت میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ ومن لم يستطع منكم طولا ان ينكح المحصنات المؤمنات فمن ما ملكت ايمانكم من فتياتكم المؤمنات (الف) ( آیت ۲۵ سورۃ النساء ۴ ) اس آیت میں ہے کہ جو آزاد عورت کی طاقت نہ رکھتا ہو وہ مومنہ باندی سے شادی کر سکتا ہے۔ اور باندی میں دونوں شامل ہیں اس لئے مسلمہ اور کتابیہ دونوں سے شادی کر سکتا ہے۔ جس طرح آزاد کتابیہ سے شادی کر سکتا ہے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ کتابیہ باندی سے شادی بالکل نہیں کرسکتا۔ آیت میں فتياتكم المؤمنات کی قید ہے کہ مومنہ باندی ہو۔ اس لئے کتابیہ سے شادی کرنا جائز نہیں ہے (۲) عبید الله بن عبد الله وسليمان بن يسار قال وكانوا يقولون لا يصلح للمسلم نكاح الامة اليهودية ولا النصرانية انما احل الله حاشیہ : (الف) تم میں سے جو طاقت نہ رکھتا ہو کہ مومنہ آزاد عورتوں سے شادی کرے تو تمہارے جوانوں میں سے مومنہ باندی بہتر ہے (ب) عبید اللہ بن عبد اللہ اور سلیمان بن یسار فرمایا کرتے تھے کہ مسلمان کے لئے یہود یہ اور نصرانیہ باندی سے شادی کرنا مناسب نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اللہ نے اہل کتاب کی آزاد عورتوں کو حلال کیا اور باندی آزاد نہیں ہے۔
And it is permissible to marry a slave woman whether she is Muslim or Kitabiyyah. 1817(92) It is permissible to marry a slave woman, whether she is Muslim or Kitabiyyah. A free man may marry a slave woman if he does not have a free wife, whether the slave woman is Muslim, Jewish, or Christian. There is proof from the verse: 'And whoever among you does not have the means to marry free believing women, then [let him marry] from among those whom your right hands possess of your believing slave girls.' (A) (Surah al-Nisa' 4:25) In this verse, it is that he who cannot afford a free woman may marry a believing slave girl. And 'slave girl' includes both, so he can marry both Muslim and Kitabiyyah, just as he can marry a free Kitabiyyah woman. Imam Shafi'i says that he cannot marry a Kitabiyyah slave woman at all. The verse restricts 'your believing slave girls', so it must be a believing slave girl; therefore, marrying a Kitabiyyah is not permissible. (2) Ubaidullah ibn Abdullah and Sulayman ibn Yasar used to say that it is not proper for a Muslim to marry a Jewish or Christian slave woman because Allah permitted free women of the People of the Book, and a slave woman is not free.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling and an inter-madhhab dispute. The matn states that it is permissible for a free man to marry a slave woman, whether Muslim or Kitabiyyah (Jewish or Christian), provided he does not have a free wife (or cannot afford one). The proof is from Quran 4:25, which permits marrying 'believing slave girls' (fatayatikum al-mu'minat). The Hanafi position is that the word 'fatayat' (slave girls) applies generally, and since free Kitabiyyah women are permissible to marry (by consensus), slave Kitabiyyah women are also permissible by analogy (qiyas). However, Imam Shafi'i argues that the verse explicitly restricts to 'believing' (mu'minat), so only Muslim slave women are allowed. The Hanafis respond that 'mu'minat' here includes all who believe in the oneness of God and the prophethood, and since Kitabiyyah women believe in some of that, they are included. Additionally, the Hanafis cite the opinion of early authorities like Ubaidullah ibn Abdullah and Sulayman ibn Yasar who disallowed it, but the Hanafi school relies on the general permission and analogy. The footnote (ب) actually supports the opposing view, but the madhhab position is as stated. The practical consequence: in the Hanafi school, a man may marry a slave woman from the People of the Book, while in the Shafi'i school, he cannot.

Key Terms
أمة (amah): A female slave; in this context, a slave woman owned by a master.
كتابية (kitabiyyah): A woman from the People of the Book (Jewish or Christian).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Only if she converts to Islam.
C) If he cannot afford to marry a free woman, and it is permissible by analogy to free Kitabiyyah women.
D) Only if he already has a free Muslim wife.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits marrying a Kitabiyyah slave woman when one cannot afford a free woman, based on a broad interpretation of 'mu'minat' and qiyas, while the Shafi'i school restricts it to Muslim slave women.

Seven Criteria for Mahr al-Mithl
Ruling with proof – defines criteria for mahr al-mithl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven criteria for mahr al-mithl, explain why each is relevant, and apply them to compare two hypothetical women.

Core Idea
Mahr al-mithl equals the dower of a woman's peers in seven attributes: age, beauty, wealth, intellect, religion, city, and time.

When a marriage contract lacks a specified mahr or is invalid, Islamic law ensures the woman receives a fair dower. The Hanafi school determines this through a detailed comparison to her female peers. This lesson unpacks the seven criteria that must be considered to achieve equity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling context
Understand when mahr al-mithl is used: when mahr was not fixed in the contract, the marriage was invalid (fasid), or the contract was silent.
Mahr al-mithl is wajib in these cases.
2
Memorize the seven criteria
The seven criteria are: age, beauty, wealth, intellect, religion, city, and time period. They ensure a fair comparison.
The Arabic terms: السن, الجمال, المال, العقل, الدين, البلد, العصر.
3
Understand the hadith proof
The hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (رضي الله عنه) states 'لها مثل صداق نسائها' – she has the like of the dower of her womenfolk. This indicates equality is required.
The word 'مثل' (mithl) is key.
4
Apply the criteria to a case
Given a specific woman, find a female relative or peer from the same community, assess the seven attributes, and set the mahr accordingly.
If no direct peer exists, look to the closest match.
5
Handle cross-madhhab differences
Some schools may use fewer criteria, but the Hanafi school considers all seven to achieve precision.
The ikhtilaf is legitimate; the Hanafi view is mufta bihi in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعتبر فى مهر المثل ان يتساوى المرأتان في السن والجمال والمال والعقل والدين والبلد والعصر (۱۸۱۷ (۹۲) و يجوز تزويج الامة مسلمة كانت او كتابية.
بہن سے شادی کی تھی جس کی وجہ سے وہ اپنے خاندان کی ہی عورت تھی۔ [۱۸۱) (۹۱) اعتبار کیا جائے گا مہر مثل میں یہ کہ برابر ہوں دونوں عورتیں عمر میں، خوبصورتی میں اور مال میں اور عقل میں اور دین میں اور شہر میں اور زمانہ میں۔
اس عورت کا دوسری عورت کے ساتھ مہر کے مثل ہونے کا اعتبار اس وقت کیا جائے گا جبکہ دونوں عورتیں اوپر کی سات چیزوں میں یکساں ہوں۔
ان چیزوں کے تفاوت سے مہر میں تفاوت ہوتا ہے۔ مثلا ایک عورت کی شادی تمہیں سال میں ہوئی تھی جس کا مہر پانچ سو درہم رکھا تھا۔ اور اس عورت کی عمر بیس سال ہے تو ظاہر ہے کہ اس کا مہر زیادہ ہوگا۔ اس لئے دونوں عورتوں کی عمر ، خوبصورتی ، مال، عقل، دین تقریبا یکساں ہوں۔ اسی طرح ایک عورت برطانیہ کی ہو تو اس کا مہر کچھ اور ہوگا اور دوسری عورت پاکستان کی ہے تو اس کا مہر کچھ اور ہوگا۔ اس لئے دونوں عورتیں ایک شہر کی ہوں۔ اور دونوں کا زمانہ بھی تقریبا ایک ہوں۔ عبداللہ ابن مسعود کی حدیث میں ہے- لها مثل صداق نسائها (ترندی شریف نمبر ۱۱۴۵) جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ دونوں عورتیں ایک طرح کی ہوں۔
And consideration in mahr al-mithl is that the two women be equal in age, beauty, wealth, intellect, religion, city, and time. The commentary explains: The mahr al-mithl of a woman is considered when she is similar to another woman in these seven aspects. Difference in these causes difference in mahr. For example, if a woman married in the same year with a mahr of five hundred dirhams, and this woman is twenty years old, obviously her mahr will be higher. Therefore, the two women should be approximately equal in age, beauty, wealth, intellect, and religion. Similarly, if one woman is from Britain, her mahr will be different, and another from Pakistan, so they should be from the same city, and also approximately the same time. The hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: 'She has the mithl of the dower of her womenfolk' (Tirmidhi #1145), meaning the two women are similar.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn followed by an explanatory commentary. The ruling establishes that in determining mahr al-mithl (the proper dower for a woman when no mahr was specified or the marriage was invalid), seven criteria are considered: age, beauty, wealth, intellect, religion, city, and time period. The commentary elaborates that these factors cause variation in mahr, so the woman whose mahr is being assessed must be comparable to a similar woman in her family or community. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) indicating that the mahr is like that of her peers. The Hanafi school uses this to ensure fairness.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower determined by comparing a woman to her female peers in seven attributes.
السن (al-sinn): Age – one of the seven criteria for mahr al-mithl.
الجمال (al-jamal): Beauty – one of the seven criteria.
المال (al-mal): Wealth – one of the seven criteria.
العقل (al-aql): Intellect – one of the seven criteria.
الدين (al-din): Religion/piety – one of the seven criteria.
البلد (al-balad): City/location – one of the seven criteria.
العصر (al-asar): Time period/era – one of the seven criteria.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Five
B) Six
C) Seven
D) Eight

Key Takeaway
Mahr al-mithl is wajib and determined by comparing the woman to a peer in seven specific attributes, ensuring fairness and equity.

Marrying a Kitabi Slave Woman: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Hanafi ruling on marrying a Kitabi slave woman with Shafi'i opposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on marrying a Kitabi slave woman, explain the Shafi'i objection, and evaluate the Hanafi response using Quranic evidence and qiyas.

Core Idea
Hanafi permits marrying Kitabi slave women by qiyas to free Kitabi women; Shafi'i prohibits citing the verse's restriction to 'believing' slave girls.

This lesson examines a classic inter-madhhab dispute: may a Muslim man marry a Jewish or Christian slave woman? The Hanafi school says yes, equating her to a free Kitabi woman, while Imam al-Shafi'i says no, because the Quranic verse (4:25) explicitly mentions 'believing slave girls.' We will walk through the proofs of both sides and understand the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from the matn: it is permissible for a free man who lacks a free wife to marry a slave woman, whether Muslim or Kitabi.
The condition 'no free wife' is key.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that marrying a Kitabi slave woman is absolutely prohibited, regardless of the man's circumstances.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i relies on the Quranic phrase 'your believing slave girls' (fatayatikum al-mu'minat) in verse 4:25, arguing that it restricts permission to believing (Muslim) slave women only.
They also cite an athar from 'Ubaydullah ibn 'Abdullah and Sulayman ibn Yasar.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafi scholars interpret the verse as addressing the man who cannot afford free believing women, but the general permissibility of marrying Kitabi women (free) is established elsewhere (e.g., Quran 5:5). By qiyas, the same permissibility extends to Kitabi slave women. The athar cited by Shafi'i is considered weak or set aside by the stronger analogy.
They also cite Abu Maysara: 'The slave women of the People of the Book are in the same position as their free women.'
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi allows a Muslim man to marry a Kitabi slave woman; Shafi'i forbids it. This affects actual marriage contracts in Hanafi jurisdictions.
The mufta bihi in Hanafi is permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۹۲) و يجوز تزويج الامة مسلمة كانت او كتابية. اور جائز ہے باندی سے نکاح کرنا مسلمان ہو یا کتابیں۔ آزاد عورت بیوی نہ ہو تو باندی سے نکاح کر سکتا ہے۔ چاہے باندی مسلمان ہو یا یہودیہ یا نصرانیہ ہو۔ آیت میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ ومن لم يستطع منكم طولا ان ينكح المحصنات المؤمنات فمن ما ملكت ايمانكم من فتياتكم المؤمنات (الف) ( آیت ۲۵ سورۃ النساء ۴ ) اس آیت میں ہے کہ جو آزاد عورت کی طاقت نہ رکھتا ہو وہ مومنہ باندی سے شادی کر سکتا ہے۔ اور باندی میں دونوں شامل ہیں اس لئے مسلمہ اور کتابیہ دونوں سے شادی کر سکتا ہے۔ جس طرح آزاد کتابیہ سے شادی کر سکتا ہے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ کتابیہ باندی سے شادی بالکل نہیں کرسکتا۔ آیت میں فتياتكم المؤمنات کی قید ہے کہ مومنہ باندی ہو۔ اس لئے کتابیہ سے شادی کرنا جائز نہیں ہے (۲) عبيد الله بن عبد الله وسليمان بن يسار قال وكانوا يقولون لا يصلح للمسلم نكاح الامة اليهودية ولا النصرانية انما احل الله المحصنات من الذين أوتوا الكتاب وليست الامة بمحصنة (ب) (سن للبیہقی ، باب لا حل نکاح لتہ کتاب مسلم بحال ج سابع ص ۲۸۷، نمبر ۱۴۰۱۴) اس اثر سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ کتابیہ سے نکاح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ یہ اثر بھی ہے۔ عن ابی ميسرة قال : اماء اهل الكتاب بمنزلة حرائرهم (مصنف ابن ابی هیته ۴۲ فی نکاح اما ء اہل الکتاب ج ثالث ۴۶۴۰ نمبر ۱۶۱۷۵)
(92) And it is permissible to marry a slave woman whether she is Muslim or from the People of the Book. Commentary: A free man may marry a slave woman if he does not have a free wife, whether she is Muslim, Jewish, or Christian. The proof is the verse: 'And whoever among you cannot afford to marry free believing women, then from what your right hands possess of your believing slave girls' (Quran 4:25). This verse includes both, so he can marry a Muslim or a Kitabi slave woman, just as he can marry a free Kitabi woman. Imam al-Shafi'i says that marrying a Kitabi slave woman is absolutely prohibited because the verse specifies 'believing slave girls.' Therefore, marrying a Kitabi woman is not permissible. There is also an athar from 'Ubaydullah ibn 'Abdullah and Sulayman ibn Yasar: 'They used to say it is not proper for a Muslim to marry a Jewish or Christian slave woman; Allah only made permissible the chaste women from the People of the Book, and a slave woman is not chaste.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, #14014). Another athar: 'Abu Maysara said: The slave women of the People of the Book are in the same position as their free women.'
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute. The matn states the Hanafi position that it is permissible to marry a slave woman whether she is Muslim or Kitabi (Jewish or Christian), provided the man does not already have a free wife. The commentator explains the proof from Quran 4:25, which mentions 'believing slave girls' but according to Hanafi interpretation, the verse's applicability extends to Kitabi slave women by analogy to free Kitabi women, who are permissible to marry. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that the verse explicitly restricts to 'believing' slave girls, thus excluding Kitabi slave women. The commentator also mentions athar from early scholars supporting the Shafi'i view, but the Hanafi school holds that the analogy to free Kitabi women is stronger, and that a slave woman can be considered 'muhsana' (chaste) as per another athar. The Hanafi position is that the permission for Kitabi slave women is valid.

Key Terms
أمة كتابية (amat kitabiyyah): A slave woman from the People of the Book (Jewish or Christian).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Whether the woman must be a virgin

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a man without a free wife to marry a Kitabi slave woman by analogy to free Kitabi women, despite the Shafi'i objection based on the literal wording of the Quran.

Maximum Number of Wives for a Free Man
Ruling on maximum wives for a free man

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the maximum number of wives a free man may marry according to the Hanafi school and explain that slave women are included in the count.

Core Idea
A free man may marry up to four wives, combining free and slave women.

This lesson presents a foundational ruling in Islamic family law: the maximum number of wives a free man may have at one time. The text, from a Hanafi matn, states the limit clearly, and the footnotes add important context about the preference for free women over slave women in marriage. Understanding this limit is essential for ensuring valid marriage contracts and avoiding prohibited relationships.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal subject
The ruling applies to a free man (hurr). Note the legal distinction between a free man and a slave in marriage capacity.
Slaves have a different limit.
2
State the maximum number
The text explicitly permits up to four wives. More than four is not allowed.
This is based on Quran 4:3 and consensus.
3
Recognize the inclusion of slave women
The phrase 'of free women and slave women' indicates that a free man may marry a total of four wives, whether they are free or slave.
This means a free man cannot marry four free women and additionally marry a slave woman; the total must not exceed four.
4
Note the consequence of exceeding the limit
If a free man marries a fifth wife while already married to four, the fifth marriage is invalid (batil) and haram.
He must divorce one of the four before marrying another.

Prohibition of Marrying a Slave Woman over a Free Woman
Ruling with proof from hadith and athar forbidding marrying a slave woman while having a free wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying a slave woman while a free wife exists and identify the proofs (mursal hadith and athar) that support the prohibition.

Core Idea
Marrying a slave woman while a free wife exists is absolutely forbidden – the Prophet forbade it unconditionally.

This lesson examines a clear-cut Hanafi ruling: the prohibition of a man marrying a slave woman when he already has a free wife. While the Quran allows marrying a slave woman under financial hardship, that concession does not apply here. We will analyze the two key proofs – a mursal hadith from al-Hasan and an athar from Ali – that establish this prohibition as absolute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What act is being judged? A man already married to a free woman marries a slave woman. The ruling is that this is not permissible (haram).
The text explicitly states 'اور نہیں جائز ہے' (and it is not permissible).
2
Locate the primary proof
The primary proof is a mursal hadith from al-Hasan: 'نهى رسول الله ان تنكح الامة على الحرة' – the Prophet forbade marrying a slave woman over a free woman. This explicit prohibition indicates haram.
In Hanafi usul, the imperative or prohibition form conveys obligation or prohibition.
3
Examine the secondary proof
An athar from Ali ibn Abi Talib states that a slave woman should not be married over a free woman. This companion report reinforces the ruling.
Ali's statement also implies priority: the free wife gets more days if a slave wife is brought over her.
4
Connect to Quranic context
The Quran (4:25) permits marrying a slave woman only when one cannot afford a free woman. Since the man already has a free wife, this condition is not met, so the permission does not apply.
The text says 'أوپر کی آیت میں ہے... اور یہاں تو آزاد عورت سے شادی کر چکا ہے' – the verse addresses inability, which is absent here.
5
Confirm the Hanafi position
Hanafi scholars hold this prohibition as absolute – even if the free wife consents. All Hanafi imams agree; it is mufta bihi.
No exception is mentioned in the sources; the prohibition is unconditional.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۸۱۸ (۹۳) اور نہیں جائز ہے باندی کی شادی آزاد پر۔ پہلے سے آزاد عورت نکاح میں ہو اب اس پر باندی سے شادی کرنا چاہتا ہے تو جائز نہیں ہے۔ اوپر کی آیت میں ہے کہ آزاد عورت کی طاقت نہ رکھتا ہو تب باندی سے شادی کرے۔ اور یہاں تو آزاد عورت سے شادی کر چکا ہے اس لئے باندی سے شادی کیسے جائز ہوگی (۲) حدیث مرسل میں ہے۔ عن الحسن قال نھی رسول الله ان تنكح الامة على الحرة (الف) (سن للبیہقی ، باب لا تنکح لست على حرة وتنكح الحرة على الامت ج، سابع ص ۲۸۴، نمبر ۱۴۰۰۱ ردار قطنی ، کتاب النکاح ج ثالث ص ۱۹۸ نمبر ۳۶۹۵) اس حدیث مرسل سے معلوم ہوا کہ آزاد بیوی کے رہتے میں باندی سے نکاح جائز نہیں ہے (۳) عـن علـى قال اذا تزوجت الحرة على الامة قسم لها يومين وللامة يوماء ان الامة لا ينبغى لها ان تزوج على الحرة (ب) (دار قطنی ، کتاب النکاح ج ثالث ، نمبر ۳۶۹۵) اس اثر سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ آزاد عورت بیوی ہو تو باندی سے شادی نہ کرے۔
1818 (93) And it is not permissible to marry a slave woman on top of a free woman. If there is already a free woman in marriage, and now he wants to marry a slave woman over her, then it is not permissible. In the above verse it says: if he does not have the power (to marry a free woman) then he may marry a slave woman. But here he has already married a free woman, so how can marrying a slave woman be permissible? (2) There is a mursal hadith: from al-Hasan who said: The Messenger of Allah forbade that a slave woman be married on top of a free woman. (a) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter: لا تنكح الأمة على الحرة وتنكح الحرة على الأمة, vol. 7 p. 284, no. 14001; al-Daraqutni, Kitab al-Nikah, vol. 3 p. 198, no. 3695) From this mursal hadith it is understood that it is not permissible to marry a slave woman while a free wife exists. (3) From Ali: he said: If a free woman is married on top of a slave woman, he gives her two days and the slave woman one day; the slave woman should not be married on top of the free woman. (b) (al-Daraqutni, Kitab al-Nikah, vol. 3, no. 3695) From this athar also it is understood that if a free woman is a wife, then do not marry a slave woman.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling that it is forbidden (haram) for a man to marry a slave woman while he already has a free wife. The proof is twofold: first, a mursal hadith from al-Hasan that the Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly forbade this. Second, an athar from Ali ibn Abi Talib which indicates that a slave woman should not be married over a free woman. Hanafi scholars hold this prohibition as absolute, even if the free wife consents, because the hadith is unconditional. The verse from Surah al-Nisa (4:25) permits marrying a slave woman only when one cannot afford a free woman, and that condition is not met when a free wife already exists.

Key Terms
امة (amah): A female slave (slave woman) in the context of marriage.
حرة (hurreh): A free woman, not a slave.
نكاح (nikah): Marriage contract.

Key Takeaway
It is absolutely forbidden (haram) for a man with a free wife to marry a slave woman, based on the Prophet's explicit prohibition and the example of Ali.

Marrying a Free Woman Over a Slave Wife: Permissibility
Ruling with proof allowing marriage to a free woman over a slave woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying a free woman over a slave woman and identify the proofs from the athar of Ali and Jabir.

Core Idea
Marrying a free woman while having a slave wife is permissible based on Companion statements and status reasoning.

In the Hanafi school, marriage (nikah) rulings often involve considerations of status and equity. One specific issue is when a man already has a slave wife and wishes to marry a free woman. This lesson presents the ruling that such a marriage is permissible, supported by explicit statements from Companions and logical reasoning about the higher status of free women.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its source
The passage states directly that it is permissible (ja'iz) to marry a free woman over a slave woman. Note this is the operative ruling.
The ruling is explicit in the text.
2
Examine the first proof: athar of Ali
The passage references an earlier athar from Ali that when a free woman is married over a slave woman, the free woman gets two days of division and the slave woman one day. This allocation implies the marriage is valid and permissible.
The division rule (bari) indicates permissibility.
3
Examine the second proof: athar of Jabir
Jabir ibn Abdullah explicitly said: 'Do not marry a slave woman over a free woman, but marry a free woman over a slave woman.' This is a direct textual evidence for permissibility in one direction and prohibition in the reverse.
The athar is recorded in Sunan al-Bayhaqi and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Consider the rational argument
The passage adds that a slave woman's child becomes a slave of her master, whereas a free woman's child is free. Thus free women are of higher status, justifying marrying them over slave women.
This is a secondary supporting argument (talil).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۸۱۹ (۹۴) اور جائز ہے آزاد سے شادی کرنا باندی پر۔ ور پہلے باندی بیوی ہو اب اس پر آزاد عورت سے شادی کرنا چاہے تو کر سکتا ہے۔ (1) اثر میں او پر حضرت علی کا قول گزرا کہ آزاد کو باندی پر شادی کرے تو اس کے لئے دو دن باری ہے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ باندی پر آزاد کی شادی کر سکتا ہے (۲) دوسرے اثر میں ہے۔ عن جابر بن عبد الله انه قال لا تنكح الامة على الحرة وتنكح الحرة على الامة، ومن وجد صداق حرة فلا ينكحن امة ابدا (ج) (سن للبیہقی ، باب لاتکح لمت على حرة وتنتج الحرة على الامت ج سابع مص ۲۸۵ نمبر ۱۴۰۰۴ر مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب نکاح الامہ علی الحرة ج سابع ص ۲۶۵ نمبر ۱۳۰۸۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ باندی پر آزاد کی شادی کر سکتا ہے (۳) باندی اتنے اعلی درجے کی نہیں ہوتی اس کا بچہ اس کے آقا کا غلام ہو جائے گا اس لئے اس پر آزاد سے شادی کر سکتا ہے جو اعلی درجے کی ہے اور اس کا بچہ بھی آزاد ہوگا۔
1819 (94) And it is permissible to marry a free woman on top of a slave woman. If a slave woman is already a wife, and he now wants to marry a free woman over her, then he may do so. (1) The athar of Ali passed earlier, that if he marries a free woman over a slave woman, then for the free woman there are two days (of division) and for the slave woman one day; from this it is understood that he can marry a free woman over a slave woman. (2) In another athar: from Jabir ibn Abdullah that he said: Do not marry a slave woman over a free woman, but marry a free woman over a slave woman; and whoever finds the dowry of a free woman should never marry a slave woman. (c) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter: لا تنكح الأمة على الحرة وتنكح الحرة على الأمة, vol. 7 p. 285, no. 14004; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter: Nikah al-amah 'ala al-hurrah, vol. 7 p. 265, no. 13089) From this athar it is understood that he can marry a free woman over a slave woman. (3) A slave woman is not of such a high status; her child becomes the slave of her master; therefore, he can marry a free woman over her, who is of higher status and her child will also be free.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling that it is permissible (ja'iz) for a man to marry a free woman even if he already has a slave wife. The proofs are: (1) the athar from Ali which shows that when a free woman is married over a slave woman, she gets a greater share of division (two days vs. one), implying the act is allowed. (2) The explicit statement from Jabir ibn Abdullah that one may marry a free woman over a slave woman, though not the reverse. (3) A rational argument: a slave woman's child becomes a slave of her master, while a free woman's child is free; thus free women are of higher status and marrying one is allowed over a slave woman. This is distinct from the previous ruling where marrying a slave woman over a free woman is forbidden.

Key Terms
امة (amah): Female slave.
حرة (hurreh): Free woman.
باري (bari): Division of nights between wives.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits marrying a free woman over a slave wife, based on Companion statements and the higher status of free women.
