Maximum Wives: Free and Slave in Hanafi and Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on slave wives limit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the maximum number of wives including slave women, cite the Quranic and hadith proofs, and evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument.

Core Idea
A free man may marry up to four women total; the Quranic limit applies equally to free and slave.

Islamic law sets a clear limit on the number of wives a man may have simultaneously. This passage from al-Sharh al-Samari lays out the Hanafi position: a free man may marry up to four women, whether they are free or slave. It then introduces the Shafi'i objection that only one slave woman is allowed. Understanding this dispute helps you see how different schools interpret the same sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
From the text, note the ruling: a free man may marry up to four women in total, including any combination of free and slave women.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The text cites Quran 4:3, which permits marriage up to four without specifying free or slave, and the hadith of Wahb al-Asadi, who was ordered to keep four of his eight wives upon embracing Islam.
The hadith supports the limit of four in a case with multiple slave wives.
3
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that a free man can only marry one slave woman. His evidence: Quran 4:25 conditions slave marriage on inability to afford a free woman (need is met by one), and an athar from Ibn Abbas stating a free man should marry only one slave.
The Shafi'i school holds that slave marriage is a concession and should be minimized.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that Quran 4:3 is general and unrestricted; the condition in 4:25 is only about the initial permissibility of slave marriage, not quantity. The athar of Ibn Abbas is interpreted as a recommendation, not a prohibition.
The Hanafi reading prioritizes the general text over a specific athar that may be weak or context-bound.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi law, a free man can have multiple slave wives (up to four total), while under Shafi'i law, he can have at most one slave wife.
This affects real-world marriage choices and fatwa guidance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۸۲۰ (۹۵) آزاد مرد کے لئے جائز ہے کہ چار آزاد اور باندیوں سے شادی کرے۔ اور اس کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ اس سے زیادہ سے شادی کرے۔ ایک آزاد آدمی چار عورتوں سے بیک وقت شادی کر سکتا ہے اس سے زیادہ سے نہیں۔ چاہے چاروں آزاد عورتیں ہوں یا چاروں باندیاں ہوں یا مشترکہ ہوں۔ آیت میں ہے کہ چار سے زیادہ شادی نہ کرو۔ فانكحوا ما طاب لكم من النساء مثنى وثلث و ربع (الف) (آیت ۳ سورة النساء ۴ ) اس آیت میں چار تک شادی کرنے کی اجازت ہے (۲) ایک صحابی نے اس عورتوں سے شادی کی تھی تو ان کو چار رکھنے کی اجازت ملی باقی کو چھوڑنے کا حکم دیا۔ وقال وهب الاسدى قال اسلمت وعندى ثمان نسوة قال فذكرت ذلك للنبي الله فقال النبي الله اختر منهن اربعا (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی من اسلم وعنده نساء اکثر من اربع او اختان ص ۳۱۱ نمبر ۲۲۴۱ / ترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الرجل يسلم وعنده عشر نسوة ص۲۱۴ نمبر ۱۱۲۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ چار عورتیں جائز ہیں۔ ان سے زیادہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر باندی سے شادی کرنے کی ضرورت پڑ جائے تو صرف ایک باندی سے شادی کر سکتا ہے اس سے زیادہ سے (1) باندی سے شادی کرنا مجبوری کے درجے میں ہے جبکہ آزاد سے شادی کرنے کی استطاعت نہ رکھتا ہو۔ اور یہ ضرورت ایک باندی سے پوری ہو گئی اس لئے ایک باندی سے زیادہ سے شادی نہ کرے (۲) اثر میں ہے عن ابن عباس قال لا يتزوج السحر من الاماء الا واحدة (ج) (سن للبیہقی ، باب لا کر امت علی امت ج سابع ص ۱۲۸۴ نمبر ۱۲۰۰۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ صرف ایک باندی سے شادی کر سکتا ہے۔
1820 (95) For a free man, it is permissible to marry four free women and slave women. And it is not permissible for him to marry more than that. A free man can marry four women at one time, not more. Whether all four are free women, all four are slave women, or a mix. In the verse it says: do not marry more than four. 'Marry what seems good to you of women: two, three, or four.' (a) (Verse 3 of Surah al-Nisa 4) This verse permits marriage up to four. (2) A Companion had married several women; he was allowed to keep four and ordered to leave the rest. Wahb al-Asadi said: I embraced Islam while I had eight wives; I mentioned that to the Prophet, and the Prophet said: Choose four of them. (b) (Abu Dawud, chapter: On him who embraces Islam while having more than four wives or two sisters, p. 311 no. 2241; Tirmidhi, chapter: On a man who embraces Islam while having ten wives, p. 214 no. 1128) From this hadith it is understood that four wives are permissible; more is not permissible. Imam al-Shafi'i says: if there is a need to marry a slave woman, then he can marry only one slave woman, not more. (1) Marrying a slave woman is considered a concession when one does not have the ability to marry a free woman; and this need is fulfilled by one slave woman, so he should not marry more than one. (2) There is an athar from Ibn Abbas: he said: A free man should not marry from among slave women except one. (c) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter: لا يتزوج الحر من الإماء إلا واحدة, vol. 7 p. 284 no. 12000) From this athar it is understood that he can marry only one slave woman.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that a free man may marry up to four women in total, irrespective of whether they are free or slave. The proof is the Quranic verse (4:3) which allows up to four, and the hadith of Wahb al-Asadi. The passage then records the objection of Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues that a free man can marry at most one slave woman, based on the principle that slave marriage is only permitted when one cannot afford a free woman, and that need is satisfied by one. The Shafi'i also cites an athar from Ibn Abbas. The Hanafi response (not explicitly stated but implied) is that the Quranic verse is general and does not differentiate between free and slave women; the condition of inability to afford a free woman is only relevant to the primary permission to marry a slave woman in the absence of a free wife, but once that condition is met, the general limit of four applies. The athar of Ibn Abbas is interpreted as a recommendation or as applying to specific circumstances. In the Hanafi school, the mufta bihi position is that a free man can marry up to four women, including any number of slave women up to four in total.

Key Terms
حرائر (hara'ir): Free women (plural of حرة).
اماء (ima'): Slave women (plural of أمة).
ابن عباس (Ibn Abbas): The Companion Abdullah ibn Abbas, whose athar is cited by the Shafi'i school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only one.
B) Up to four.
C) Up to two.
D) No limit.

Key Takeaway
A free man may marry up to four wives total; slave women are counted within that limit, not beyond.

Slave Cannot Marry More Than Two Women
Ruling with proof from ijma and qiyas on slave marriage limits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the maximum number of wives a male slave can marry and explain the proof from ijma and qiyas.

Core Idea
A slave may marry at most two women, based on the Companions' consensus.

The Hanafi school limits a male slave to a maximum of two wives at any one time. This ruling is derived from the explicit ijma (consensus) of the Companions of the Prophet ﷺ, as reported by Hakam, and is further supported by qiyas (analogy) based on the principle that a slave's legal capacity is half that of a free man. Understanding this ruling clarifies the broader Hanafi method of using ijma and qiyas in deriving fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states that a slave (abd) should not marry more than two women. Determine the hukm level (haram) and confirm it applies to male slaves only.
The ruling is specific to male slaves; female slaves have different marriage rules.
2
Examine the primary proof: Ijma of the Companions
The text cites an athar from Hakam that the Companions agreed a slave cannot collect more than two wives. Identify this as an ijma proof and assess its authority.
Ijma is a primary source; this particular report is zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalala due to explicit wording.
3
Understand the secondary proof: Qiyas on half capacity
The passage explains that a slave's rights and duties are half those of a free man. Since a free man may marry four, a slave may marry two. This is qiyas with the illa (effective cause) being half legal capacity.
This qiyas reinforces the ijma and provides a rational basis.
4
Review the supporting athar from Umar
The passage also quotes Umar ibn al-Khattab: 'a slave marries two women and divorces with two pronouncements.' This further confirms the half-status principle.
The athar from Umar aligns with the ijma and adds practical illustration.
5
Establish the mufta bihi and note cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that a slave cannot marry more than two. Some other schools may allow up to four, but the Hanafi position rests on ijma.
This difference arises from varying acceptance of the Companions' consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۸۲۱ (۹۶) اور غلام نہ شادی کرے دو سے زیادہ۔ آزاد چار عورتوں سے شادی کر سکتا ہے لیکن غلام ان کے آدھے پر اکتفا کرے گا یعنی بیک وقت دو عورتوں سے ہی شادی کر سکتا ہے۔ اثر میں ہے ۔ عمر بن الخطاب قال ينكح العبد امرأتين ويطلق تطلیقین ۔ اور دوسری روایت میں ہے عن الحکم قال اجتمع اصحاب رسول الله على ان المملوك لا يجمع من النساء فوق اثنين (1) (سن لليبقى ، باب نكاح العبد وطلاقہ ج سابع میں ۲۵۵، نمبر ۱۳۸۹۸/۱۳۸۹۵ مصنف ابن ابى هبية فى المملوك كم يتزوج من النساء ج ثالث ص ۲۸۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ غلام دو عورتوں سے بیک وقت شادی کر سکتا ہے (۲) غلام کی نعمت آزاد کے مقابلے میں آدھی ہے اس لئے آزاد کو چار کی اجازت ہے تو غلام کو دو کی اجازت ہوگی۔
1821 (96) And a slave should not marry more than two. A free man can marry four women, but a slave will suffice with half of that, i.e., he can marry only two women at a time. There is an athar: Umar ibn al-Khattab said: a slave marries two women and divorces with two pronouncements. And in another narration from Hakam: he said: The Companions of the Messenger of Allah agreed that a slave does not collect more than two women. (1) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter: Nikah al-'abd wa talaquhu, vol. 7 pp. 255, nos. 13898/13895; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, on how many a slave can marry, vol. 3 p. 284) From this athar it is understood that a slave can marry two women at one time. (2) The blessings of a slave are half compared to a free man; thus, since a free man is allowed four, a slave is allowed two.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling that a male slave (abd) cannot marry more than two women at a time. The proof is the explicit agreement (ijma) of the Companions of the Prophet, as reported by Hakam, that a slave does not collect more than two wives. Additionally, an athar from Umar ibn al-Khattab confirms that a slave marries two women and divorces with two pronouncements (further indicating half status). The rationale is that the slave’s rights and capacity are considered half of a free man, analogous to the reduction in other matters such as punishments (e.g., hudud are half for slaves). This ruling is part of the Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi position.

Key Terms
عبد (abd): Male slave.
مملوك (mamluk): Slave (synonym for عبد).
اثنتين (ithnatayn): Two (feminine).
اجْماع (ijma): Consensus of scholars; here specifically the consensus of the Companions.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; here using the half-capacity principle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) One

C) Four

Key Takeaway
A male slave is limited to two wives based on the Companions' ijma and the principle of half legal capacity.

Free Man May Marry Up to Four Wives
Ruling on maximum wives for free man with Quran and Hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the maximum number of wives a free man may marry, identify the Quranic and Prophetic proofs, and apply the ruling to scenarios involving multiple marriages.

Core Idea
A free Muslim man may marry up to four wives; the Quran and Sunnah explicitly forbid a fifth.

This lesson addresses one of the most well-known rulings in Islamic family law: the limit of four wives. The Hanafi school, like all Sunni schools, derives this from the Quranic verse and the Prophet's practice. Understanding the proof and its application is essential for anyone studying fiqh al-nikah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is marrying multiple wives. The ruling is permissible (mubah) up to four, and prohibiting (haram) beyond four.
The text specifies 'free man', so this ruling applies only to free men.
2
Locate the dalil
Primary dalil is Quran 4:3, which explicitly limits to 'two, three, or four'. Secondary dalil is the hadith of Wahb al-Asadi, who upon embracing Islam was ordered by the Prophet to keep only four of his eight wives.
The hadith is from Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi; it is sahih.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'fankihu' indicates permission, and the enumeration 'mathna, thulatha, ruba' explicitly caps the maximum at four. The hadith confirms this by requiring the Companion to choose four.
Both proofs are qat'i in thubut and dalala, making the ruling definitive.
4
Note the scope and conditions
The ruling applies to free men. The wives may be free or slave women. The limit is simultaneous; a man cannot hold more than four at once, but may divorce and remarry.
The passage does not discuss the condition of justice among wives; that is a separate requirement.
5
Evaluate the evidence strength
The Quranic verse is mutawatir and clear; the hadith is mashhur and supports the limit. There is no ikhtilaf among the Hanafi school or the four Sunni schools on this ruling.
Cross-madhhab status: muttafaq alayh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک آزاد آدمی چار عورتوں سے بیک وقت شادی کر سکتا ہے اس سے زیادہ سے نہیں۔ چاہے چاروں آزاد عورتیں ہوں یا چاروں باندیاں ہوں یا مشترکہ ہوں۔ آیت میں ہے کہ چار سے زیادہ شادی نہ کرو۔ فانكحوا ما طاب لكم من النساء مثنى وثلث و ربع (الف) (آیت ۳ سورة النساء ۴ ) اس آیت میں چار تک شادی کرنے کی اجازت ہے (۲) ایک صحابی نے اس عورتوں سے شادی کی تھی تو ان کو چار رکھنے کی اجازت ملی باقی کو چھوڑنے کا حکم دیا۔ وقال وهب الاسدى قال اسلمت وعندى ثمان نسوة قال فذكرت ذلك للنبي الله فقال النبي الله اختر منهن اربعا (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی من اسلم وعنده نساء اکثر من اربع او اختان ص ۳۱۱ نمبر ۲۲۴۱ / ترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الرجل يسلم وعنده عشر نسوة ص۲۱۴ نمبر ۱۱۲۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ چار عورتیں جائز ہیں۔ ان سے زیادہ جائز نہیں ہے۔
A free man can marry four women at one time, not more. Whether all four are free women, or all four are slave women, or a mix. The verse says: do not marry more than four. 'Marry what is good for you of women, two, three, or four.' (Surah Nisa 4:3). This verse permits marriage up to four. (2) A Companion had married many women; he was permitted to keep four and ordered to leave the rest. Wahb al-Asadi said: 'I accepted Islam and I had eight wives. I mentioned that to the Prophet, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: Choose four of them.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). From this hadith it is known that four wives are permissible, and more than that are not permissible.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states the Hanafi position that a free Muslim man may marry up to four wives simultaneously, whether free or slave. The primary proof is from the Quran (4:3) which explicitly limits to four. The secondary proof is from the Sunnah: the hadith of Wahb al-Asadi, who upon embracing Islam was ordered by the Prophet to keep only four of his eight wives. This establishes the limit definitively. There is no ikhtilaf among the Hanafi school on this ruling.

Free Man Marrying a Slave Woman: Ruling and Condition
Ruling on free man marrying slave women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a free man marrying a slave woman and identify the condition of necessity that permits it.

Core Idea
A free man may marry only one slave woman, and only when necessary.

Marriage to a slave woman (amah) is not unrestricted for a free man. The Hanafi school permits it only under necessity—when he cannot afford to marry a free woman—and even then he is limited to one. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its basis in the athar of Ibn Abbas, and the condition that governs it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a free man marrying a slave woman. The ruling is that it is makruh tahrimi (disliked to the point of prohibition) except when necessary, and even then only one is allowed.
This is a restriction on the general permissibility of marriage.
2
Identify the condition of necessity
The necessity is defined as the inability to marry a free woman, whether due to financial incapacity or unavailability. Without this necessity, marrying a slave woman is impermissible.
The condition is based on the principle that free women are preferred for free men.
3
Recognize the textual basis
The passage cites an athar (saying) of Ibn Abbas: 'A free man may not marry from slave women except one.' This is reported in Sunan al-Bayhaqi and supports the Hanafi position.
Although the passage begins by attributing the view to Imam Shafi'i, the Hanafi school also relies on this athar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر باندی سے شادی کرنے کی ضرورت پڑ جائے تو صرف ایک باندی سے شادی کر سکتا ہے اس سے زیادہ سے (1) باندی سے شادی کرنا مجبوری کے درجے میں ہے جبکہ آزاد سے شادی کرنے کی استطاعت نہ رکھتا ہو۔ اور یہ ضرورت ایک باندی سے پوری ہو گئی اس لئے ایک باندی سے زیادہ سے شادی نہ کرے (۲) اثر میں ہے عن ابن عباس قال لا يتزوج السحر من الاماء الا واحدة (ج) (سن للبیہقی ، باب لا کر امت علی امت ج سابع ص ۱۲۸۴ نمبر ۱۲۰۰۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ صرف ایک باندی سے شادی کر سکتا ہے۔
Imam Shafi'i says: if there is a need to marry a slave woman, then he may marry only one slave woman, not more. (1) Marrying a slave woman is only in a situation of necessity, when one does not have the ability to marry a free woman. And this need is fulfilled by one slave woman, so he should not marry more than one. (2) There is an athar from Ibn Abbas: 'A free man may not marry from slave women except one.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). From this athar it is learned that he may only marry one slave woman.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on a free man marrying slave women. Although it begins by attributing the view to Imam Shafi'i, the author then quotes an athar from Ibn Abbas that supports the same ruling. The Hanafi school also holds that a free man may marry a slave woman only when necessary and only one. The necessity condition is because free women are preferred. The athar provides the textual basis. This is a ruling statement without explicit proof beyond the athar.

Key Terms

اثر (athar): Saying or action of a Companion

Slave May Marry at Most Two Wives
Ruling on the maximum number of wives for a male slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the maximum number of wives for a male slave and identify the proof from the Companions' consensus.

Core Idea
A slave may marry at most two wives because his capacity is half that of a free man.

In this lesson, we examine a clear ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the marriage limit for a male slave. Unlike a free man who may marry up to four wives, a slave is restricted to two. This ruling is based on the principle of half capacity and is supported by the practice of the Companions, as reported by Umar ibn al-Khattab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a male slave contracting marriage. The ruling: he may marry up to two wives; marrying a third is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) and invalid.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the statement of Umar ibn al-Khattab and the consensus of the Companions that a slave marries two women.
The athar is cited in the source.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit statement 'yanakahu al-'abdu imra'atayn' indicates the limit. Also, the principle of half capacity: free man can have four, so slave can have two.
The qiyas is based on other halvings like punishments.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools allow a slave to marry three or four, but the Hanafi school follows the Companion consensus.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on the stronger evidence from the Companions' consensus and the qiyas of half capacity.
No intra-Hanafi dispute; all three imams agree.

[۱۸۲۱) (۹۶) اور غلام نہ شادی کرے دو سے زیادہ۔ آزاد چار عورتوں سے شادی کر سکتا ہے لیکن غلام ان کے آدھے پر اکتفا کرے گا یعنی بیک وقت دو عورتوں سے ہی شادی کر سکتا ہے۔ عن عمر بن الخطاب قال ينكح العبد امرأتين ويطلق تطلیقین ۔ اور دوسری روایت میں ہے عن الحکم قال اجتمع اصحاب رسول الله على ان المملوك لا يجمع من النساء فوق اثنين (1) (سن لليبقى ، باب نكاح العبد وطلاقہ ج سابع میں ۲۵۵، نمبر ۱۳۸۹۸/۱۳۸۹۵ مصنف ابن ابى هبية فى المملوك كم يتزوج من النساء ج ثالث ص ۲۸۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ غلام دو عورتوں سے بیک وقت شادی کر سکتا ہے (۲) غلام کی نعمت آزاد کے مقابلے میں آدھی ہے اس لئے آزاد کو چار کی اجازت ہے تو غلام کو دو کی اجازت ہوگی۔
[1821] (96) And a slave should not marry more than two. A free man can marry four women, but a slave will suffice with half of that, i.e., he can marry only two women at a time. From Umar ibn al-Khattab: 'A slave marries two women and divorces twice.' And in another narration from al-Hakam: 'The Companions of the Messenger of Allah agreed that a slave should not accumulate more than two women.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). From this athar it is learned that a slave can marry two women at a time. (2) A slave's capacity is half that of a free man, so since a free man is allowed four, a slave is allowed two.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing that a male slave may marry no more than two wives at once. The author presents the matn, then proof from athar: the statement of Umar ibn al-Khattab and the consensus of the Companions as reported by al-Hakam. The reasoning is also given: the slave's legal capacity is half that of a free man (qiyas based on other halvings like punishments). This is a settled ruling in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
غلام (ghulam): Male slave (abd)
مملوك (mamluk): A slave owned by another

Key Takeaway
A male slave's marriage capacity is half that of a free man, so he may marry at most two wives; a third would be invalid.

Cannot Marry a Fifth Wife During the Iddah of a Bain Divorce
Ruling prohibiting fifth marriage during iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a man with four wives cannot marry a fifth until the iddah of a bain divorce expires and explain the proof from athar.

Core Idea
During iddah, the divorced wife is still legally his wife, so marrying another exceeds four.

Marriage contracts are limited to four wives at any one time. But what happens when a man divorces one of his four with a bain (irrevocable) divorce? Does the divorce free up a slot immediately? In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling that the divorced wife remains counted until her iddah expires, preventing a fifth marriage. The evidence comes from the practice of the Companions, as recorded in athar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under consideration is marrying a woman while already having four wives, one of whom is in the iddah of a bain divorce. The ruling is haram.
The prohibition is temporary, lasting until the iddah ends.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites athar (narrations) from Ali ibn Abi Talib and Amr ibn Shu'ayb, both stating that a fifth marriage is not allowed until the iddah of the divorced wife expires.
These athar are considered as Sunnah (ahad) proofs in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit wording 'he should not marry a fifth until the iddah expires' directly shows the prohibition. The illah (effective cause) is that during iddah the woman is still legally connected to the husband.
Thus, the four-wife limit is preserved during iddah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no significant ikhtilaf among the madhahib on this specific point; the ruling is mutually agreed upon (muttafaq alayh).
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah mentions no dispute here.
5
Evaluate the thamarah
The practical consequence: a man must wait for the iddah (typically three months or three menstrual cycles) before marrying a fifth woman.
If he marries before iddah ends, the marriage is invalid (batil) due to exceeding the limit.

احدى الاربع طلاقا بائنا لم يجز له ان يتزوج رابعة حتى تنقضي عدتها [ ۱۸۲۳ (۹۸) واذا زوج الامة مولاها ثم ثم اعتقت فلها الخيار حرا كان زوجها او عبدا. [۱۸۲۲] (۹۷) پس اگر آزاد نے ایک کو طلاق بائنہ دی تو اس کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ چوتھی سے شادی کرے یہاں تک کہ اس کی عدت گزر جائے آزاد آدمی کے پاس چار بیویاں تھیں ۔ ان میں سے ایک طلاق کو بائنہ دی تو جب تک اس کی عدت نہ گزرے اور شوہر سے مکمل طور پر کے پاس چار ان میں سے ایک طلاق باندی تو نہ طور پر جدائیگی نہ ہو اس وقت تک پانچویں سے شادی نہیں کر سکتا۔ جب تک طلاق شدہ عورت کی عدت نہ گزر جائے اس وقت تک وہ من وجہ شوہر کی بیوی ہے۔ اور جب چار بیوی موجود ہیں تو پانچویں سے شادی نہیں کر سکتا (۲) اثر میں ہے عن علی قال لا يتزوج خامسة حتى تنقضى عدة التي طلق (الف)(مصنف ابن ابي شيبة افی الرجل یکون تحته اربع نسوة فيطلق احداهن ج ثالث ص ۵۵۷، نمبر ۱۶۷۳۹) دوسرے اثر میں ہے عن عمر بن شعیب قال طلق رجل امرأة ثم تزوج اختها في عدتها قال نكاحها حرام ويفرق بينها و بينه حتى تنقضى عدة التي طلق (ب) مصنف ابن ابی هیتة ۱۶ افی الرجل يكون تحته الوليدة فيطلقها طلاقا با من فترجع الى سيدها فيطاً ها اكثر وجها ان يراجعھاج ثالث ص ۵۱۶، نمبر ۱۶۷۳۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جب تک عدت نہ گزر جائے پانچویں سے شادی نہیں کر سکتا۔
One of the four divorces with a bain divorce, it is not permissible for him to marry a fifth until her iddah expires. [1823] (98) And if a slave woman is married by her master then she is emancipated, she has the choice whether her husband is free or a slave. [1822] (97) So if a free man gives one of them a bain divorce, it is not permissible for him to marry a fourth until her iddah expires. A free man had four wives. He gave one a bain divorce. Until her iddah passes and she is completely separated, he cannot marry a fifth. As long as the divorced woman's iddah has not passed, she is in some respects still his wife. And when he has four wives present, he cannot marry a fifth. (2) There is an athar from Ali: 'He should not marry a fifth until the iddah of the one he divorced expires.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). Another athar from Amr ibn Shu'ayb: 'A man divorced his wife, then married her sister during her iddah. He said: her marriage is haram, and separation is made between them until the iddah of the one he divorced expires.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). From these athar it is learned that he cannot marry a fifth until the iddah expires.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with proof. It states that if a man has four wives and gives one a bain (irrevocable) divorce, he cannot marry another woman (a fifth) until the divorced wife's iddah has ended. The reason is that during iddah, the woman is still considered his wife in some respects, so marrying another would effectively give him five. The proof is from athar of Ali and Amr ibn Shu'ayb. This ruling ensures the limit of four is not circumvented.

Key Terms
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): Irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately
عدت (iddah): Waiting period after divorce or death before remarriage
أثر (athar): A narration from a Companion or Successor, often used as a proof in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Takeaway
A bain divorce does not immediately free up a slot; the divorced wife remains counted until her iddah expires.

Khiyar al-Itq: The Emancipated Slave Woman's Choice
Ruling on khiyar al-itq for a female slave emancipated after being married by her master

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-itq and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
An emancipated slave woman has the option to stay or leave her marriage, regardless of her husband's status.

This lesson examines a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the rights of a female slave upon emancipation. The Hanafi school holds that she has an unconditional choice to remain with her husband or dissolve the marriage, while the Shafi'i school restricts that choice to cases where the husband is a slave. We will analyze the evidence and reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: an emancipated slave woman has khiyar (option) to stay or leave, whether her husband is free or a slave.
This is the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees: the choice exists only if the husband is a slave.
Shafi'i relies on a different narration of the Barirah hadith.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i dalil: the hadith stating Barirah's husband was a slave and she was given the choice.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that the narration showing the husband was free is more authentic, and the choice is based on the lack of her consent in marriage, not the husband's status.
Hanafi also uses the principle that necessity (forced marriage) warrants the option.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi — a woman married to a free man can leave after emancipation; Shafi'i — she cannot.
This affects fatwa in historical contexts and informs discussions on marital consent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا زوج الامة مولاها ثم ثم اعتقت فلها الخيار حرا كان زوجها او عبدا. [۱۸۲۳] (۹۸) اگر شادی کرائی آقا نے باندی کی پھر آزاد کی گئی تو باندی کو اختیار ہوگا ، آزاد ہو اس کا شوہر یا غلام ہو۔ باندی کے آقا نے شادی کرائی بعد میں آزاد کر دی گئی تو اس باندی کو شوہر کے پاس رہنے یا نہ رہنے کا اختیار ہوگا جس کو خیار عتق کہتے ہیں۔ حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت بریرہ آزاد کی گئی تو ان کو حضور نے خیار حق دیا اور کہا کہ آپ کو شوہر کے ساتھ رہنے یا نہ رہنے کا اختیار ہے۔ اور یہ بھی حضرت عائشہ کی حدیث میں ہے کہ ان کا شوہر مغیث اس وقت آزاد تھے۔ عن عائشة ان زوج بريرة كان حرا حين اعتقت وانها خيرت (ج) ( ابو داؤد شریف، باب من قال کان حراء کتاب الطلاق ص ۱۳۱۱ نمبر ۲۲۳۵ ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء في الامتة تحقق ولها زوج ص ۲۱۹ نمبر ۱۱۵۵ر ابن ماجہ شریف، باب خیار الامته اذا اعتقت ص نمبر ۲۰۷۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت بریرہ کے شوہر آزاد تھے اس کے باوجود ان کو اختیار دیا (۲) چونکہ مولی نے شادی کرائی ہے۔ اپنے اختیار سے باندی نے شادی نہیں کی۔ اس لئے بھی آزاد ہونے کے بعد اس کو اختیار ملنا چاہئے ۔ انده امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ شوہر غلام ہو تو باندی کو اختیار ملے گا اور آزاد ہو تو اختیار نہیں ملے گا۔ حدیث میں ہے عن عائشة في قصة بريرة قالت كان زوجها عبدا فخيرها النبي الله فاختارت نفسها ولو كان حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت علی نے فرمایا پانچویں سے شادی نہ کرے یہاں تک کہ اس کی عدت گزر جائے جس کو طلاق دی ہے (ب) عمر بن شعیب نے فرمایا آدمی بیوی کو طلاق دے پھر اس کی عدت میں اس کی بہن سے شادی کرے۔ پھر اس کا نکاح حرام ہے۔ دونوں میں علیحدگی کرادی جائے یہاں تک کہ جس کو طلاق دی ہے اس کی عدت ختم ہو جائے (ج) حضرت عائشہ فرماتی ہیں کہ حضرت بریرہ کے شوہر آزاد تھے جب وہ آزاد کی گئی اور ان کو خیار حق دیا گیا تھا ( د ) ( حاشیہ اگلے صفحہ پر )
And if a master marries his slave woman, then she is emancipated, she has the choice whether her husband is free or a slave. [1823] (98) If the master marries the slave woman, then she is emancipated, the slave woman will have the choice, whether her husband is free or a slave. If the master married her, then later she is emancipated, that slave woman has the choice to stay with her husband or not, which is called khiyar al-itq. The hadith says that when Barirah was emancipated, the Prophet gave her the choice and said: 'You have the choice to stay with your husband or not.' And also in the hadith of Aisha, it says that her husband Mughith was free at that time. From Aisha: 'The husband of Barirah was free when she was emancipated, and she was given the choice.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah). This hadith shows that even though Barirah's husband was free, she was still given the choice. (2) Because the master married her; she did not marry by her own choice, so after emancipation she should have the choice. But Imam Shafi'i says: if the husband is a slave, the woman gets the choice; if the husband is free, she does not get the choice. (He cites the hadith of Aisha in the story of Barirah: she said her husband was a slave, and the Prophet gave her the choice, and she chose herself...)
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. It presents the Hanafi position on khiyar al-itq: if a female slave is married by her master (i.e., the master arranges her marriage), then she is emancipated, she has the option (khiyar) to either remain in the marriage or dissolve it, regardless of whether her husband is free or a slave. The proof is from the hadith of Barirah, where her husband was free, yet she was given the choice. The Hanafi reasoning is that because she was forced into marriage by her master, she should have the option after gaining freedom. Imam Shafi'i disagrees, holding that the choice only applies if the husband is a slave; if he is free, she has no choice. Shafi'i relies on another version of the Barirah story. The Hanafi rebuttal is that the husband was free according to Aisha's narration. The author also includes a hashiya with additional proofs.

Key Terms
خیار عتق (khiyar al-'itq): The option given to a female slave upon emancipation to continue or dissolve her marriage
امة (amah): Female slave

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a female slave who is emancipated have the choice (khiyar al-itq) to leave her husband?
A) Only if her husband was a slave at the time of her emancipation.
B) Always, whether her husband is free or a slave.
C) Only if she was married by her master without her consent.
D) Only if she hasn't consummated the marriage.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, khiyar al-itq is unconditional: an emancipated slave woman may choose to leave her marriage regardless of her husband's status.

The Option of an Emancipated Slave Woman (Khiyar al-'Itq): A Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling and proof for khiyar al-'itq with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on khiyar al-'itq, identify the proof from the hadith of Barirah, and distinguish the Shafi'i counterargument.

Core Idea
A freed slave woman married by her master has the option to stay or leave, regardless of whether her husband is free or a slave.

When a slave woman is emancipated after being married off by her master, does she have the right to annul the marriage? The Hanafi school affirms this right in all cases, while Imam al-Shafi'i restricts it. This lesson examines the key proofs and the underlying legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds regarding the option of an emancipated slave woman. Note that the option applies whether the husband is free or a slave.
The option is a right (mubah), not obligatory.
2
Identify the Hanafi dalil
Locate the proof cited by the Hanafis: the hadith of Barirah where her husband was free and the Prophet gave her the choice.
The exact phrase from the hadith is: 'عن عائشة ان زوج بريرة كان حرا حين اعتقت وانها خيرت'
3
State the Shafi'i position and dalil
Present the opposing view: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the option exists only if the husband is a slave. His proof is a different narration of the Barirah story where her husband was a slave.
The Shafi'i hadith includes: 'كان زوجها عبدا فخيرها النبي فاختارت نفسها ولو كان حرا لم يخيرها'
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Explain how the Hanafi school rebuts the Shafi'i argument: both narrations are authentic; the version with a free husband takes precedence, so the rule is general.
The Hanafi response is based on accepting both hadiths and preferring the one with the free husband as it establishes the general principle.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical consequence: Hanafis give the option in all cases; Shafi'is only when the husband is a slave.
This difference affects actual fatwa and practice.

واذا زوج الامة مولاها ثم اعتقت فلها الخيار حرا كان زوجها او عبدا. باندی کے آقا نے شادی کرائی بعد میں آزاد کر دی گئی تو اس باندی کو شوہر کے پاس رہنے یا نہ رہنے کا اختیار ہوگا جس کو خیار عتق کہتے ہیں۔ حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت بریرہ آزاد کی گئی تو ان کو حضور نے خیار حق دیا اور کہا کہ آپ کو شوہر کے ساتھ رہنے یا نہ رہنے کا اختیار ہے۔ اور یہ بھی حضرت عائشہ کی حدیث میں ہے کہ ان کا شوہر مغیث اس وقت آزاد تھے۔ عن عائشة ان زوج بريرة كان حرا حين اعتقت وانها خيرت (ابو داؤد شریف، باب من قال كان حراء کتاب الطلاق ص ۱۳۱۱ نمبر ۲۲۳۵ ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء في الامتة تحقق ولها زوج ص ۲۱۹ نمبر ۱۱۵۵ر ابن ماجہ شریف، باب خیار الامته اذا اعتقت ص نمبر ۲۰۷۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت بریرہ کے شوہر آزاد تھے اس کے باوجود ان کو اختیار دیا۔ چونکہ مولی نے شادی کرائی ہے۔ اپنے اختیار سے باندی نے شادی نہیں کی۔ اس لئے بھی آزاد ہونے کے بعد اس کو اختیار ملنا چاہئے۔ انده امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ شوہر غلام ہو تو باندی کو اختیار ملے گا اور آزاد ہو تو اختیار نہیں ملے گا۔ حدیث میں ہے عن عائشة في قصة بريرة قالت كان زوجها عبدا فخيرها النبي الله فاختارت نفسها ولو كان حرا لم يخيرها (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فى المملوكية تعتق وهى تحت حراد عبدص۳۱۰ نمبر ۲۲۳۳ ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی الامه تحقق ولھا زوج ص ۲۱۹ نمبر ۱۱۵۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ شوہر غلام ہونے کی وجہ سے اختیار دیا گیا اگر آزاد ہوتا تو اختیار نہ دیا جاتا۔ اگر اس باندی سے شوہر وطی کرے تب اختیار ختم ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اختیار ملنے کے بعد اس نے شوہر کو اختیار کیا تب ہی تو صحبت کرنے دیا۔ حدیث میں ہے عن عائشة قالت قال رسول الله ال لبيرة ان وطنك فلا خيار لك (ابوداؤد شریف، باب حتى متى يكون لها الخيار ص ۳۱۱ نمبر ۲۲۳۶ مردار قطنی ، کتاب النکاح ج ثالث ص ۲۰۴ نمبر ۳۷۳۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ صحبت کرلے تو اب اختیار باقی نہیں رہے گا۔
And if her master marries off the slave woman, then she is freed, she has the option, whether her husband is free or a slave. The slave woman's master married her off, later she was freed; so that slave woman will have the option to stay with or not stay with her husband, which is called khiyar al-'itq (option of emancipation). In the hadith, Barirah was freed, and the Prophet gave her the right of option and said, 'You have the choice to stay with your husband or leave him.' Also in the hadith of Aisha, that her husband Mughith was free at that time. From Aisha: that Barirah's husband was free when she was freed, and she was given the choice. (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah) In this hadith, Barirah's husband was free, yet she was given the option. Because the master married her off; the slave woman did not marry by her own choice. Therefore, after being freed, she should have the option. Meanwhile, Imam Shafi'i says that if the husband is a slave, the woman gets the option; if he is free, she does not get the option. There is a hadith from Aisha in the story of Barirah: she said, 'Her husband was a slave, and the Prophet gave her the choice, and she chose herself; if he had been free, he would not have given her the choice.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi) From this hadith, it is understood that the choice was given because the husband was a slave; if he were free, the choice would not have been given. If the husband has intercourse with her, then the option is lost. Because after receiving the option, she chose her husband by allowing intercourse. There is a hadith from Aisha: the Prophet said to Barirah, 'If he touches you, then you have no choice.' (Abu Dawud, al-Daraqutni) From this hadith, it is understood that if he has intercourse, the option no longer remains.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the option of an emancipated slave woman (khiyar al-'itq). The Hanafi position is that if a female slave is married off by her master and later freed, she gets the option to stay with her husband or separate, regardless of whether the husband is free or a slave. The proof is the hadith of Barirah, where her husband was free, yet the Prophet gave her the choice. The commentary then brings the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who restricts the option to cases where the husband is a slave, citing another version of the Barirah hadith where her husband was a slave. The Hanafi response is that the version with a free husband is also authentic and thus takes precedence. Additionally, the passage clarifies that if the husband has intercourse with her after she learns of her option, she loses the option because that constitutes acceptance of the marriage. This is based on another prophetic directive to Barirah.

Key Terms
خیار عتق (khiyar al-'itq): The option given to a slave woman upon emancipation to annul her marriage if she was married by her master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does an emancipated slave woman lose her option (khiyar al-'itq) to leave her husband?
A) After one month
B) If her husband is free
C) If her husband has intercourse with her after she learns of her option
D) If she lives with him for more than a year

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school grants an emancipated slave woman the option to annul her marriage regardless of her husband's status, based on the hadith of Barirah.

Khiyar al-'Itq for the Mukatabah
Extends khiyar al-'itq from full slaves to mukatabah women.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a mukatabah woman also receives the option of emancipation upon becoming free, and identify the basis for this ruling.

Core Idea
A mukatabah gets the same khiyar as a full slave upon emancipation.

In the previous lesson, we learned that a slave woman married by her master has the option to annul or stay upon emancipation. The same rule applies to a mukatabah—a slave woman who has a contract to earn her freedom. This lesson clarifies that her intermediate status does not remove her right to choose, reinforcing the general principle from the hadith of Barirah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State that the mukatabah has the khiyar al-'itq (option upon emancipation).
The option allows her to stay or leave her husband.
2
Understand the condition
The ruling applies only if the master married her off. If she married herself, the option may differ.
The passage implies the master arranged the marriage.
3
Recognize the universal scope
Her husband's status (slave or free) does not affect her right. The option is unconditional.
This differs from some other schools that limit the option based on the husband's status.
4
Connect to the dalil
The proof is the same hadith of Barirah, which is general and includes mukatabah women.
The hadith is cited in Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك المكاتبة. مکاتبہ باندی کی شادی آقا نے کرائی تھی۔ وہ مال کتابت دے کر آزاد ہوئی تو اس کو بھی خیار حق ملے گا۔ اب چاہے تو اس کے شوہر کے پاس رہے چاہے تو نہ رہے۔ چاہے اس کا شوہر غلام ہو یا آزاد ہو۔ مکاتبه باندی بھی ہے اور آقا نے شادی کرائی ہے اس لئے آزاد ہونے کے بعد حدیث کی رو سے اس کو بھی خیار عتق ملے گا۔ حدیث بریرہ پہلے گزر چکی ہے ( ابو داؤد شریف نمبر ۲۲۳۵ ترمذی شریف نمبر ۱۱۵۴)
And similarly the mukatabah. The mukatabah slave woman was married by her master. She becomes free by paying the kitabah (contract) money, so she will also get the khiyar al-'itq. Now she may stay with her husband or not, whether her husband is a slave or free. The mukatabah is also a slave woman and her master married her off, so after emancipation, by the hadith, she also gets the option of emancipation. The hadith of Barirah has preceded. (Abu Dawud no. 2235, Tirmidhi no. 1154)
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This brief passage extends the ruling on khiyar al-'itq to a mukatabah (a slave woman who has made a contract of manumission with her master and is paying off her freedom). Since she was also married by her master, upon becoming free, she too gets the option to annul the marriage or remain. The proof is the same hadith of Barirah, which is general in application. The Urdu commentary confirms that her husband's status (free or slave) does not affect her right.

Key Terms
مكاتبة (mukatabah): A female slave who has a written contract with her master to earn her freedom by paying installments or performing certain work.
خيار العتق (khiyar al-'itq): The option of emancipation: a slave woman's right to annul her marriage upon becoming free if she was married by her master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A mukatabah woman married by her master receives khiyar al-'itq upon emancipation, an unconditional right to annul or continue the marriage.

No Option for the Slave Woman Who Married Without Permission
Ruling on option after emancipation for voluntarily married slave woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a slave woman who marries without her master's permission and then is freed has a valid marriage but no option to annul it.

Core Idea
Voluntary marriage by a slave woman without permission becomes valid upon freedom, but she cannot annul it.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from Hanafi fiqh concerning a slave woman's marriage contracted without the master's permission. The question arises: when she is later freed, does she have the option (khiyar) to remain with her husband or leave? The text provides a clear answer based on the nature of the marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A slave woman marries without her master's permission, then is emancipated before the master gives permission.
The marriage was not performed under duress but voluntarily.
2
Determine the status of the marriage before emancipation
The marriage is mawquf (suspended) pending the master's permission, so it is not yet effective.
It is not void, but conditional.
3
Determine the effect of emancipation
Emancipation removes the condition: the marriage becomes valid immediately upon freedom.
The master's permission is no longer needed because the woman is free.
4
Apply the rule for khiyar al-'itq
The option to annul upon emancipation is only granted if the marriage was effective before emancipation and contracted under duress. Here, it became effective after emancipation and was voluntary, so no option.
This is the core principle from the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان تزوجت امة بغير اذن مولاها ثم اعتقت صح النكاح ولا خيار لها. ا باندی نے آقا کی اجازت کے بغیر شادی کر لی۔ ابھی آقا نے اجازت نہیں دی تھی کہ آزاد کر دی گئی تو باندی کو شوہر کے پاس رہنے یا نہ رہنے کا اختیار نہیں ملے گا۔ اب نکاح نافذ ہو جائے گا اور شوہر کے ساتھ ہی رہنا پڑے گا۔ یہ شادی آقا کے دباؤ سے نہیں ہوئی ہے۔ بلکہ خود باندی کے اختیار سے ہوئی ہے اس لئے اس کو اختیار نہیں ملے گا۔ اختیار تو اس وقت ملتا ہے جب آقا کے دباؤ سے شادی ہوئی ہو۔ آزادگی سے پہلے نکاح آقا کی اجازت پر موقوف تھا۔ نکاح نافذ نہیں ہوا تھا۔ نکاح نافذ ہوا ہے آزادگی کے بعد جو باندی کے اختیار سے تھا۔ جب باندی ہونے کے زمانے میں نکاح ہی نافذ نہیں ہوا ہے تو خیار حق کیسے ملے گا ؟ یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ آزادگی سے پہلے نکاح نافذ ہوا ہو تو خیار حق ملے گا۔ اور آزادگی کے بعد نکاح نافذ ہوا ہو تو خیار حق نہیں ملے گا۔
And if a slave woman marries without her master's permission, then is freed, the marriage is valid and she has no option. A slave woman married without her master's permission. Before the master had given permission, she was freed, so the slave woman will not get the option to stay with or leave her husband. Now the marriage becomes effective and she must remain with her husband. This marriage was not performed under the master's duress; rather, it was by the woman's own choice, so she will not get the option. The option is only given when the marriage was performed under the master's duress. Before emancipation, the marriage was contingent on the master's permission; it was not effective. It became effective after emancipation, which was by the woman's choice. When the marriage was not effective during her enslavement, how can she get the option? This case is based on the principle: if the marriage was effective before emancipation, she gets the option; if it becomes effective after emancipation, she does not get the option.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage states a conditional ruling: if a slave woman marries without her master's permission, and then later she is freed, the marriage becomes valid upon her freedom (since the master's permission was lacking, the marriage was suspended), but she has no option to annul it. The reasoning is that the option (khiyar al-'itq) is given only when the marriage was contracted under the pressure or authority of the master, i.e., against her own voluntary consent. Here, she married voluntarily, so she is deemed to have accepted the marriage. The commentary explicitly differentiates: option is granted when the marriage was effective before emancipation (i.e., with permission); if it only becomes effective after emancipation (due to the condition of permission being fulfilled by emancipation itself), then no option. This is a nuanced application of qiyas.

Key Terms
موقوف (mawquf): A marriage that is suspended pending the master's permission and becomes effective only upon permission or upon emancipation by operation of law.
خيار العتق (khiyar al-'itq): The option granted to a slave woman upon emancipation to annul her marriage if it was contracted under her master's authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of a slave woman's marriage and her right to option when she marries without her master's permission and is then freed?
A) The marriage is invalid and she has the option to leave
B) The marriage is valid and she has no option
C) The marriage is suspended and she has the option upon freedom
D) The marriage becomes valid only if the master later approves, and she has no option

Key Takeaway
A slave woman's marriage without permission becomes valid upon emancipation, but she has no option to annul if she married voluntarily.

The Principle: Marriage Effectiveness Before vs After Emancipation
Derivation of the legal principle and its qiyas application

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a slave woman loses the option to annul when her marriage becomes effective only after emancipation, and apply the underlying principle to analogous cases.

Core Idea
Option to annul exists only if the marriage was effective before emancipation; if effective after, no option.

The previous lesson presented the ruling; now we unpack its legal reasoning. The text provides a clear principle: the timing of the marriage's effectiveness determines the right to option. Let's explore how this principle is derived and applied.

Guided Path
1
Recap the two scenarios
Identify the two possible cases: marriage with master's permission (effective before emancipation) and marriage without permission (effective after emancipation).
The passage explicitly contrasts these.
2
Identify the illa (effective cause)
The effective cause for granting the option is whether the marriage was effective during the period of slavery.
This is a khafiyyah (hidden) cause, discovered by qiyas.
3
Understand the rationale
The option (khiyar al-'itq) is a remedy for marriages contracted under the master's authority, which could involve duress. If the marriage was voluntary and only became effective after freedom, there is no historical duress to remedy.
The commentary emphasizes this point.
4
Apply qiyas to other cases
Use the same illa to derive rulings for cases where a marriage becomes effective conditionally or under coercion.
This step builds critical reasoning.

Now the marriage becomes effective and she must remain with her husband. This marriage was not performed under the master's duress; rather, it was by the woman's own choice, so she will not get the option. The option is only given when the marriage was performed under the master's duress. Before emancipation, the marriage was contingent on the master's permission; it was not effective. It became effective after emancipation, which was by the woman's choice. When the marriage was not effective during her enslavement, how can she get the option? This case is based on the principle: if the marriage was effective before emancipation, she gets the option; if it becomes effective after emancipation, she does not get the option.

Commentary
This passage states a conditional ruling: if a slave woman marries without her master's permission, and then later she is freed, the marriage becomes valid upon her freedom (since the master's permission was lacking, the marriage was suspended), but she has no option to annul it. Marriage of Two Women in One Contract: One Unlawful
Ruling on a single marriage contract involving two women, one unlawful.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a man marries two women in a single contract and one is unlawful.

Core Idea
The lawful marriage is valid; the unlawful one is void ab initio.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in Islamic marriage law: a single contract encompassing two women, where one is permanently unlawful (e.g., two sisters). The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling to distinguish validity from invalidity. Although the source text is corrupted, the established ruling is preserved from reliable Hanafi sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the prohibition
The act is a single marriage contract naming two women. One of them is unlawful for the man (e.g., mahram or existing sister-in-law). Determine which relationship makes her unlawful.
Unlawful (haram) means permanently prohibited, not merely temporary.
2
Apply the Hanafi rule of partial validity
According to the Hanafi school, the contract is valid for the lawful woman and void for the unlawful one. The contract does not become entirely invalid.
The contract is severed (takhsis) based on the permissibility of each party.
3
Conclude the ruling
The marriage to the lawful woman is valid and produces all legal effects (mahr, inheritance, etc.). The marriage to the unlawful woman is void (batil) and must be annulled.
If the unlawful woman is identified, the contract is separated immediately.

And whoever marries two women in one contract... he does not give her the option. (Unclear) From this hadith it is understood that the option was given because the husband was a slave; if he were free, the option would not have been given. If the husband has intercourse with her, then the option is lost. Because after receiving the option, she chose her husband by allowing intercourse. (2) There is a hadith from Aisha: the Prophet said to Barirah, 'If he touches you, then you have no choice.' (Abu Dawud, al-Daraqutni) From this hadith, it is understood that if he has intercourse, the option no longer remains.

Ruling on Marrying Two Women When One is Forbidden
States ruling on validity when marrying two, one prohibited, with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a man marries two women, one of whom is permanently prohibited, and explain why the invalidity does not transfer to the valid marriage.

Core Idea
Invalidity does not spread: a marriage to a permissible woman remains valid even if contracted alongside a forbidden one.

This passage addresses a common scenario: a man marries two women simultaneously, but one is permanently prohibited (e.g., his sister). Does the invalidity of the forbidden marriage taint the permissible one? The Hanafi school firmly answers no, relying on a established principle and a Prophetic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The passage describes a man who marries two women simultaneously, one of whom is not lawful for him. The ruling: the marriage to the lawful woman is valid (sahih), and the marriage to the unlawful woman is void (batil).
The key point is that the two marriages are treated independently.
2
Extract the Hanafi principle
The passage mentions a principle: 'a marriage does not become invalid due to a corrupt condition.' This means that the invalidity of one contract does not automatically invalidate another, separate contract.
This principle is derived from broader Hanafi usul that fasād (corruption) in one element does not spread unless directly linked.
3
Analyze the hadith of Wahb al-Asadi
The hadith: Wahb al-Asadi embraced Islam while having eight wives. The Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed him to choose only four. This shows that the invalid marriages (those exceeding the limit) did not affect the valid ones he kept.
The Prophet did not require him to divorce all and remarry; the valid marriages remained intact.
4
Understand the application
The principle from the hadith is generalized: any impermissible factor in one marriage does not infect another marriage that is lawful. Thus, the validity of a marriage is evaluated individually.
This avoids unnecessary hardship and upholds the original validity of permissible contracts.

احديهما لا يحل له نكاحها صح نكاح التي يحل له نكاحها وبطل نكاح الاخرى

نکاح باطل ہو گا۔ لیکن اس کی وجہ سے چازاد بہن کا نکاح باطل نہیں ہوگا بلکہ اس کا نکاح صحیح رہے گا۔ (1) اصل میں نکاح شرط فاسد سے فاسد نہیں ہوتا جیسا کہ قاعدہ پہلے گزر چکا ہے۔ اس لئے اپنی بہن کا فساد چچازاد بہن میں سرایت نہیں کرے گا اور نکاح درست رہے گا (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ دس عورتوں سے شادی کی پھر اسلام لانے کے بعد چار کو بحال رکھا اور باقی کو چھٹکارا دے دیا تو جن عورتوں کو چھٹکارا دیا ان کا نکاح درست نہیں تھا پھر بھی ان کا اثر ان عورتوں کے نکاح پر نہیں پڑا جن کو بحال رکھا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ فساد کا اثر حلال پر نہیں پڑے گا۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ وقال وهب الاسدى قال اسلمت وعندى ثمان نسوة قال فذكرت ذلك للنبي الله فقال النبي الله اختر منهن اربعا (الف) ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی من اسلم وعنده نساء اکثر من اربع او اختان ص ۳۱۱ نمبر ۲۲۴۱ / ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الرجل يسلم وعنده عشرة نسوة ص ۲۱۴ نمبر ۱۱۲۸)
If one of them is not lawful for him to marry, then the marriage of the one that is lawful for him is valid, and the marriage of the other is void. [Urdu:] The marriage will be invalid. But due to this, the marriage of the paternal cousin sister will not be invalid; rather her marriage will remain valid. (1) The original principle is that a marriage does not become invalid due to a corrupt condition, as the rule has previously passed. Therefore, the corruption of one sister does not affect the paternal cousin sister, and the marriage remains valid. (2) There is a hadith that a person married ten women, then after accepting Islam, he kept four and dissolved the rest. The marriages of those he dissolved were not valid, yet their effect did not fall upon the marriages of those he kept. From this it is understood that corruption does not affect what is lawful. There is a hadith: Wahb al-Asadi said: I embraced Islam while I had eight wives. I mentioned that to the Prophet (peace be upon him), and he said: 'Choose four of them.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, Tirmidhi)
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling on a marriage scenario where a man marries two women, one of whom is not permissible for him to marry (e.g., his sister or a close relative). The ruling states that the marriage to the permissible woman is valid, and the marriage to the impermissible woman is void. The commentary explains that the invalidity does not transfer to the valid marriage, following the principle that a marriage is not nullified by a corrupt condition. It then cites a hadith about a man who had eight wives upon embracing Islam; the Prophet instructed him to keep only four. The hadith illustrates that the invalid marriages do not affect the valid ones, as the corruption of some does not spread to the permissible ones.

Key Terms
فساد (fasad): In this context, fasad refers to the invalidity or corruption of a marriage contract due to a prohibited factor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is valid.
B) It is void.
C) It is suspended until the sister marriage is annulled.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
A marriage contracted with a permissible woman remains valid even if simultaneously contracted with a prohibited woman, because corruption does not spread to what is lawful.

Ruling on Wife's Defects: No Option for Husband
Ruling that a husband does not have the option to annul the marriage due to wife's defects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school denies the husband the option to annul for wife's defects and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, a wife's defect does not give the husband the right to annul the marriage.

This passage addresses a critical difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding marital defects. While both schools recognize that defects can affect the marriage, they differ on the husband's right to separate. The Hanafi school, relying on companion reports, maintains that the husband has no option (khiyar) to annul the marriage due to the wife's defects; he may only divorce. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i allows annulment for certain serious defects.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the husband has no option to annul the marriage if the wife has a defect. He may divorce but cannot force separation.
This is the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the husband may seek annulment for serious defects like insanity, leprosy, vitiligo, or fistula.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i argument relies on a hadith where the Prophet separated due to vitiligo, and the principle that defects hinder the marriage's purpose.
The Prophet's action is a key evidence.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school counters with athar from Ali and Ata stating that the wife remains his and he is more entitled to her. Separation causes harm to the wife, so it is not permitted.
The Hanafi response prioritizes the stability of marriage.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In Hanafi fiqh, the husband cannot obtain judicial separation; in Shafi'i, he can. The practical consequence affects the couple's legal options.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۰۱۲۷ واذا كان بالزوجة عيب فلا خيار لزوجها .

( عيوب کا بیان)

[۱۸۲۷) (۱۰۲) إذا كان بالزوجة عيب فلا خيار لزوجها

شادی کرنے سے پہلے شوہر کو عیب کا پتہ نہیں تھا اور نہ اس عیب سے راضی تھا۔ شادی کے بعد اس کا علم ہوا تو عیب کی وجہ سے شوہر کو طلاق دینے اور تفریق کا اختیار نہیں ہے۔
شادی ہوتی ہے ایک دوسرے کے اطمینان کے لئے ۔ اور تفریق سے بیوی کو تکلیف ہوگی اس لئے تفریق کی اجازت نہیں ہوگی (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ قال علی ایما رجل تزوج امرأة مجنونة او جذماء او بها برص او بها قرن فهى امرأته ان شاء امسک وان شاء طلق (ب) (دار قطنی، کتاب النکاح ج ثالث ص ۱۸۷ نمبر ۳۶۳۳ سفن للبیہقی ، باب مایرد به النکاح من العيوب ج سابع ص۳۵۰ نمبر ۱۴۲۲۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عیب والی عورتیں بیوی ہیں چاہے ان کو رکھیں چاہے ان کو طلاق دیں (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ قتلت لعطاء فالرجل ان كان به بعض الاربع جذام او جنون او برص او عفل، قال ليس لها شيء هو احق بها (ع) (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب مارد من النکاح ج سادس ص ۲۴۹ نمبر ۱۰۷۰۱) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عیوب کی وجہ سے جدا کرنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جذام، برص، جنون اور قرآن کی بیماری ہو تو جدا کرنے کی گنجائش ہے۔ (۱) ان بیماریوں کی وجہ سے استفادہ مشکل ہوگا جو اصل مقصود ہے۔ اس لئے شوہر کو جدا کرنے کی اجازت ہوگی (۲) حضور نے برص کی وجہ
حاشیہ: (الف) وہب اسدی نے فرمایا میں اسلام لایا اور میرے پاس آٹھ بیویاں تھیں۔ میں نے حضور سے اس کا تذکرہ کیا تو آپ نے فرمایا ان میں سے چار کو منتخب کرلو (ب) حضرت علی نے فرمایا کسی آدمی نے مجنونہ یا جذام والی یا برص والی یا قرن والی عورت سے شادی کی تو وہ اس کی بیوی ہے۔ چاہے اپنے پاس رکھے چاہے طلاق دیدے (ج) میں نے حضرت عطاء سے کہا آدمی کو چار عیوب میں سے کوئی ہو جذام یا جنون یا برص یا عفل ہو تو عورت کو حق نہیں ہے۔ انہوں نے فرمایا مزد
عورت کا زیادہ حقدار ہے۔
10,127: If the wife has a defect, her husband has no option. (Chapter on Defects) [18,27] (102) If the wife has a defect, her husband has no option. He did not know of the defect before marriage, nor was he content with it. After marriage, when he learns of it, he does not have the option to divorce or separate due to the defect. Marriage occurs for mutual comfort, and separation would cause harm to the wife, so separation is not permitted. (2) There is an athar: Ali said: 'Any man who marries a woman who is insane, or has leprosy, or vitiligo, or a fistula, she is his wife; if he wishes, he may keep her, and if he wishes, he may divorce her.' (Darqutni, Bayhaqi) From this athar it is understood that women with defects are wives; whether they keep them or divorce them. (2) Another athar: I said to Ata: 'If a man has one of the four defects: leprosy, insanity, vitiligo, or elephantiasis, she has no right [to separation].' He said: 'He is more entitled to her.' (Abd al-Razzaq) From this athar it is understood that separation due to defects is not permitted. Imam al-Shafi'i states that if there is leprosy, vitiligo, insanity, or a fistula, there is scope for separation. (1) Because these diseases make benefit difficult, which is the primary purpose. Therefore, the husband should be allowed to separate. (2) The Prophet separated due to vitiligo. [Footnote: (b) Ali said: ... (c) I said to Ata: ... He said: He is more entitled to her.]
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on defects ('uyub) in marriage. The key ruling is that if the wife has a physical defect, the husband does not have the option (khiyar) to annul the marriage against her will. The commentary explains that the husband cannot claim separation because he did not know of the defect and did not consent to it, but the marriage bond is strong, and divorce would cause harm to the wife. This is supported by athar (reports) from Ali ibn Abi Talib and Ata ibn Abi Rabah. The passage then contrasts the Hanafi position with that of Imam al-Shafi'i, who grants the husband the option to separate if the wife has serious defects such as insanity, leprosy, vitiligo, or fistula. The Hanafi school maintains that these defects do not give the right to separation; rather, the husband may divorce but not compel separation. The passage emphasizes the principle that defects do not automatically nullify the marriage contract.

Key Terms
خيار (khiyar): Option or right to annul a contract. Here, it means the husband's right to annul the marriage due to a defect.
جذام (judham): Leprosy
برص (baras): Vitiligo
جنون (junun): Insanity
قرن (qarn): Fistula or a chronic disease
عفل (ufl): Elephantiasis or a chronic disease

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the husband's right if he discovers his wife has a serious defect after marriage?
A) He can automatically annul the marriage.
B) He has no option to annul but can divorce if he wishes.
C) He must keep her and cannot divorce.
D) He can seek annulment from the judge.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a wife's defects do not grant the husband the option to annul the marriage; he may only divorce.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Wife's Option Due to Husband's Defects
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wife's option due to husband's defects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on wife's option due to husband's defects and evaluate the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Defects in the husband do not give the wife the right to annulment—only defects in the wife do.

Within the Hanafi school, there is a notable difference of opinion on whether a wife can seek separation (khiyar) if her husband suffers from insanity, leprosy, or vitiligo. The majority view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) denies her this right, while Muhammad al-Shaybani grants it. This lesson examines the evidence for each position and the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and intra-madhhab split
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf versus that of Muhammad. Note that the dispute is about the existence of a legal right (khiyar), not a hukm taklifi.
Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf: no option. Muhammad: has option.
2
Identify the key proofs for each side
Trace the dalil for the majority: (a) hadith of Ibn Umar about returning wife for a defect, (b) athar of al-Thawri on equality. For Muhammad: (a) hadith of Ibn Abbas warning against marrying defective persons, (b) statement of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab giving wife the choice.
Muhammad's dalil are from quran/hadith; majority's are from practice and principle.
3
Evaluate the tarjih and thamarah al-khilaf
Understand why the majority view is preferred: the earlier athar and the principle of symmetry between spouses. The practical difference: without option, wife must seek khul' or wait for husband's divorce; with option, she can obtain judicial annulment.
Mufta bihi: no option.
4
Apply to a scenario
Given a case where a husband develops vitiligo after marriage, determine the wife's options under the mufta bihi position. She cannot get an annulment but may negotiate khul'.
Contrast with the view of Imam Muhammad.

كتاب النكاح
[۱۲۸ (۱۰۳) واذا كان بالزوج جنون او جذام او برص فلا خيار للمرأة عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف رحمهما الله تعالى وقال محمد رحمه الله تعالى لها الخيار
سے بیوی کو علیحدہ کیا تھا۔ عن ابن عمر ان النبى الله تزوج امرأة من بنى غفار فلما ادخلت علیه رای بکشحها بیاضا فناء عنها وقال ارخى عليك فخلى سبيلها ولم ياخذ منها شيء (الف) (سن للبیہقی ، باب ما مرد به النکاح من العيوب ج سابع جس ۱۳۴۸ نمبر (۱۴۲۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عیب کی وجہ سے بیوی کو علیحدہ کر سکتے ہیں (۳) عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله اجتنبوا في النكاح اربعة الجنون والجذام و البرص (ب) (دار قطنی ، کتاب النکاح ج ثالث نمبر ۳۶۲۸) (۴) عن سعيد بن المسيب قال قضى عمر في البرصاء والجذماء والمجنونة اذا دخل بها فرق بينهما والصداق لها لمسيسه اياها وهو له على وليها (ج) (دار قطنى ، كتاب النکاح ج ثالث ص ۱۸۷ نمبر ۳۶۳۱ سفن للبیہقی ، باب ما یرد بی النکاح من العيوب ج سابع ، مايرد ص ۳۴۹، نمبر ۱۴۲۲۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ان عیوب کی وجہ سے میاں بیوی میں تفریق کی جاسکتی ہے۔ [۱۸۲۸ (۱۰۳) اگر شوہر کو جنون ہو یا جذام ہو یا برص ہو تو عورت کے لئے اختیار نہیں ہے امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ۔ اور فرمایا امام محمد نے اس کے لئے اختیار ہے۔ او پر مسلہ نمبر ۱۰ میں اثر گزر گیا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ شوہر کو جنون وغیرہ ہو تو عورت کو تفریق کرانے کا اختیار نہیں ہو گا (۲) ایک اور اثر میں ہے۔ عن الثورى فى رجل يحدث به بلاء لايفرق بينهما هو بمنزلة المرأة لا يرد الرجل ولا ترد المرأة وذكره عن حماد عن ابراهيم (و) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب مارد من النکاح ج سادس ص ۲۴۹ نمبر ۱۰۷۰۰) اس اثر سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ تفریق نہیں کرائی جائیگی۔ نا امام محمد قرماتے ہیں کہ شوہر کو جنون، جذام یا برص ہو تو عورت کو قاضی کے ذریعہ تفریق کرانے کا حق ہوگا۔ او پر حدیث گزر چکی ہے کہ عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله اجتنبوا في النكاح اربعة الجنون والجذام والبرص (ه) (دار قطنی ، کتاب النکاح ج ثالث ص ۱۸۶ نمبر ۳۶۲۸) (۲) عن سعيد بن المسيب قال ايما رجل تزوج امرأة وبه جنون او ضرر فانها تختر فان شاءت فارقته وان شاءت قرت (و) (سنن ) ن للبیہقی ، باب ما یرد به النکاح من العيوب ج سابع ص ۱۳۵۱ نمبر
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے بنی غفار کی عورت سے شادی کی۔ پس جب ان کے پاس گئے تو اس کے پہلو میں برص کی بیماری دیکھی تو آپ ان سے دور ہو گئے اور فرمایا پردہ کرلو اور اس کو رخصت کر دیا اور ان سے دیا ہوا مہر نہیں لیا (ب) آپ نے فرمایا نکاح میں چار عیوب سے بچو۔ جنون ، کوڑھ اور برص کی بیماری سے (ج) حضرت عمر نے برص والی، کوڑھ والی اور مجنونہ عورتوں کے بارے میں فیصلہ فرمایا کہ ان سے محبت کی ہو پھر بھی تفریق کی جائے گی۔ اور اس صحبت کی وجہ سے مہر لازم ہو گا۔ اور وہ مہر عورت کے ولی سے شوہر وصول کرے گا (1) حضرت ثوری نے فرمایا کسی آدمی پر بلاء نازل ہو جائے تو دونوں میں تفریق نہیں کی جائے گی۔ اور مرد عورت کی طرح ہے، نہ مرد لوٹا یا جائے گا نہ عورت لوٹائی جائے گی۔ یعنی کسی کے مرض کی وجہ سے تفریق نہیں ہوگی۔ یہی قول حضرت حماد نے حضرت ابراہیم سے نقل کیا ہے (و) آپ نے فرمایا نکاح میں چار بیماریوں سے بچو ۔ جنون، کوڑھ اور برص سے (1) حضرت سعید بن مسیب نے فرمایا کسی آدمی نے عورت سے شادی کی (باقی اگلے صفحہ پر )
اس اثر سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ عورت کو ان عیوب کی وجہ سے تفریق کا اختیار ہوگا۔ حاشیہ : (پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے ) اور اس کو جنون یا کوئی بیماری ہو تو عورت کو اختیار ہوگا۔ چاہے تو مرد کو جدا کر دے، چاہے تو اس کے پاس ٹھہری رہے
Book of Marriage. [128 (103)] And if the husband has insanity, leprosy, or vitiligo, there is no option for the woman according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on them. Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, said: She has the option. ... This effect also indicates that the woman has the option to separate due to these defects. Footnote: (continuation from previous page) And if he has insanity or any illness, the woman has the option. If she wishes, she may separate from him; if she wishes, she may stay with him.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the wife's right to seek dissolution of marriage when the husband suffers from insanity (junun), leprosy (judham), or vitiligo (baras). The passage begins by stating the ruling (no. 103) and then provides proofs and counter-proofs. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the wife has no option to separate (khiyar al-faskh) due to these defects in the husband. Their position is supported by an athar from al-Thawri and also by the principle that defects in the husband do not give the wife the right to annulment, analogous to the rule for the wife's defects (as mentioned in earlier discussion). Muhammad al-Shaybani, however, holds that the wife does have the option. He quotes the hadith of Ibn Abbas (marfu'an): 'Avoid four things in marriage: insanity, leprosy, and vitiligo,' and the statement of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab that any man who marries a woman with insanity or harm, she may choose to leave or stay. The text then includes footnotes explaining each hadith/athar. The author concludes that the relied-upon position is that of the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), as the effect of Umar regarding the wife's defects does not apply symmetrically to the husband. This is the mu'tamad position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
خيار (khiyar): The option or right to choose to continue or dissolve a marriage contract due to a defect.
جنون (junun): Insanity or mental disorder, a defect giving rise to khiyar in marriage according to some scholars.
جذام (judham): Leprosy, a contagious disease considered a defect in marriage.
برص (baras): Vitiligo or leprosy, a skin disease considered a defect in marriage.
فرقة (furqah): Separation or dissolution of the marriage, either by talaq or faskh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if the husband suffers from insanity after marriage, does the wife have the right to seek separation (khiyar)?
A) Yes, she has the right to seek separation through the qadi.
B) No, she has no right to seek separation (khiyar).
C) It depends on the type of insanity.
D) Only if the insanity existed before marriage.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the wife cannot seek annulment for the husband's insanity, leprosy, or vitiligo; she must rely on khul' or talaq.

Impotent Husband (Anin): Deferral and Separation as Talaq Ba'in
Ruling on the impotent husband and the judge's deferral procedure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on an impotent husband (anin), including the one-year deferral procedure and whether the resulting separation is a talaq or faskh.

Core Idea
An impotent husband gets one year; if still unable, the judge separates them as a talaq ba'in — protecting the wife's rights.

This lesson addresses the case of an impotent husband (anin) — a man unable to consummate the marriage. The Hanafi school grants him a one-year deferral for treatment, but if he remains impotent and the wife demands separation, the judge pronounces a divorce that counts as talaq ba'in. The ruling is derived from the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab and relevant hadith, ensuring the wife is not trapped in a barren marriage while preserving the husband's chance to recover.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the judge's procedure for an impotent husband. The ruling is: the judge gives a one-year deferral; if no improvement, separation upon wife's demand is a talaq ba'in.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence includes the practice of Umar (radiAllahu anhu) recorded by Darqutni and Bayhaqi, and the hadith of the wife of Rifa'a (Muslim).
The hadith implies permissibility of separation due to impotence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Umar explicitly decreed one year then separation; the Prophet's silence when the wife complained indicates support for separation.
The wife's description of her husband as 'like the fringe of a garment' confirms impotence.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) also grant one year but consider the separation an annulment (faskh), not a talaq. The Hanafi view holds it as talaq ba'in because the defect is from the husband.
The practical difference: after talaq ba'in, remarriage requires new contract; after faskh, no iddah? Actually iddah is required in both. The main difference is whether it counts towards the three divorces.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi based on the practice of Umar and Ibn Mas'ud, and analogy that the husband's defect makes the divorce attributable to him.
The wife retains full mahr if valid seclusion occurred.

۱۳۹ (۱۰۴) اگر شوہر عنین ہو تو حاکم اس کو مہلت دے گا ایک سال۔ پس اگر صحبت کر لے اس مدت میں تو عورت کو اختیار نہیں ہوگا ورنہ دونوں میں تفریق کر دے اگر عورت اس کا مطالبہ کرے۔
شوہر نامرد ہو، بیوی سے صحبت نہ کر سکتا ہو تو حاکم اس کو ایک سال تک مہلت دے گا تا کہ اس کا علاج کرائے ۔ پس اگر ایک سال میں صحبت کے قابل ہو گیا تو ٹھیک ہے۔ اور اگر محبت کے قابل نہ ہوا اور عورت نے علیحدگی کا مطالبہ کیا تو حاکم تفریق کر دیں گے۔ (۱) ایک سال میں تینوں موسم ہیں اس لئے آسانی سے علاج کراسکتا ہے اس لئے ایک سال کی مہلت دی جائے گی (۲) اثر میں ہے عہ عمر قال يوجل العنين سنة (الف) (دار قطنی ، کتاب النکاح ج ثالث ص ۲۱۱ نمبر ۳۷۶۹) اور سنن بیہقی میں یوں ہے۔ عن عمر بن الخطاب انه قال في العنين يوجل سنة فان قدر عليها والا فرق بينهما ولها المهر وعليها العدة(ب) (سن ليبقى ، باب اجل العنين ج سابع ، ص ۱۳۶۸، نمبر ۱۴۲۸۹/ مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب اجل العنین ج سادس ص ۲۵۳ نمبر ۱۰۷۲۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ حاکم کے پاس معاملے لے جانے کے وقت سے ایک سال کی مہلت دی جائے گی۔ اس مدت میں محبت کے قابل ہو جائے تو ٹھیک ہے ورنہ عورت کے مطالبے پر تفریق کر دی جائے گی۔ پھر عورت کو مہر بھی ملے گا اور اس پر عدت بھی لازم ہوگی۔ کیونکہ خلوت صحیحہ ہو چکی ہے۔ حنین میں تفریق کا مسئلہ امراة رفاعہ کی حدیث سے ثابت ہے کہ حضرت رفاعہ کی بیوی نے فرمایا کہ میرا شوہر محبت نہیں کر سکتا وہ کپڑے کی پلو کی طرح نرم اور کمزور ہے۔ حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت جاءت امرأة رفاعة الى النبي الله فقالت ... وانما معه مثل هدية الثوب الخ (ج) (مسلم شريف، باب لا تحل المطلقة مثلا المطلقها الخ ص ۲۶۳ نمبر ۱۴۳۳)
