عنین ہونے کی وجہ سے جو علیحدگی ہوگی یہ طلاق بائنہ کے درجے میں ہوگی۔
یہ فرقت مرد کی جانب سے ہو رہی ہے کیونکہ اسی میں مرض ہے۔ اور مرد کی جانب سے جو فرقت ہوتی ہے وہ طلاق شمار ہوتی ہے۔ اور طلاق رجعی سے عورت کی جان مکمل نہیں چھوٹے گی اس لئے طلاق بائنہ کے درجے میں ہوگی تاکہ عورت کی جان مکمل چھوٹ جائے (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ ان عمر وابن مسعود قضيا بانها تنتظر به سنة ثم تعتد بعد السنة عدة المطلقة وهو احق بامرها في
1 (104) And if the husband is impotent, the judge gives him a period of one year. If he has intercourse during this period, then she has no option. Otherwise, he separates them if the woman demands that. [1830] (105) And the separation is (counted as) a divorce (talaq ba'in). ... Explanation: If the husband is impotent, the judge gives him a one-year grace period. If he becomes capable of intercourse within that year, then fine. If not, and the woman demands separation, the judge will separate them. This separation is in the category of talaq ba'in (irrevocable divorce).
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on an impotent husband (anin). The term 'anin' refers to a man who cannot achieve or maintain an erection sufficient for intercourse. The Hanafi ruling is that the judge (qadi) grants the husband a deferral of one full year from the date the wife brings the complaint to court. The reason for one year is to cover all seasons and allow for treatment (as climate may affect health). If the husband becomes capable of intercourse within that year, the marriage continues and the wife has no right to demand separation. If after one year he remains impotent and the wife demands separation, the judge separates them. This separation is not an annulment (faskh) but counts as a talaq ba'in (irrevocable divorce) by the husband because the defect is from his side. The wife retains the full mahr (since valid seclusion/khalwa sahiha occurred) and must observe iddah. The proof comes from the action of Umar ibn al-Khattab (radyAllahu anhu) and the hadith of the wife of Rifa'a who complained that her husband was like a garment fringe (weak). The sabab for this rule is the husband's inability, and the hikmah is to protect the wife's right to a fulfilling marriage without leaving her in suspense indefinitely.

Key Terms
عنين (anin): A man who is impotent and unable to have intercourse with his wife due to physical or psychological reasons.
تطليقة (tatliqah): A single divorce, counted as talaq ba'in in this context.
خلوت صحیحہ (khalwa sahiha): Valid seclusion between husband and wife that implies full mahr and iddah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a wife complains of her husband's impotence and the judge grants a one-year deferral, what happens if the husband remains impotent after the year and the wife demands separation?
A) The judge declares the marriage annulled (faskh).
B) The judge separates them and it counts as one talaq ba'in.
C) The marriage continues indefinitely.
D) The wife must seek khul'.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, separation due to the husband's impotence is a talaq ba'in after a one-year deferral, not an annulment.

Ruling on Impotence: The Judge's One-Year Delay and its Proof
States ruling on 'anin and provides proof from Umar's athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on impotence ('unna) and explain the proof from the athar of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab.

Core Idea
The impotent husband gets one year; if he remains incapable, the wife may seek separation.

This lesson addresses a specific marital defect: impotence in the husband. The Hanafi school provides a structured procedure: the judge grants a one-year delay for treatment, and only if the condition persists and the wife requests it, separation is effected. The ruling is grounded in the practice of 'Umar, which forms the primary proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Recognize that the ruling concerns the husband being impotent (anin). The judge must grant a one-year delay (ajal). Determine the hukm: wajib upon the judge to give the delay, and separation (firqah) is a talaq upon the wife's request if no cure.
The delay is not from the marriage contract but from the time the case is brought to the judge.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the athar of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab transmitted in Dar Qutni, Sunan al-Bayhaqi, and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq. This is a qawl sahabi (Companion's statement) and acts as a sunnah proof.
The text provides the Arabic: عن عمر بن الخطاب انه قال في العنين يوجل سنة...
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the athar proves the ruling. The explicit statement 'yujjal sanah' indicates a one-year delay, and 'illa farraqa baynahuma' shows separation if no cure. The mention of mahr and iddah supports that separation is a divorce.
The Hanafi school accepts qawl sahabi as a proof in the absence of contradictory evidence.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the opposing view: the Shafi'i school does not grant a delay and permits immediate separation upon the wife's request. Their proof may include general principles of harm and lack of textual evidence for the delay.
This is a mukhtalaf fih issue; the Hanafi position relies on the specific athar.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand why the Hanafi school adopts the one-year delay: the athar is considered strong evidence, and the delay gives opportunity for treatment which aligns with the objective of preserving marriage. The wisdom of one year includes all seasons for treatment.
The ruling is part of Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text

(104) And if the husband is impotent (anin), the judge gives him a delay of one year. If he has intercourse during this period, then she has no choice; otherwise, they are separated if the woman requests that. [1830] (105) And the separation is a divorce. Also understood from this evidence is that a woman will have the option of separation due to these defects. 139 (104) If the husband is impotent, the judge will grant a one-year delay. If he has intercourse during this period, the woman has no option; otherwise, if the woman requests, he will separate them. The husband is impotent, cannot have intercourse with his wife, so the judge gives him a one-year delay so that he can be treated. Then if within one year he becomes capable of intercourse, it is fine. If he does not become capable and the woman demands separation, the judge will separate them. (1) All three seasons occur within one year, so he can easily get treatment; hence one year is given. (2) There is an athar: 'Umar said: He gives a one-year delay to the anin. (Dar Qutni, Kitab al-Nikah, vol. 3, p. 211, no. 3769) And in Sunan al-Bayhaqi: From 'Umar ibn al-Khattab that he said regarding the anin: A delay of one year is given; if he is able to have intercourse, [fine]; otherwise, they are separated, and she gets the mahr and she must observe the iddah. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Ajl al-Anin, vol. 7, p. 1368, no. 14289; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab Ajl al-Anin, vol. 6, p. 253, no. 10720) From this athar it is understood that from the time the case is taken to the judge, a one-year delay will be given. If he becomes capable during this period, fine; otherwise, upon the woman's request, separation will be effected. Then the woman also gets the mahr, and she must observe iddah because valid seclusion (khalwa sahiha) had occurred. Regarding the issue of separation due to impotence, it is proven by the hadith of the wife of Rifa'a: The wife of Rifa'a said, 'My husband cannot have intercourse; he is like the fringe of a garment, soft and weak.' A portion of the hadith: From Aisha: The wife of Rifa'a came to the Prophet and said, '... and he has with him only like the fringe of a garment...' (Muslim, Bab La Tahill al-Mutallaqa... p. 263, no. 1433)
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on impotence (unna) in marriage. The ruling states that if the husband is impotent (anin), the judge grants a one-year delay (ajal) to allow for treatment. During this year, if the husband becomes capable of intercourse, the wife has no right to seek separation. If he remains incapable and the wife requests separation, the judge separates them. The wisdom of one year is that it includes all seasons, giving ample opportunity for treatment. The proof is the athar of Umar, who gave a one-year delay for anin. The commentary also mentions that upon separation, the wife gets full mahr and must observe iddah because valid seclusion had occurred, citing the hadith of the wife of Rifa'a to illustrate the condition of impotence.

Key Terms
عنين (anin): A man who is impotent, unable to have intercourse with his wife.
اجل (ajal): A fixed period of delay granted by the judge for treatment of impotence.
تفريق (tafriq): Separation or divorce ordered by the judge due to a defect like impotence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Six months
B) One year
C) Two years
D) No delay is given

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school gives a one-year delay to an impotent husband; only if he remains incapable after that and the wife requests can the judge order separation.

Separation Due to Impotence: Ba'in Divorce
Clarifies that separation due to 'unna is a ba'in divorce and provides proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school classifies separation due to impotence as a ba'in divorce and cite the proof from the Companions.

Core Idea
Separation due to impotence is a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce, not an annulment, to fully free the woman.

In Hanafi law, when a husband is impotent ('unna) and unable to consummate the marriage, the wife may seek a judicial separation. This passage explains why that separation is considered a ba'in divorce (irrevocable) rather than a revocable one or an annulment. The ruling is based on the reasoning that the defect is from the man, so the separation is attributed to him, and to fully liberate the woman it must be final. The proof comes from the practice of the Companions Umar and Ibn Mas'ud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State that the separation due to impotence is a ba'in divorce (irrevocable).
The text says 'والفرقة تطليقة بائنة'.
2
Understand the rationale
The separation is from the man's side because he has the defect; hence it is treated as a divorce. A revocable divorce would not fully free the woman, so it must be irrevocable.
3
Locate the proof
The proof is from the athar of Umar and Ibn Mas'ud: she waits one year, then observes the iddah of a divorced woman, and he has more right to take her back during the iddah.
This indicates the separation is treated as a divorce, not an annulment.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools consider separation due to impotence a faskh (annulment) rather than talaq. The Hanafi school treats it as ba'in talaq.
5
Recognize the legal effect
As a ba'in divorce, the husband cannot take back his wife without a new marriage contract. She is completely free after the iddah.
This prioritizes the wife's freedom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۰۵) والفرقة تطليقة بائنة [۱۸۳۰) (۱۰۵) اور فرقت طلاق بائنہ کے درجے میں ہوگی۔ عنین ہونے کی وجہ سے جو علیحدگی ہوگی یہ طلاق بائنہ کے درجے میں ہوگی۔ یہ فرقت مرد کی جانب سے ہو رہی ہے کیونکہ اسی میں مرض ہے۔ اور مرد کی جانب سے جو فرقت ہوتی ہے وہ طلاق شمار ہوتی ہے۔ اور طلاق رجعی سے عورت کی جان مکمل نہیں چھوٹے گی اس لئے طلاق بائنہ کے درجے میں ہوگی تاکہ عورت کی جان مکمل چھوٹ جائے (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ ان عمر وابن مسعود قضيا بانها تنتظر به سنة ثم تعتد بعد السنة عدة المطلقة وهو احق بامرها في حاشیہ : (پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے ) اور اس کو جنون یا کوئی بیماری ہو تو عورت کو اختیار ہوگا۔ چاہے تو مرد کو جدا کر دے، چاہے تو اس کے پاس ٹھہری رہے (الف) حضرت عمر نے فرمایا نین کو ایک سال کی مہلت دی جائے گی (ب) حضرت عمرؓ نے فرمایا عنین کی وجہ سے ایک سال کی مہلت دی جائے گی۔ پس اگر عورت پر قدرت ہو گئی تو ٹھیک ہے اور نہ دونوں میں تفریق کر دی جائے گی۔ اور عورت کے لئے مہر ہوگا اور اس پر عدت ہوگی (ج) حضرت رفاعہ کی بیوی حضور کے پاس آئی اور کہا ۔ اس کے پاس کپڑے کے پلو کی طرح ہے۔
(105) And the separation is a ba'in divorce. [1830] (105) And the separation will be of the level of ba'in divorce. The separation that occurs due to impotence will be of the level of ba'in divorce. This separation is from the man's side because he has the defect. And the separation that comes from the man's side is counted as divorce. And with a revocable divorce (raj'i), the woman does not fully become free, so it will be a ba'in divorce so that the woman becomes completely free. (2) There is proof in the athar: 'Umar and Ibn Mas'ud ruled that she waits for him for one year, then after the year observes the iddah of a divorced woman, and he has more right to her [during iddah]. In the margin: (From previous page) And if there is insanity or any other disease, the woman has an option. She can separate from the man or stay with him. (a) 'Umar said: The anin will be given a one-year delay. (b) 'Umar said: Due to impotence, a one-year delay is given; if he becomes capable, fine; otherwise, they are separated, and she gets the mahr and observes iddah. (c) The wife of Rifa'a came to the Prophet and said: He has with him only like the fringe of a garment.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage clarifies the nature of the judicial separation due to impotence. It is a ba'in divorce (irrevocable), not a revocable divorce. The reasoning is that since the defect is from the man, the separation is attributed to him, and it must be irrevocable to fully free the woman from the marriage. The proof is from the athar of Umar and Ibn Mas'ud, who ruled that after one year, the woman observes the iddah of a divorced woman, and the man is more entitled to take her back during iddah (implying it is a revocable divorce in their ruling? The text says 'he has more right to her' which suggests revocability, but the Hanafi position is that it is ba'in. There may be a nuance: the athar states 'he has more right to her' regarding the waiting period, but the Hanafi school interprets the separation as ba'in because the defect is incurable and the wife's freedom is prioritized. The margin note adds that for other defects like insanity, the wife has an option to separate or stay.

Key Terms
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that does not allow the husband to take back his wife without a new marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Faskh (annulment)
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, judicial separation due to impotence is a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce, supported by the athar of Umar and Ibn Mas'ud.

Full Mahr for Wife After Valid Seclusion Before Separation Due to Impotence
States that wife gets full mahr if valid seclusion occurred, with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that valid seclusion (khalwa sahiha) obligates full mahr even without intercourse, and explain the proofs from the mursal hadith and the athar of Ali.

Core Idea
Valid seclusion obligates full mahr even without intercourse.

When a marriage ends due to the husband's impotence after valid seclusion, does the wife still deserve the full dower? The Hanafi school answers yes, based on prophetic hadith and the practice of the Companions. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the proofs, and the key concept of khalwa sahiha.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the legal act (separation due to impotence after valid seclusion) and the ruling (full mahr is wajib). Note that the wife has submitted herself, so the mahr is due.
Ruling applies only if seclusion was valid — no impediment to intercourse.
2
Locate the primary proof
Find the athar of Umar (passed in ruling 104) which says 'she gets the mahr and she observes iddah'. Also note the specific proofs: the mursal hadith and the athar of Ali.
The athar of Umar establishes the general principle; the specific proofs are for the condition of seclusion.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For the hadith: the Prophet said that uncovering a wife's veil and looking at her makes the dower obligatory, whether intercourse occurred or not. This is applied to seclusion (khalwa) because seclusion implies the same privacy and opportunity. For the athar of Ali: closing the door and letting down a curtain, or seeing the private parts, makes the dower due.
The key phrase in the hadith is 'دخل بها او لم يدخل بها' – whether he had intercourse or not.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school does not consider khalwa alone sufficient for full mahr; they require actual intercourse. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within fiqh.
Hanafi proofs are based on the hadith and athar, which explicitly link seclusion to the dower.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi within the school, supported by the zahir al-riwayah texts. The hadith and athar are considered sufficient evidence.
Even though the hadith is mursal and zanni, it is accepted in Hanafi usul for non-criminal matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عمر اور حضرت ابن مسعود نے فیصلہ کیا کہ منین میں وہ ایک سال تک انتظار کرے گی۔ پھر ایک سال کے بعد مطلقہ کی عدت گزارے گی۔ اور مرد عورت کے معاملے کا زیادہ حقدار ہو گا عورت کی عدت میں (ب) عورت کو مہر ملے گا اور اس پر عدت ہوگی (ج) آپ نے فرمایا کسی نے بیوی کی اوڑھنی کھولی اور اس کو دیکھا تو اس پر مہر لازم ہو گا صحبت کی ہو یا نہ کی ہو ( 1 ) حضرت علی نے فرمایا اگر دروازہ بند کیا اور پردہ لٹکا دیا یا سر کو دیکھا تو شوہر پر مہر لازم ہوگا۔
(106) And she gets the full mahr if he had seclusion with her. [1831] (106) The woman will get the full mahr if he had seclusion with her. Even if the anin could not have intercourse, which is why separation occurred, still the rule is that if he had seclusion, full mahr is due. (1) The woman has submitted herself, so she gets the mahr. (2) Above in ruling 104, the athar of Umar passed: 'and she gets the mahr and she observes iddah.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Ajl al-Anin, vol. 7, p. 1368, no. 14289; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab Ajl al-Anin, vol. 6, p. 253, no. 10727/10721) And for seclusion, mahr becomes due; its proof is the mursal hadith: From Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Thawban, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Beware! Whoever uncovers a woman's veil and looks at her, then the dower becomes obligatory, whether he had intercourse with her or not.' (Dar Qutni, Kitab al-Nikah, vol. 3, p. 213, no. 3780) And the athar of Ali: From Ali, he said: 'If he closes a door and lets down a curtain, or sees the private parts, then the dower is due upon him.' (Dar Qutni, Kitab al-Nikah, vol. 3, p. 212, no. 2777) From this athar it is understood that if seclusion occurred, full mahr is due.
Marginal notes: (a) 'Umar and Ibn Mas'ud ruled that in case of anin, she waits for him for one year, then after the year observes the iddah of a divorced woman, and he has more right to her during her iddah. (b) The woman gets the mahr and she observes iddah. (c) He said: Whoever uncovers his wife's veil and looks at her, then mahr becomes due, whether he had intercourse or not. (d) Ali said: If he closes the door and lets down a curtain or sees the private parts, then mahr is due upon him.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This ruling establishes that if a valid seclusion (khalwa sahiha) occurred between the anin husband and his wife, the wife is entitled to the full mahr despite the subsequent separation due to impotence. The proof is from the athar of Umar which states that the wife gets the mahr and observes iddah. Additional proofs include a mursal hadith from the Prophet that dower becomes obligatory upon seclusion even without intercourse, and an athar from Ali that seclusion with closing doors and letting down curtains makes the dower due. The commentary underscores that because the wife submitted herself to the husband, the mahr is fully owed.

Key Terms
خلوت صحیحہ (khalwa sahiha): Valid seclusion between husband and wife in private, with no legal or physical impediment to intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) The passage of one year

Key Takeaway
Valid seclusion (khalwa sahiha) makes the full mahr wajib even without intercourse, based on explicit hadith and athar.

Full Mahr Obligatory After Khalwah Even with Impotent Husband
Ruling with proof that khalwah obligates full mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that valid khalwah (privacy) obligates the full mahr, and identify the evidence from mursal hadith and athar of Ali.

Core Idea
Khalwah alone obligates the full mahr, even if intercourse is impossible.

In this passage, we examine a key Hanafi ruling: the wife's entitlement to full mahr upon valid khalwah, regardless of consummation. The author supports this with a mursal hadith and an athar of Ali. Understanding this rule clarifies the legal effect of privacy in marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the opening statement: the woman gets full mahr if the husband had khalwah with her. Note that this applies even if he is impotent.
The ruling is unconditional regarding consummation.
2
Locate the evidence
The author cites two pieces of evidence: a mursal hadith from Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Thawban and an athar from Ali ibn Abi Talib.
Mursal hadith is accepted in Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze the mursal hadith
The hadith states that the dower becomes obligatory upon uncovering the veil and looking, regardless of whether intercourse occurs. Identify the operative phrase 'fagad wajaba al-sadaq'.
The phrase directly indicates obligation.
4
Analyze the athar of Ali
The athar says that closing the door and drawing the curtain, or seeing the private part, obligates the dower. This establishes khalwah as the trigger.
Both narrations emphasize privacy, not intercourse.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Some schools require actual intercourse for full mahr. The Hanafi school stands on khalwah as sufficient.
Be aware of the khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولها كمال المهر اذا كان قد خلا بها. [۱۸۳۱] (۱۰۶) عورت کے لئے پورا مہر ہوگا اگر اس سے خلوت کر چکا ہو۔ عنین اگر چہ محبت کا ملہ نہیں کر سکتا اسی لئے علیحدگی ہوئی ہے پھر بھی مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ خلوت کر چکا ہوتو پورا مہر لازم ہوگا۔ (۱) عورت نے اپنا مال سپرد کر دیا ہے اس لئے اس کو مہر ملے گا (۲) اوپر مسئلہ نمبر ۱۰۴ میں حضرت عمر کا اثر گزرا ولهـا الـمـهـر وعليها العدة (ب) (سن للبیہقی ، باب اجل العنين صبح سابع ص ۱۳۶۸ نمبر ۱۴۲۸۹ر مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب اجل العنين ج سادس ص ۲۵۳ نمبر ۱۰۷۲۷/۱۰۷۲۱) اور خلوت کرنے پر مہر لازم ہوگا اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث مرسل ہے۔ عن محمد بن عبد الرحمن بن ثوبان قال قال رسول الله الا الله من كشف خمار امرأة ونظر اليها فقد وجب الصداق دخل بها او لم يدخل بها (ج) (دارقطنی، کتاب النکاح ج ثالث ص ۲۱۳ نمبر ۳۷۸۰) او حضرت علی کا یہ اثر ہے۔ عن علی قال اذا اغلق بابا وارخی سترا او راى عورة فقد وجب عليه الصداق (د) (دار قطنی، کتاب النکاح ج ثالث ص ۲۱۲ نمبر ۲۷۷۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ خلوت ہوئی ہو تو پورا مہر لازم ہوگا۔
For her is the full mahr if he had privacy with her. [1831] (106) For the woman, the full mahr will be if he had privacy with her. Even though the impotent man cannot achieve intercourse, due to which separation occurred, still the rule is that if he had privacy, the full mahr becomes obligatory. (1) The woman has entrusted her wealth to him, so she should get the mahr. (2) Above in problem no. 104, the athar of Umar passed: 'For her is the mahr and upon her is the iddah.' And for privacy obligating mahr, the proof is this mursal hadith: From Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Thawban, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Beware! Whoever uncovers the veil of a woman and looks at her, then the dower becomes obligatory, whether he entered with her or did not enter.' And this athar of Ali: From Ali, he said: 'When he closes the door and lets down the curtain, or sees the private part, then the dower becomes obligatory upon him.' From this athar it is known that if privacy occurred, the full mahr is obligatory.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states the Hanafi position that if a husband has had valid khalwah (privacy) with his wife, the full mahr becomes obligatory, even if he is impotent and cannot consummate the marriage. The author provides two evidences: first, the mursal hadith from Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Thawban that the Prophet (peace be upon him) declared the dower obligatory upon uncovering the wife's veil and looking at her, regardless of intercourse. Hanafis accept mursal hadith as proof. Second, the athar of Ali ibn Abi Talib that closing the door and letting down the curtain or seeing the private part obligates the dower. The commentary clarifies that even though separation occurs due to impotence, the full mahr is still due because the wife has submitted herself (entrusted her wealth) and khalwah triggers the obligation by istihsan, supported by these narrations.

Key Terms
خلوت (khalwah): Valid privacy between spouses in a marriage that is not impeded by legal or physical barriers.
مهر (mahr): The mandatory bridal gift from husband to wife, becoming fully due upon valid khalwah or consummation.
عنین (‘innin): A man who is impotent, unable to perform intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what obligates the full mahr to the wife?
A) Only actual intercourse
B) Valid khalwah (privacy) after marriage
C) The signing of the marriage contract only
D) The wife demanding the mahr

Key Takeaway
Valid khalwah (privacy) after marriage obligates the full mahr in Hanafi fiqh, regardless of intercourse or impotence.

Immediate Separation for the Majbub Husband
Ruling that a man with severed penis is separated immediately without waiting period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a majbub husband and explain why immediate separation is granted without a waiting period.

Core Idea
When a marital defect is incurable, separation is immediate—delay serves no purpose.

This lesson addresses a specific case in marriage annulment: a husband who is majbub (his penis is severed). Unlike some physical defects that may be curable and require a waiting period, the Hanafi school rules that the judge must separate the couple immediately upon the wife's request. The reasoning is straightforward: since there is no hope of cure, granting a delay would be futile.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the judge's decision to separate a married couple when the husband is a majbub. The ruling is that separation must happen immediately (hālan), without any delay.
2
Define the key term 'majbub'
The term majbub refers to a man whose penis is completely cut off, making sexual intercourse permanently impossible. This is a physical defect that is incurable.
Contrast this with 'innin (impotent man), where a one-year waiting period is granted.
3
Identify the rationale for immediacy
The passage states that giving a delay would be useless because the condition cannot be cured. This rationale is based on the legal principle that if a defect is permanent, waiting serves no benefit.
Hanafi fiqh values avoiding unnecessary hardship for the wife.
4
Apply the ruling to the judge's duty
The ruling imposes a duty on the judge (qādī) to perform the separation immediately upon the wife's request. The judge cannot postpone it.
The hukm level for the judge's action is wājib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كان مجبوبا فرق القاضى بينهما في الحال ولم يؤجله. [۱۸۳۲] (۱۰۷) اگر ذکر کٹا ہوا ہو تو قاضی تفریق کرا دے فی الحال اور اس کو مہلت نہ دے۔ ذکر کٹا ہوا ہے تو مہلت دینے سے ٹھیک نہیں ہو سکتا اس لئے مہلت دینے سے کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اس کو مہلت نہ دے اور فی الحال میاں بیوی کے درمیان تفریق کرادے۔
And if he is a majbub, the judge separates between them immediately and does not give him a delay. [1832] (107) If the penis is cut off, the judge causes separation immediately and does not give him a delay. Since the penis is cut, giving a delay cannot cure him, so there is no benefit in granting a delay. Therefore, he should not give a delay and should cause separation between the husband and wife immediately.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a straightforward ruling. It distinguishes the majbub (a man whose penis is severed) from the 'innin. Since there is no possibility of cure, the wife can seek immediate annulment from the judge without any waiting period. The commentary explains the rationale: giving time is useless because the condition is permanent. This ruling is based on the principle that when the defect is incurable, delay serves no purpose.

Key Terms
مجبوب (majbub): A man whose penis is cut off, making intercourse impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the majbub husband separated immediately without a waiting period?
A) Because he is a non-Muslim
B) Because there is no hope of cure
C) Because the wife is entitled to a divorce immediately
D) Because the judge prefers speed

Key Takeaway
A majbub husband must be separated from his wife immediately by the judge because the defect is permanent and incurable.

Ruling on the Khasii Husband's One-Year Delay
Ruling that a khasii is given a one-year delay.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a khasii husband and explain why a one-year delay is wajib before the wife can seek annulment.

Core Idea
A khasii husband is given a one-year period to seek treatment before the wife can seek annulment.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a husband is unable to consummate the marriage due to a physical defect, the wife may seek annulment. However, if the defect is potentially curable, the judge grants a delay of one year. This lesson examines the specific case of the khasii—a man whose testicles are absent but whose penis is intact. The ruling equates him with the 'innin (impotent man) because treatment may restore his ability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is granting a delay to a khasii husband. The ruling is wajib: it is obligatory to give him a one-year period before the marriage can be annulled.
This applies when the wife complains of non-consummation.
2
State the legal reason (sabab)
The reason is that the khasii's penis is intact, so there is hope that treatment can make him capable of intercourse. Thus, the law grants time for treatment.
The source explicitly says 'it can be hoped that through treatment he may become capable'.
3
Identify the condition for the delay
The condition is that the husband is a khasii (testicles absent but penis sound). The wife must also have complained of inability to consummate.
If the khasii's penis is not intact, the ruling may differ.
4
Understand the consequence if cure fails
If after one year he remains incapable, the wife may seek annulment of the marriage. This is the same as the 'innin ruling.
The source does not detail this but it is implied from the general law on defects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخصى يؤجل كما يؤجل العنين. [۱۸۳۳] (۱۰۸) اور خصی کو مہلت دی جائے گی جیسے عنین کو مہلت دی جاتی ہے۔ خصی اس کو کہتے ہیں جس کا آلہ تناسل تو ٹھیک ہو البتہ خصیہ نہ ہو۔ اگر چہ خصیہ نہیں ہے لیکن آلہ تناسل ٹھیک ہے اس لئے امید کی جاسکتی ہے کہ علاج کرانے سے محبت کے قابل ہو جائے۔ اس لئے اس کو بھی ایسے ہی ایک سال کی مہلت ملے گی جیسے عنین کو ملتی ہے۔
And the khasii is given a delay just as the 'innin is given a delay. [1833] (108) And the khasii will be given a delay just as the 'innin is given a delay. The khasii is one whose reproductive organ is intact but he has no testicles. Even though he has no testicles, his penis is sound, so it can be hoped that through treatment he may become capable of intercourse. Therefore, he too will be given a one-year delay like the 'innin receives.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage defines the khasii (a man missing testicles but with intact penis) and equates his ruling with that of the 'innin (impotent man). Since there is hope of cure through medical treatment, the wife cannot demand immediate separation. Instead, the judge grants a one-year period. If after a year he remains incapable, the wife may seek annulment. This is based on the principle that curable defects require a waiting period to allow treatment.

Key Terms
خصی (khasii): A man whose testicles are removed or absent, but whose penis is intact and potentially functional.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because he is a minor
B) Because his condition may be curable
C) Because the judge is busy
D) Because the wife must give consent

Key Takeaway
A khasii husband is given a one-year delay before annulment because cure is possible.

Nikah — Marriage

Separation When Wife Converts and Husband Refuses Islam
Ruling with evidence on separation after wife's conversion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the separation when a wife converts and her husband refuses Islam, explain the proofs (Quran, hadith, and athar), distinguish the intra-Hanafi views of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, and compare the Hanafi position with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Upon wife's conversion, the judge presents Islam; if the husband refuses, separation is immediate and is talaq ba'in.

This passage deals with a common scenario in lands where Muslims are a minority: a married woman embraces Islam while her husband remains a non-Muslim. The classical Hanafi ruling is that the judge must give the husband a chance to convert; if he refuses, the marriage is ended. However, the jurists differ on the exact nature of that separation—is it a divorce or an annulment? And how long should the husband be given? Let's explore the evidence and the debates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the event
A married woman converts to Islam while her husband is still a kafir (non-Muslim). The judge becomes involved. The question is: what happens to the marriage?
This is not a case of both converting together; only one spouse converts.
2
State the Hanafi ruling and procedure
The judge must present (display/offer) Islam to the husband. If he converts, the marriage continues. If he refuses, the judge must separate them. The separation is immediate, not delayed.
The procedure is wajib (obligatory) on the judge.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the nature of separation
Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani say the separation is talaq ba'in (irrevocable divorce). Imam Abu Yusuf says it is a mere separation (firqah) without the effect of talaq.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is talaq ba'in.
4
Examine the dalil (evidence) cited
The passage uses: (1) Quran 2:221 and 60:10 — prohibition of Muslim marrying polytheist; (2) Hadith of Abu al-As — the Prophet (s) remarried his daughter Zaynab to him with a new contract after he accepted Islam; (3) Athar of Umar — he separated a woman from her husband after the husband refused Islam.
Each proof supports that the marriage cannot persist after one spouse's conversion if the other remains kafir.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i says the husband is given a waiting period of three menstrual cycles to convert; only then is separation ordered. The Hanafi school does not grant this delay because the marriage becomes invalid immediately from the Quranic prohibition.
The practical difference: under Hanafi, the woman can marry another Muslim after iddah immediately; under Shafi'i, she must wait three cycles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا اسلمت المرأة وزوجها كافر عرض عليه القاضي الاسلام فان اسلم فهى امرأته والا فرق بينهما. [۱۸۳۴] (۱۰۹) اگر عورت اسلام لائی اور اس کا شوہر کافر ہے تو قاضی اس پر اسلام پیش کرے، پس اگر اسلام لے آئے تو عورت اس کی بیوی رہے گی۔ اور اگر اسلام سے انکار کر دیا تو دونوں کے درمیان تفریق کر دی جائے يؤمنوا (الف) (آیت ۲۲۱ سورة البقرة ٢) اس آیت میں ہے کہ مشرک یا مشرکہ مسلمان کے لئے حلال نہیں ہے۔ دوسری آیت میں ہے لا مـن حـل لهـم ولاهـم يـحـلـون لهن ( آیت ۱۰ سورة المتحیه (۶۰) اس آیت میں بھی ہے کہ مشرکہ حلال نہیں ہیں (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت ابو العاص بعد میں ایمان لائے تو نکاح جدید کے ذریعہ حضرت زینب کو ان کے حوالے کیا گیا۔ عن عمر بن شعيب عن ابيه عن جده ان رسول الله رد ابنته صلى الله على ابي العاص بن الربيع بمهر جديد ونكاح جدید (ب) (ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء في الزوجين المشركين يسلم احدهماص ۲۱۷ نمبر ۱۱۴۲) اور اسلام پیش کرے پس شوہر انکار کرے تو اس انکار کو تفریق کا سبب اس لئے بنائے کہ اسلام ۱۱۰، نمبر ۷ ۱۸۲۹) اس اثر میں شوہر پر اسلام پیش کیا اور اس کے انکار کے بعد حضرت عمر نے تفریق کی۔ ایک اور اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابن شهاب انه قال يعرض عليه الاسلام فان اسلم فهى امرأته والا فرق بينهما الاسلام (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب النصرانيين تسلم المرأة قبل الرجل ج سابع ص ۷۴ انمبر ۱۲۶۵۷) امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ تین حیض گزرنے تک شوہر کے اسلام لانے کا انتظار کیا جائے گا ۔ اور تین حیض گزر جائے تو تفریق ہو جائیگی۔
And if the woman converts to Islam and her husband is a kafir, the judge presents Islam to him; if he converts, she remains his wife; otherwise, he separates them. [1834] (109) If a woman comes to Islam and her husband is a kafir, the judge presents Islam to him. If he accepts Islam, then the woman remains his wife. If he refuses Islam, then separation is made between them. This separation will be a talaq ba'in according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad. And Imam Abu Yusuf said that this separation is without talaq. The woman converted and the husband is kafir, so the judge presents Islam to the husband. If he accepts Islam, she remains his wife. If he refuses, the judge separates them. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), this separation is in the category of talaq ba'in. According to Abu Yusuf, it is in the category of separation and conciliation (firqat wa sulh). The reason for presenting Islam to the husband is that the marriage of a Muslim to a kafir is not permissible. The verse says: 'Do not marry polytheist women until they believe; and a believing slave woman is better than a polytheist woman, even if she pleases you. And do not marry polytheist men until they believe.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:221). This verse states that a polytheist man or woman is not lawful for a Muslim. Another verse: 'They are not lawful for them, nor are they lawful for them' (Surah al-Mumtahanah 60:10). Also in this verse, polytheist women are not lawful. (2) The hadith: That Abu al-As later accepted Islam, and the Prophet returned his daughter Zaynab to him with a new mahr and new marriage. (Tirmidhi, Kitab al-Nikah, no. 1142). And he presents Islam; if the husband refuses, that refusal is made a cause for separation because accepting Islam is a blessing. It is not good for the husband to lose this blessing due to his refusal, so his refusal is made a cause for separation. (2) There is evidence in the athar: That a man from Banu Tha'labah called 'Abbad ibn al-Nu'man had a wife from Banu Tamim. She converted, so Umar called him and said: 'Either you accept Islam or I will take her away from you.' He refused to accept Islam, so Umar took her away from him. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 18297). In this athar, Islam was presented to the husband, and after his refusal, Umar separated them. Another athar: From Ibn Shihab, he said: 'Islam is presented to him; if he accepts, she is his wife; otherwise, separation is made between them.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, no. 12657). Imam al-Shafi'i says that three menstrual cycles will be waited for the husband to accept Islam; after three cycles, separation occurs.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute. It addresses the scenario where a married woman converts to Islam while her husband remains a non-Muslim. The Hanafi ruling is that the judge must present Islam to the husband. If he converts, the marriage continues; if he refuses, the judge separates them. According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, this separation is a talaq ba'in (irrevocable divorce). Imam Abu Yusuf, however, considers it a mere separation (firqah) without the effect of talaq. The textual evidence includes: (1) Quran 2:221 and 60:10, which prohibit marriage between Muslims and polytheists. (2) The hadith of Abu al-As, where the Prophet re-married his daughter Zaynab to him with a new contract, indicating that the previous marriage did not automatically continue after conversion. (3) The practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab, as reported in the athar, where he separated a woman from her husband after the husband refused Islam. The passage also mentions the Shafi'i position, which grants a three-month waiting period (three menstrual cycles) for the husband to convert before separation. The Hanafi position does not give such a delay because the marriage becomes immediately invalid due to the verse's prohibition, and presenting Islam is a courtesy. The dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf revolves around the nature of the separation: whether it is a form of talaq or a judicial annulment.

Key Terms
تفریق (tafriq): Judicial separation decreed by the judge in case of irreconcilable difference or legal impediment.
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately; the husband cannot take back the wife without a new marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what is the legal nature of the separation when a husband refuses Islam after his wife's conversion?
A) Talaq ba'in (irrevocable divorce)
B) Talaq raj'i (revocable divorce)
C) Faskh (annulment) only
D) Khul' (divorce by redemption)

Key Takeaway
When a married woman converts to Islam and her husband refuses to convert, the Hanafi school mandates immediate judicial separation as talaq ba'in, based on Quranic prohibition, prophetic practice, and the precedent of Umar.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
10 min
Separation When Wife Converts: Bainunah Talaq or Mere Dissolution?
Ruling on wife's conversion to Islam before husband

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a wife converts and the husband refuses Islam, distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Separation due to husband's refusal is a bainunah talaq for Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but only a dissolution for Abu Yusuf.

When a married woman accepts Islam and her husband remains a non-Muslim, Islamic law requires the qadi to invite the husband to convert. If he refuses, the marriage is dissolved. But what kind of dissolution is it? This lesson explores a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: is it a full, irrevocable divorce (talaq bain) or simply a judicial separation that does not count toward the three divorces? The difference has profound implications for future remarriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering event
The wife converts to Islam while the husband remains a non-Muslim (whether original disbeliever or apostate). The qadi must present Islam to the husband.
This presentation is wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school.
2
Note the two possible outcomes
If the husband accepts Islam, the marriage continues. If he refuses, the qadi orders separation. The dispute is about the legal nature of this separation.
3
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
They rule that the separation constitutes one bainunah talaq (irrevocable divorce). This means it counts as a divorce and the couple cannot remarry without a halal (intervening marriage with consummation).
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position.
4
State the position of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf holds that it is a judicial dissolution (firqa) without talaq. It does not count towards the three divorces, so the couple could remarry with a new contract without needing tahlil.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
5
Analyze the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical fruit of the difference) is whether the separation reduces the number of available divorces. Under the majority view, if the husband later remarries the woman and divorces her again, he would have used two divorces. Under Abu Yusuf's view, it is as if no divorce occurred.
This affects the couple's ability to reunite.

13 (109) When a woman becomes Muslim and her husband is a disbeliever, the qadi presents Islam to him. If he becomes Muslim, she remains his wife. If he refuses Islam, they are separated. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, this separation is a bainunah talaq (irrevocable divorce). According to Abu Yusuf, it is a separation without talaq. (Urdu commentary follows with proofs and discussion).
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where a married woman converts to Islam while her husband remains a non-Muslim. The ruling is that the qadi must call upon the husband to accept Islam. If he does, the marriage continues. If he refuses, the qadi separates them. The key intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rule that this separation constitutes a bainunah (irrevocable) talaq, meaning it counts as a single, irrevocable divorce. Abu Yusuf, however, holds that it is merely a dissolution (firqa) without the effect of a talaq, so it does not count towards the three divorces. The passage then provides proofs: Quranic verses prohibiting Muslim marriage to polytheists (2:221, 60:10), hadith about the Prophet returning his daughter Zaynab to Abu al-As with a new marriage (implying the first marriage ended), and athar from Umar and others. It also mentions that Imam al-Shafi'i would wait for three menstrual cycles for the husband to convert before separation. The commentary concludes by arguing that since the separation is due to the husband's refusal, it is attributed to his action, and thus takes the ruling of a talaq. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, making it a bainunah talaq.

Key Terms
طلاق بائن (talaq bain): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately and prevents remarriage without a new contract and intervening marriage (tahlil).
فرقة (firqa): Separation or dissolution of a marriage, not necessarily a divorce.
عرض عليه الإسلام (arda alayhi al-islam): The qadi offers Islam to the non-Muslim husband, giving him a chance to convert before any separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, what is the effect of the separation ordered by the qadi when a wife converts to Islam and her husband refuses to convert?
A) It is a bainunah talaq (irrevocable divorce).
B) It is a separation without talaq.
C) The marriage remains valid until the end of the iddah.
D) The wife must return the mahr.

Key Takeaway
The separation when a wife converts and the husband refuses Islam is a bainunah talaq according to the mufta bihi of the Hanafi school, counting as one of the three divorces.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Proof for Continuation of Marriage During Iddah After Conversion
Hadith and athar proving marriage remains valid if husband converts within iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the status of marriage when one spouse converts to Islam during the iddah period, and identify the dalil that supports this ruling.

Core Idea
If a spouse converts during the iddah, the marriage remains valid; refusal results in ba'in talaq.

When a non-Muslim couple embraces Islam, the marriage does not automatically nullify. Instead, the iddah period serves as a window for the other spouse to accept Islam. This lesson examines the Hanafi position through key hadith and athar that affirm the continuity of marriage during this transitional period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Determine the Hanafi position on the marital status when one spouse converts to Islam. According to Abu Hanifa, if the wife converts, the marriage remains intact. If the husband refuses Islam, the judge separates them, and this separation is a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce.
The ruling applies only if the marriage was consummated and the iddah has not expired.
2
Locate the Dalil
The author cites two main proofs: the hadith of 'Ikrimah and Safwan's wives (from al-Bayhaqi and al-Bukhari) and the hadith of Zaynab (from Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi). Identify these sources and note their transmission status.
Both are ahad hadith, thus zanni al-thubut.
3
Extract the Wajh al-Dalalah
Analyze how the hadith prove the ruling. In the story of 'Ikrimah and Safwan, the husbands were disbelievers for a period after their wives' conversion, yet the Prophet confirmed the marriage when they later converted within the iddah. This shows that marriage does not dissolve automatically; the iddah is a waiting period.
The same lesson is derived from the case of Zaynab, who was returned to Abu al-'As after his conversion during her iddah.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf considered the separation upon refusal to be faskh (annulment) rather than talaq. However, the relied position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that it is a ba'in talaq (Imam Muhammad agreed with Abu Hanifa).
This ikhtilaf is fully discussed in the next lesson.
5
Understand the Mufta Bihi
The operative ruling for fatwa today is that if the husband refuses Islam during the iddah, the marriage ends with a single ba'in talaq. This is based on Abu Hanifa's view, preferred by Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah.
The cross-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i school, which holds immediate dissolution, is resolved in favor of the Hanafi view due to stronger dalil.

كتاب النكاح اسلم فهي امرأته وان ابى عن الاسلام فرق بينهما وكان ذلك طلاقا بائنا عند ابي حنيفة حديث فيه أن عكرمة بن أبي جهل وصفوان بن أمية زوجتاهما أسلما وهرب زوجاهما ناحية اليمن من طريق اليمن كافرين إلى بلد كفر ثم جائا فأسلموا بعد مدة وشهد صفوان حنينا كافرا فدخل دار الإسلام بعد هربه منها كافرا فاستقر على النكاح وكان ذلك كله ونساؤهم مدخول بهن لم تنقض عدتهن (أ) (سنن البيهقي، باب من قال لا ينفسخ النكاح بينهما بإسلام أحدهما إذا كانت مدخولا بها حتى تنقضي عدتها قبل إسلام المتخلف منهاج سابع، ص 1301 نمبر 14062/ بخاری شریف، باب إذا أسلمت المشركة أو النصرانية تحت الذمي أو الحربي ص 796 نمبر 5288) هذا الحديث فيه دليل أن عدتهن لم تنقض قبل إسلام الزوجين فبقي النكاح. (ب) وروي عن ابن عباس قال: رد رسول الله زينب على أبي العاص بالنكاح الأول لم يحدث شيئا. (أبو داود شریف، باب إلى متى ترو عليه امرأته إذا أسلم بعدها ص 1311 نمبر 2240 / ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء في الزوجين المشركين يسلم أحدهماص 217 نمبر 143 / سنن البيهقي، باب من قال لا ينفسخ النكاح بينهما بإسلام أحدهما ج سابع ص 303 نمبر 14067) وفي هذا الحديث: أن زينب ردت إلى أبي العاص بالنكاح الأول، وكانت في العدة. وعن الحسن قال: إذا كان الرجل وامرأته مشركين فأسلمت وأبى أن يسلم بانت منه بواحدة وقال عكرمة مثل ذلك. ورواية أخرى: أن الحسن وعمر بن عبد العزيز قالا: تطليقة بائنة. (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة 85 من قال إذا أبى أن يسلم فهي تطليقة ج رابع ص 110 نمبر 18308/18309) وفي هذا الأثر: التفريق طلاق بائن.
Book of Marriage: If she accepts Islam, she is his wife. If he refuses Islam, separation occurs between them, and that is a ba'in divorce according to Abu Hanifa. A hadith that the wives of 'Ikrimah ibn Abi Jahl and Safwan ibn Umayyah accepted Islam, and their husbands fled towards Yemen as disbelievers to a land of disbelief, then they came and accepted Islam after a period, and Safwan attended Hunayn as a disbeliever, then entered Dar al-Islam after fleeing from it as a disbeliever, so the marriage was confirmed, and all that happened while their wives had been consummated with and their 'iddah had not expired. This hadith indicates that their 'iddah did not expire before the husbands' Islam, so the marriage remained. And it is narrated from Ibn 'Abbas: The Messenger of Allah returned Zaynab to Abu al-'As with the first marriage, having not done anything new. In this hadith, Zaynab was returned to Abu al-'As with the first marriage, and she was in 'iddah. And from al-Hasan: If a man and his wife are polytheists, then she accepts Islam and he refuses to accept Islam, she becomes separated from him by one (divorce), and 'Ikrimah said the same. Another narration: al-Hasan and 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz said: one ba'in divorce. In this athar, the separation is a ba'in divorce.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the hadith and athar. The ruling states that if a wife becomes Muslim, the marriage remains, but if the husband refuses Islam, the judge separates them, and this separation is a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The proof is from the hadith of 'Ikrimah and Safwan's wives, where the husbands remained disbelievers for a while but later converted before the wives' 'iddah expired, and the Prophet confirmed the marriage. This shows that the marriage is not immediately dissolved; the 'iddah period is a window for the other spouse to embrace Islam. The same is derived from the hadith of Zaynab, the Prophet's daughter, who was returned to her husband Abu al-'As after his conversion during her 'iddah. The athar of Hasan al-Basri and 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz further support that the separation after refusal is a single ba'in divorce.

Key Terms
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately; the husband cannot take back his wife without a new marriage contract and her consent.
عدة (iddah): The waiting period after marriage dissolution during which a woman cannot remarry, to confirm she is not pregnant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of 'Ikrimah and Safwan, what happened after their wives converted and the husbands later converted within the iddah?
A) The marriages were annulled.
B) The wives were returned to their husbands upon conversion within iddah.
C) The husbands were executed.
D) The marriages continued only after a new contract.

Key Takeaway
The iddah period after one spouse's conversion is a window for the other to accept Islam; if they do, marriage continues; if they refuse, separation is a ba'in divorce.

Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: Separation is Faskh, Not Talaq
Intra-Hanafi dispute: Sahibayn argue faskh instead of talaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the reasoning of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani for considering the separation after a wife's conversion as faskh and contrast it with Abu Hanifa's view that it is a ba'in talaq.

Core Idea
When both spouses contribute to the separation, it is an annulment, not a divorce.

In the previous lesson, we learned that Abu Hanifa considered the separation after a wife's conversion as a ba'in talaq. However, his two main students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagreed. In this passage, they argue that since both spouses are involved in the separation, it cannot be a divorce pronounced by the husband alone; rather, it is an annulment of the marriage contract (faskh). We will examine their evidence from the athar of Hasan al-Basri and 'Ata' and explore the practical difference between talaq and faskh.

Guided Path
1
Restate the dominant Hanafi position
Begin by recalling Abu Hanifa's view that the separation after a wife's conversion is a ba'in talaq. This is the mufta bihi position of the school.
2
Identify the dissenting view of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that it is a faskh (annulment), not a talaq. Their key argument: the separation arises from both spouses (the wife by converting, the husband by refusing), so it is not a unilateral act of the husband.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; both are major authorities.
3
Examine the evidence (athar) for the Sahibayn view
They cite the athar of Hasan al-Basri: 'When a woman accepts Islam before her husband, what is between them of marriage is severed.' Also the athar of 'Ata: 'They are separated.' These statements use terms like 'inqaṭa'a' and 'yufarraqu', not 'talaq', supporting annulment.
The Sahibayn argue that these athar explicitly indicate dissolution without divorce.
4
Analyze the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If deemed talaq, the husband has used one divorce and has two remaining; the wife observes iddah of talaq; they could remarry with a new mahr. If faskh, the marriage is void ab initio, no divorce counts are consumed; if the husband later converts, a new marriage contract is required.
The number of remaining divorces and the need for a new contract differ.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and the school's response
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view that it is a ba'in talaq. The text does not provide a direct rebuttal to the Sahibayn, but the school's preference for Abu Hanifa is established in later works.
This shows that even within a school, there can be valid differences; the mufta bihi is settled by majority and later tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و محمد رحمهما الله وقال ابو يوسف رحمه الله هو الفرقة بغير طلاق[۱۸۳۵](۱۱۰) امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ اس تفریق میں میاں بیوی دونوں شریک ہیں اس لئے یہ طلاق نہیں ہوگی بلکہ فسخ نکاح ہوگا (۱) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن الحسن قال اذا اسلمت المرأة قبل زوجها انقطع ما بينهما من النكاح (الف) دوسری راویت ہے۔ عن عطاء في النصرانية تسلم تحت زوجها قال يفرق بينهم المصنف ابن ابى هيبته ما قالوافي المرأة تسلم قبل زوجها من قال يفرق بينهما ج رابع ص ۱۰۹، نمبر ۱۸۲۹۳/۱۸۲۹۶) ان اثروں میں يفرق بينهما اور انقطع ما بينهما ہیں۔ جن سے پتہ چلا کہ دونوں کے درمیان تفریق ہوگی طلاق نہیں ہوگی۔
And Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them both) and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) said: it is separation without divorce. (110) Imam Abu Yusuf says: in this separation, both spouses are partners, so it will not be a divorce but rather an annulment of marriage. Proof of this is in the athar: from al-Hasan: 'If the woman accepts Islam before her husband, what is between them of marriage is severed.' Another narration: from 'Ata regarding a Christian woman who accepts Islam under her husband, he said: 'They separate them.' These athar indicate that separation occurs between them, not a divorce.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. After stating Abu Hanifa's view that separation is a ba'in talaq, the text records that Muhammad al-Shaybani and Abu Yusuf disagree. Abu Yusuf argues that since both spouses are involved in the separation (the wife by converting, the husband by refusing), it cannot be considered a divorce from the husband alone. Instead, it is a faskh (annulment) of the marriage contract. He supports this with the athar of Hasan al-Basri, who said the marriage is 'cut off' (inqaṭa'a), and the athar of 'Ata, who said they are separated (yufarraqu baynahum). These terms do not use 'talaq' but rather 'faskh' or 'firqah', indicating an annulment rather than a revocable divorce. The practical implication is that in a faskh, the husband does not have the right to take back his wife during iddah (as in revocable divorce), and the waiting period is for iddah of faskh, not talaq.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of the marriage contract; it cancels the marriage from its inception or from the time of faskh, without the need for divorce.
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately; the husband cannot take back his wife during iddah without a new marriage contract.
اخْتِلَاف (ikhtilaf): Difference of opinion among scholars, especially within a madhhab, based on valid evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf's view, why is the separation after a wife's conversion not considered a talaq?
A) Because the husband has no choice in the matter.
B) Because both spouses are partners in the separation, so it is a faskh.
C) Because the wife initiated the separation.
D) Because the Prophet never called it talaq.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the separation after a wife's conversion is considered a ba'in talaq according to the relied-upon position, but the Sahibayn argued it is a faskh, highlighting a nuanced intra-school debate.

Ruling on a husband who converts with a Magian wife
Ruling on conversion of husband with Magian wife, and mahr consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a husband converts and his Magian wife refuses Islam, and explain the mahr consequence based on consummation.

Core Idea
If a Magian wife refuses Islam after husband converts, separation is faskh, not talaq, and mahr depends on consummation.

This lesson examines a specific scenario within interfaith marriage: a husband accepts Islam while his wife remains Magian. The Hanafi school provides detailed rules for the invitation to Islam, the nature of the separation, and the financial consequences. Understanding this ruling clarifies how the school balances continuity of marriage with religious obligations.

Guided Path
1
State the core ruling
Identify the two possible outcomes based on the wife's response: if she accepts Islam, marriage continues; if she refuses, the judge separates them. Note that the separation is not a divorce (talaq) but a dissolution (faskh).
2
Understand the prerequisite invitation
The husband must first invite his wife to Islam. This is a condition before any separation occurs. If she accepts, no separation needed.
3
Distinguish faskh from talaq
The separation is faskh, not talaq. This means it does not count toward the three talaq limit and does not require pronouncement. It is an annulment by the qadi.
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold this view; Abu Hanifa may have considered it talaq, but the relied-upon position follows the Sahibayn.
4
Apply the mahr rule
If the marriage was consummated, she receives the full mahr. If not consummated, she receives nothing. This is derived from the athar of al-Thawri regarding apostasy.
The mahr is a debt once consummated.
5
Recognize the proof and its application
The ruling is supported by the athar of Sufyan al-Thawri about a woman who apostatizes. The same rule applies to the Magian wife who refuses Islam, as the cause (refusal of Islam) is analogous.
The athar is from Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۸۳۵](۱۱۰) وان اسلم الزوج وتحته مجوسية عرض عليها الاسلام فإن اسلمت فهى امرأته وان ابت فرق القاضي بينهما ولم تكن الفرقة طلاقا [ ١٨٣٦ (١١١) فان كان قد دخل بها فلها كمال المهر وان لم يكن دخل بها فلا مهر لها (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔عن الثورى قال اذا ارتدت المرأة ولها زوج ولم يدخل بها فلا صداق لها وقد انقطع ما بينهما فان كان قد دخل بها فلها الصداق كاملا (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب امرتدین ج سابع ص ۶۱ نمبر ۱۲۶۱۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ محبت نہ کی ہوتو کچھ نہیں ملے گا اور صحبت کی ہو تو پورا مہر ملے گا۔
(110) And if the husband accepts Islam and under him is a Magian woman, he presents Islam to her. If she accepts Islam, she is his wife. If she refuses, the judge separates them, and the separation is not a divorce. (111) If he had consummated with her, she has the full mahr; if he had not consummated, she has no mahr. Proof is in the athar: from al-Thawri: 'If a woman apostatizes while married, and he has not consummated, she has no mahr and what is between them is severed. If he had consummated, she has the full mahr.'
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage provides a specific ruling for the case where a husband converts to Islam and his wife is a Magian (fire-worshiper). The husband must invite her to Islam. If she accepts, the marriage remains. If she refuses, the qadi separates them, and importantly, this separation is not a divorce (talaq) but a dissolution (faskh). This is consistent with the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad that such separations are not talaq. The passage then addresses the mahr: if the marriage was consummated, she is entitled to the full mahr as specified in the contract; if not, she gets nothing. The proof is the athar of Sufyan al-Thawri regarding the female apostate: if the husband had consummated, full mahr; if not, no mahr. The reasoning is that the separation is caused by the wife's refusal (or apostasy), so she is not entitled to anything if un-consummated, but if consummated, the mahr is settled as a debt.

Key Terms
مجوسية (majusiyyah): A Zoroastrian (fire-worshiper) woman; Magians are considered People of the Book in some aspects but with different marriage rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Half the mahr.
B) Full mahr.
C) No mahr.
D) Mahr al-mithl.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a husband converts and his Magian wife refuses Islam, the judge dissolves the marriage as faskh (not talaq), and the wife's mahr depends on whether consummation occurred.

Conversion in Dar al-Harb: Delayed Separation
Ruling on conversion of a woman in enemy territory; separation occurs after three menstrual cycles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of separation when a woman converts to Islam in dar al-harb and distinguish it from the immediate separation in dar al-Islam.

Core Idea
A woman's conversion in enemy territory does not immediately end the marriage; separation occurs after three menstrual cycles.

This passage addresses a specific scenario: a woman converts to Islam while residing in dar al-harb (enemy territory) while her husband remains a non-Muslim. Unlike the immediate dissolution in dar al-Islam, the Hanafi school grants a waiting period of three menstrual cycles to allow for the husband's conversion or the wife's immigration. Understanding this distinction is essential for comprehending how Islamic law accommodates practical constraints in hostile lands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Locate the two key conditions: (1) the woman accepts Islam, and (2) this occurs in dar al-harb (enemy territory) while the husband remains a disbeliever.
The location matters—this ruling is specific to dar al-harb.
2
State the Effect on the Marriage
The marriage is not immediately dissolved. The text explicitly says 'la taqa' al-furqah' (separation does not occur) until a period passes.
This contradicts the usual rule in dar al-Islam where conversion of either spouse immediately ends the marriage.
3
Identify the Duration
The waiting period is three menstrual cycles (thalaathat hayd). After they pass, the woman becomes ba'in (irrevocably separated).
The term 'hayd' here refers to complete menstrual periods, not partial ones.
4
Understand the Rationale
The delay serves a practical purpose: it gives the husband time to also convert, and it allows the wife to possibly emigrate to Muslim territory without being in a state of suspension.
This demonstrates the Hanafi principle of flexibility (taysir) in difficult circumstances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۸۳۷) (۱۱۲) اذا اسلمت المرأة في دار الحرب لا تقع الفرقة حتى تمضي ثلاثة حيض. فإذا مضت ثلاثة حيض تبين منه.
(112) If a woman accepts Islam in dar al-harb, the separation does not occur until three menstrual cycles pass. When three menstrual cycles pass, she becomes ba'in (separated) from him.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage states a ruling for a woman who converts to Islam while in enemy territory (dar al-harb), and her husband remains a disbeliever. Unlike the case where conversion happens in dar al-Islam, here the marriage is not immediately dissolved. Instead, it remains valid for the duration of the 'iddah (three hayds). This is because the husband may also convert, or she might be unable to immigrate. After three menstrual periods, the separation becomes effective, and she becomes ba'in (irrevocably separated). This ruling gives time for the husband to consider Islam or for the wife to reach Muslim lands. The mahr aspects are not mentioned here but follow similar rules: if consummated, full mahr; if not, possibly half or none? The text is concise.

Key Terms
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim control where Islamic law is not implemented.
حيض (hayd): Menstrual cycle; used as a unit of time in iddah and similar contexts.
بائن (ba'in): Irrevocably separated; the marriage cannot be renewed without a new contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) After three menstrual cycles.
D) After one year.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a woman's conversion in dar al-harb does not immediately dissolve the marriage; separation occurs after three menstrual cycles.

Nature of Separation After Wife's Conversion: Faskh vs Talaq
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether separation is divorce or annulment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between faskh (annulment) and talaq (divorce) in the context of marital dissolution after the wife's conversion to Islam, and state the Hanafi position with its evidence.

Core Idea
Separation due to wife's conversion is faskh, not talaq — the husband's right to divorce is not implicated.

When a married woman embraces Islam before her husband, what is the nature of the resulting separation? Is it a divorce (talaq), which is the husband's prerogative, or an annulment (faskh) that dissolves the marriage by operation of law? This passage from the Hanafi tradition presents the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani that it is faskh, supported by statements of early authorities. Understanding this distinction is crucial because faskh and talaq have different consequences for 'iddah, revocability, and future remarriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The case is: a woman converts to Islam before her husband does. The marriage is still valid at the moment of her conversion, but a legal separation occurs.
The husband has not divorced her; the separation is triggered by the difference in religion.
2
State the two views
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold it is faskh (annulment), not talaq. Some early authorities (al-Hasan, Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz) said it is one talaq ba'in. Identify which view is the relied-upon Hanafi position.
The Hanafi position is the former; the latter is a minority view within the school.
3
Analyze the evidence (athar)
Examine the athar cited: from al-Hasan, 'the marriage between them is severed' (inqata'a). From Ata, 'they are separated' (yufarraq). Note that the language used is 'separation' not 'divorce.'
The choice of words supports the faskh view.
4
Understand the Hanafi reasoning
Abu Yusuf reasoned that both spouses share in the cause of separation, so it cannot be talaq, which is solely the husband's act. Therefore, it must be faskh.
Talaq requires a deliberate pronouncement by the husband; here, the separation occurs by operation of law.
5
Note the practical consequences
Faskh does not count toward the three permissible divorces, and the 'iddah may differ from that after talaq. Also, the couple can remarry with a new contract if the husband later converts.
If it were talaq ba'in, remarriage would require a fresh contract and the woman would need to observe 'iddah as for talaq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و محمد رحمهما الله وقال ابو يوسف رحمه الله هو الفرقة بغير طلاق امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ اس تفریق میں میاں بیوی دونوں شریک ہیں اس لئے یہ طلاق نہیں ہوگی بلکہ فسخ نکاح ہوگا (۱) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن الحسن قال اذا اسلمت المرأة قبل زوجها انقطع ما بينهما من النكاح (الف) دوسری راویت ہے۔ عن عطاء في النصرانية تسلم تحت زوجها قال يفرق بينهم المصنف ابن ابى هيبته ما قالوافي المرأة تسلم قبل زوجها من قال يفرق بينهما ج رابع ص ۱۰۹، نمبر ۱۸۲۹۳/۱۸۲۹۶) ان اثروں میں يفرق بينهما اور انقطع ما بينهما ہیں۔ جن سے پتہ چلا کہ دونوں کے درمیان تفریق ہوگی طلاق نہیں ہوگی۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت حسن اور عمر بن عبد العزیز نے فرمایا ایک طلاق بائنہ ہوگی (1) حضرت حسن نے فرمایا اگر عورت شوہر سے پہلے مسلمان ہوئی تو دونوں کے درمیان کا نکاح ٹوٹ جائے گا
And Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them both) and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) said: It is separation without divorce. Imam Abu Yusuf says that in this separation, both husband and wife are partners, so it will not be divorce, rather it will be annulment of marriage (faskh). (1) There is evidence for this in the athar: from al-Hasan, he said: When a woman embraces Islam before her husband, what is between them of marriage is severed. (Another narration:) from Ata regarding a Christian woman who embraces Islam while under her husband, he said: They are separated. Al-Musannif Ibn Abi Haybah says what they said about a woman who embraces Islam before her husband: those who said they are separated, volume 4, page 109, numbers 18293/18296. In these athar are 'they are separated' and 'what is between them is severed', which shows that there will be separation between them, not divorce. Margin note (a): al-Hasan and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz said: one irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in). (1) al-Hasan said: If a woman becomes Muslim before her husband, the marriage between them is broken.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal nature of the separation that occurs when a woman embraces Islam before her husband. The author quotes Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) as stating that this separation is not a divorce but rather a dissolution (faskh) of the marriage. The commentary explains that Abu Yusuf reasoned that both spouses share in the cause of separation, so it cannot be divorce, which is exclusively the husband's prerogative. The text then provides evidential support (athar) from Hasan al-Basri and Ata ibn Abi Rabah, using the terms 'severed' (inqita') and 'separated' (tafriq) to argue that the separation is not a talaq. The margin note (a) records a dissenting view from Hasan and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, who considered it one irrevocable divorce, indicating this was not universally agreed upon. The Hanafi position, however, as held by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, is that it is faskh, not talaq.

Key Terms
الفرقة (al-furqa): Separation between husband and wife, here specifically the legal dissolution of marriage.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of marriage, a dissolution that is not a divorce, often due to a legal impediment that arises after the contract.
طلاق (talaq): Divorce initiated by the husband or his delegate, a specific legal act with well-defined rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when a woman converts to Islam before her husband, what is the nature of the separation according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?
A) It is a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i)
B) It is an irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in)
C) It is an annulment (faskh), not a divorce
D) It is not a separation; the marriage continues

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that when a wife converts to Islam before her husband, the marriage dissolves by faskh (annulment), not talaq, supported by athar and the principle that talaq is exclusively the husband's act.
