intermediate
6 min
Husband Converts, Wife Zoroastrian: Faskh not Talaq
Ruling on presenting Islam and separation as faskh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a husband converts to Islam with a Zoroastrian wife, explain the requirement to present Islam, and apply the distinction between faskh and talaq.

Core Idea
The wife's refusal of Islam triggers a court-ordered separation (faskh), not a divorce (talaq).

When a husband embraces Islam but his wife remains a Zoroastrian, the marriage is not automatically dissolved. Instead, Hanafi law requires the husband to present Islam to her. If she accepts, the marriage continues; if she refuses, the judge separates them. This separation is legally distinct from talaq, with important consequences for future reconciliation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering event
The husband converts to Islam while his wife is a Zoroastrian. Note that the marriage itself becomes irregular (but not void) at the moment of his conversion, pending the wife's response.
The Zoroastrian wife is considered a polytheist, so the marriage is not valid from the Hanafi perspective; but it is not instantly nullified.
2
Recognize the obligation to present Islam
The husband must present Islam to his wife. This is a legal duty (wajib) before any final separation can occur.
Presentation gives the wife a chance to embrace Islam and preserve the marriage.
3
Determine the outcome based on her response
If she accepts Islam, the marriage remains valid (she is his wife). If she refuses, the qadi separates them.
The separation is not a divorce (talaq) because it originates from the wife's refusal, not the husband's pronouncement.
4
Distinguish faskh from talaq
A divorce (talaq) is the husband's right to revocably dissolve the marriage. A separation (faskh) due to the wife's refusal is an annulment that does not count as one of the three divorces and does not allow the husband to take her back without a new nikah.
This distinction affects the possibility of remarriage and the waiting period requirements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان اسلم الزوج وتحته مجوسية عرض عليها الاسلام فإن اسلمت فهى امرأته وان ابت فرق القاضي بينهما ولم تكن الفرقة طلاقا اگر شوہر اسلام لے آیا اور اس کے نکاح میں آتش پرست ہو تو اس پر اسلام پیش کرے۔ پس اگر اسلام لے آئے تو وہ اس کی بیوی رہے گی۔ اور اگر انکار کر دے تو قاضی دونوں کے درمیان تفریق کرا دے۔ اور یہ فرقت طلاق نہیں ہوگی۔ اسلام پیش کرنے کا اثر پہلے گزر گیا۔ اور یہ فرقت طلاق اس لئے نہیں ہوگی کہ عورت کی جانب سے انکار کرنے پر فرقت ہوتی ہے۔ اور عورت کی جانب سے طلاق نہیں ہوتی اس کی جانب سے فرقت ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے یہ تمام کے نزدیک فرقت شمار ہوگی۔
And if the husband embraces Islam and under him is a Zoroastrian woman, then Islam is presented to her. If she embraces Islam, then she is his wife. If she refuses, the judge separates them, and the separation is not a divorce. If the husband becomes a Muslim and under his marriage is a fire-worshipper, then he presents Islam to her. So if she accepts Islam, she will remain his wife. And if she refuses, the judge will cause separation between them. And this separation will not be a divorce. The effect of presenting Islam has passed earlier. And this separation is not divorce because the separation occurs due to the woman's refusal. And divorce does not come from the woman; rather separation comes from her side. Therefore, according to all, it will be considered separation.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This is a ruling statement regarding the case where a husband converts to Islam but his wife is a Zoroastrian (majusiyya). The Hanafi ruling is that the husband must present Islam to her. If she converts, the marriage remains valid. If she refuses, the qadi (judge) separates them, and this separation is not a divorce (talaq) but rather an annulment (faskh). The commentary explains that the reason it is not a divorce is that the wife is the cause of the separation through her refusal, and divorce is only validly issued by the husband. Hence, the legal consequence is that this separation does not count as one of the three divorces and does not have the rules of talaq. This ruling is consistent with the principle that a woman cannot initiate talaq; her actions can only cause faskh.

Key Terms
مجوسية (majusiyya): A Zoroastrian woman, one who follows the Magian religion.
عرض الاسلام (ard al-islam): Presenting the Islamic faith to a non-Muslim spouse after one spouse converts, giving them an opportunity to accept Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a husband who converts to Islam with a Zoroastrian wife, if the wife refuses Islam, what does the qadi do?
A) He divorces them
B) He separates them, and this separation is a divorce
C) He separates them, and this separation is not a divorce
D) He leaves the marriage intact

Key Takeaway
When a Zoroastrian wife refuses Islam after the husband's conversion, the judge separates them by faskh, not talaq, preserving the husband's number of divorces and requiring a new nikah for reconciliation.

Mahr Ruling After Separation Due to Wife's Refusal of Islam
Ruling on mahr with athar evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr when separation occurs due to the wife's refusal of Islam after the husband's conversion, and explain the condition of consummation.

Core Idea
Full mahr is due only if consummation occurred; without it, no mahr because the separation is caused by the wife.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on mahr when a marriage ends due to the wife's refusal to accept Islam after her husband's conversion. The key determinant is whether the marriage was consummated. The text provides a clear ruling supported by an athar from al-Thawri, illustrating the principle that mahr is earned through consummation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the two cases: full mahr if consummated, no mahr if not.
2
Locate the condition
The decisive condition is dukhul (consummation).
Some schools consider khalwa (seclusion) equivalent, but Hanafi here requires actual intercourse.
3
Examine the evidence
The athar from al-Thawri explicitly distinguishes based on dukhul, giving full sadaq if consummated.
The chain is from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Understand the rationale
Mahr is compensation for marital intimacy. If not consummated and wife causes separation, she forfeits the right.
Because the wealth was not yet delivered and she is the cause of dissolution.
5
Apply to a scenario
Imagine a husband converts, wife refuses, no consummation. Then no mahr.
If consummated, full mahr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان كان قد دخل بها فلها كمال المهر وان لم يكن دخل بها فلا مهر لها ۱۳۷ (۱۲) واذا اسلمت المرأة في اور اگر اس سے صحبت کی تو اس کے لئے پورا مہر ہوگا۔ اور اگر صحبت نہیں کی تو اس کے لئے مہر نہیں ہو گا۔ صحبت کر لی تھی پھر عورت نے اسلام لانے سے انکار کیا تو چونکہ مال سپرد کر دیا تھا اس لئے اس کو پورا مہر ملے گا۔ اور محبت سے پہلے انکار کیا تو مال ابھی سپرد نہیں کیا۔ اور تفریق کا سبب وہ بنی اس لئے اس کو کچھ نہیں ملے گا (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔عن الثورى قال اذا ارتدت المرأة ولها زوج ولم يدخل بها فلا صداق لها وقد انقطع ما بينهما فان كان قد دخل بها فلها الصداق كاملا (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب امرتدین ج سابع ص ۶۱ نمبر ۱۲۶۱۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ محبت نہ کی ہوتو کچھ نہیں ملے گا اور صحبت کی ہو تو پورا مہر ملے گا۔ حاشیہ : (ب) حضرت نوری فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر عورت مرتد ہو جائے اور اس کا شوہر ہو جس نے صحبت نہ کی ہو تو اس کو مہر نہیں ملے گا اور نکاح ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ اور اگر اس سے صحبت کر چکا ہو تو اس کو پورا مہر ملے گا۔
If he had consummated the marriage with her, then she gets the full mahr; if he had not consummated with her, then no mahr for her. And if he had intercourse, then for her is the full mahr. And if he did not have intercourse, then for her is no mahr. He had intercourse then the woman refused Islam, because the wealth was already delivered, so she gets full mahr. If refusal occurred before intercourse, wealth not yet delivered, and she became the cause of separation, so she gets nothing. (2) There is evidence from the athar: from al-Thawri, he said: If a woman apostatizes and she has a husband, and he has not consummated with her, then no sadaq for her, and what is between them is severed; if he had consummated with her, then she gets the full sadaq. (b) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on apostates, vol. 7, p. 61, no. 12618) From this athar it is known that if intercourse did not occur, she gets nothing; if it occurred, she gets full mahr. Margin note (b): Hazrat Nuri says that if a woman apostatizes and her husband has not consummated with her, then she gets no mahr and the marriage is broken; if he had consummated with her, then she gets full mahr.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on mahr (dower) when the separation occurs after the husband's conversion and the wife refuses Islam, analogous to the case of apostasy. The Hanafi position is bifurcated by consummation: if the marriage was consummated (dakhala biha), the wife receives the full mahr because the marital rights have been exchanged; if not consummated, she receives no mahr because the marriage ended before any rights were transferred, and she is the cause of the dissolution. The text cites an athar from al-Thawri regarding apostasy to support this ruling. The margin note (b) confirms the same rule from another authority. The underlying principle is that mahr is fully earned by consummation, and if the separation occurs before consummation due to the wife's action (here her refusal of Islam, akin to apostasy), no mahr is due.

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): The dower given by the husband to the wife as an obligation of marriage, often specified in the contract.
صداق (sadaq): Synonym for mahr, used in the athar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on mahr if the husband converts, the wife refuses Islam, and the marriage had not been consummated?
A) She gets full mahr
B) She gets half mahr
C) She gets no mahr
D) She gets mahr based on the husband's wealth

Key Takeaway
Full mahr is due only if consummation occurred; without it, no mahr because the separation is caused by the wife.

Woman Converts in Dar al-Harb: Separation After 'Iddah
Ruling with proof on conversion and 'iddah in Dar al-Harb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a woman's conversion in Dar al-Harb leads to separation, explain the role of the 'iddah, and cite the proof from the story of Ikrimah's wife.

Core Idea
Conversion in Dar al-Harb does not immediately dissolve marriage; the 'iddah is a waiting period for the husband to also convert.

This lesson addresses a nuanced situation: a woman in non-Muslim territory accepts Islam while her husband remains a non-Muslim. Because she is in Dar al-Harb, she cannot immediately leave or present Islam to him. The Hanafi school defers the separation to provide an opportunity for the husband to convert, using the 'iddah as a timeframe. The precedent from the Companion Ikrimah ibn Abi Jahl supports this approach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a woman's conversion to Islam in Dar al-Harb. The Hanafi ruling is that separation (faskh) does not occur immediately but is postponed until three menstrual periods pass.
If the husband converts during this 'iddah, the marriage is preserved.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ikrimah's wife as reported by al-Zuhri, found in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah. It describes that Ikrimah's wife converted first, then he converted while she was in 'iddah, and she was returned to him.
This indicates that during the 'iddah, the marriage is still potentially revivable.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The fact that she was returned to him because he converted during the 'iddah implies that before the 'iddah ends, the marriage can be restored, and after the 'iddah, separation becomes final.
The 'iddah serves as a waiting period for the husband to consider Islam.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i also uses the completion of 'iddah as the point of separation, but the Hanafi school emphasizes the 'iddah as a window for conversion rather than a mere terminal point.
Both schools agree on the practical outcome: separation after completed 'iddah if no conversion.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi, supported by the practice of the Companions as seen in the story of Ikrimah.
The ruling is based on a sound athar (narration) that was applied during the Prophet's time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۸۳۷) (۱۱۲) اگر عورت دار الحرب میں اسلام لے آئے تو فرقت واقع نہیں ہوگی یہاں تک کہ تین حیض گزر جائے۔ پس جب تین حیض گزر جائے تو اس کے شوہر سے بائنہ ہو جائے گی۔ دار الحرب لم تقع الفرقة عليها حتى تحيض ثلث حيض فاذا حاضت بانت من زوجها عورت دار الحرب میں اسلام لے آئے تو تین حیض گزرنے پر تفریق ہوگی۔ دار الحرب میں ہونے کی وجہ سے شوہر پر اسلام پیش نہیں کر سکتے۔ اور اسلام لانے کو تفریق کا سبب نہیں بنا سکتے۔ اس لئے عدت گزرنے کو تفریق کا سبب بنائیں گے۔ جیسا کہ امام شافعی نے عدت گزرنے کو تفریق کا سبب بنایا (۲) اس بارے میں سنن بیہقی کی حدیث گزرچکی ہے (۳) عن الزهرى ان امرأة عكرمة بن ابى جهل اسلمت قبله ثم اسلم وهي في العدة فردت اليه وذلك على عهد النبي الله (الف) (مصنف ابن ابی شبیبه ۶ ۸ ما قالوافیہ اذا اسلم وحی فی عد تھا من قال ھو احق بھاج رابع ص ۱۱۱، نمبر ۱۸۳۱۱) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عدت میں شوہر مسلمان ہو جائے تو عورت اس کی بیوی رہے گی۔ اور عدت گزر جائے تو تفریق ہو جائے گی۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عکرمہ کی بیوی ان سے پہلے مسلمان ہوئی پھر وہ مسلمان ہوئے جبکہ وہ عدت میں تھی تو بیوی ان کو لوٹا دی گئی۔ اور یہ معاملہ حضور کے زمانے میں ہوا
(1837) (112) If a woman embraces Islam in Dar al-Harb, separation will not occur until three menstrual periods pass. Then when three menstrual periods pass, she becomes irrevocably separated from her husband. In Dar al-Harb, separation does not occur for her until she menstruates three times; when she menstruates, she becomes separated from her husband. A woman embraces Islam in Dar al-Harb, so after three menstrual periods separation occurs. Because she is in Dar al-Harb, Islam cannot be presented to the husband. And embracing Islam itself cannot be made the cause of separation. Therefore, the passing of the 'iddah will be made the cause of separation. Just as Imam Shafi'i made the passing of the 'iddah the cause of separation. (2) The hadith regarding this has already passed in Sunan al-Bayhaqi. (3) From al-Zuhri: Indeed, the wife of Ikrimah ibn Abi Jahl embraced Islam before him, then he embraced Islam while she was in 'iddah, and she was returned to him. That was during the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him). (a) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, etc.) From this athar it is known that if the husband becomes Muslim during the 'iddah, the woman remains his wife; and if the 'iddah passes, then separation occurs. Margin note (a): Hazrat Ikrimah's wife embraced Islam before him, then he embraced Islam while she was in 'iddah, so the wife was returned to him. And this matter happened during the time of the Prophet.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This lesson addresses the scenario where a woman in Dar al-Harb (non-Muslim territory) converts to Islam. Since her husband is not present in Dar al-Islam, Islam cannot be presented to him immediately. The Hanafi ruling postpones the separation until the completion of three menstrual periods (the 'iddah of separation). If the woman completes three menses without her husband converting, then she becomes irrevocably separated (ba'in). The rationale is that the separation cannot be immediate because the husband is unavailable for presentation of Islam, so the 'iddah acts as a waiting period. The commentary references Imam al-Shafi'i's view that the passing of 'iddah causes separation, and then cites the story of Ikrimah ibn Abi Jahl's wife: she converted first, then he converted during her 'iddah, and she was returned to him by the Prophet's command, indicating that if the husband converts within the 'iddah, the marriage is restored. This hadith supports the Hanafi view that the 'iddah is a period of waiting; if the husband converts within it, the marriage survives; if not, separation becomes final.

Key Terms
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Non-Muslim territory, where Islamic law is not enforced and hostilities may exist.
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after the dissolution of marriage, here used as the period after conversion before separation becomes final.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a woman converts to Islam in Dar al-Harb, when does the separation from her non-Muslim husband become final?
A) Immediately upon her conversion
B) After one menstrual period
C) After three menstrual periods
D) Only if she returns to Dar al-Islam

Key Takeaway
A woman's conversion in Dar al-Harb does not immediately end her marriage; she observes a waiting period of three menstrual cycles, and if her husband converts within that time, the marriage is restored.

Marriage Remains Valid When Husband of a Kitabiyya Converts
Ruling that marriage to a Jewish or Christian wife remains valid upon husband's conversion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the continuity of marriage when a Kitabi husband converts to Islam and justify it using the Quranic verse and the athar of Hani ibn Qubaysa.

Core Idea
A Kitabi husband's conversion to Islam does not dissolve the marriage if the wife is Kitabiyya.

When a non-Muslim man married to a Jewish or Christian woman embraces Islam, a question arises: must they separate because the husband is now Muslim? The Hanafi school rules that the marriage continues intact. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning, drawing on Quranic permission and the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The case: a Kitabi man (Jewish or Christian) who is married to a Kitabiyya woman (Jewish or Christian) converts to Islam. Determine the legal status of the marriage.
The wife remains non-Muslim (Kitabiyya).
2
State the Hanafi Ruling
The marriage remains valid and neither party needs to renew the contract. This is based on the principle that a Muslim man may marry a Kitabiyya woman, so conversion of the husband does not create incompatibility.
The ruling is unanimous among the three Hanafi imams.
3
Examine the Quranic Proof
Quote Quran 5:5, which permits Muslim men to marry chaste women from the People of the Book. Since the husband is now Muslim and the wife is Kitabiyya, the marriage falls under this permission.
The verse establishes the general permissibility of such unions.
4
Examine the Athar (Practice of the Companions)
The narration from Hani ibn Qubaysa: he came to Madinah with four Christian wives, converted to Islam, and Caliph Umar confirmed the wives with him. This shows the precedent that the marriage continues.
The athar is recorded in Sunan al-Bayhaqi and is considered evidence (hujja) in the Hanafi school.
5
Derive the Legal Principle
The key principle: a marriage valid at inception remains valid upon the husband's conversion because the underlying permissibility (ibahah) for a Muslim man to marry a Kitabiyya is unchanged.
This contrasts with cases where the wife is a mushrik (idolater) – then the marriage would be affected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا اسلم زوج الكتابية فهما على نكاحهما [ ۱۸۳۸] (۱۱۳) إذا كتابیہ کا شوہر مسلمان ہو جائے تو دونوں اپنے نکاح پر بحال رہیں گے۔ کتابیہ یعنی یہودیہ اور نصرانیہ کا شوہر مسلمان ہو گیا تو مسلمان کے تحت میں نصرانیہ اور یہودیہ ہو ئیں۔ اور مسلمان کے تحت میں کتابیہ ہو تو نکاح شروع سے جائز ہے۔ اس لئے یہ بھی جائز ہوگا۔ اس لئے دونوں کا نکاح بحال رہے گا۔ وجه اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن الحكم ان هاني بن قبيصة قدم المدينة فنزل على ابن عوف وتحته اربع نسوة نصرانيات فاسلم واقرهن عمر معه (ب) (سن للبیہقی ، باب الرجل يسلم وتحتة نصرانية ج سابع ص۱۹۰) اس اثر سے پتہ چلا کہ نصرانی مسلمان ہو جائے تو اس کے تحت میں نصرانیہ یا یہودیہ رہ سکتی ہیں (۲) آیت میں ہے۔ والمحصنات من المؤمنات والمحصنات من الذين أوتوا الكتاب م قبلكم اذا اتيتموهن أجورهن (آیت ۵ سورۃ المائدة (۵) اس آیت میں کتابیہ عورتوں سے نکاح کرنا حلال قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ حاشیہ : (ب) حضرت ہانی بن قبیصہ مدینہ آئے اور ابن عوف کے مہمان ہوئے۔ اور ان کے تحت چار نصرانی بیویاں تھیں۔ پس وہ مسلمان ہوئے اور عورتوں کو حضرت عمر نے ان کے ساتھ برقرار رکھا
And if the husband of a Kitabiyya (Scriptuary) embraces Islam, then they remain upon their marriage. (113) If the husband of a Kitabiyya becomes Muslim, then both will remain upon their marriage. Kitabiyya means Jewish or Christian woman; her husband becomes Muslim, so a Christian or Jewish woman remains under a Muslim. And when a Kitabiyya is under a Muslim, the marriage is valid from the beginning. Therefore this is also permissible. So both remain upon their marriage. Reason: There is evidence in the athar: from al-Hakam that Hani ibn Qubaysa arrived in Madinah and stayed with Ibn Awf, and under him were four Christian wives; so he embraced Islam and Umar confirmed them with him. (b) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on a man who embraces Islam while under him is a Christian woman, vol. 7, p. 190) From this athar it is known that if a Christian becomes Muslim, the Christian or Jewish woman can remain under him. (2) In the verse: 'And the chaste from among the believers and the chaste from among those who were given the Scripture before you, when you have given them their due compensation' (Quran 5:5). In this verse, marriage to Kitabi women is declared permissible. Margin note (b): Hazrat Hani ibn Qubaysa came to Madinah and stayed with Ibn Awf. Under him were four Christian wives. He became Muslim, and Umar confirmed the women with him.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This lesson deals with the ruling when a man who is a Kitabi (originally Jewish or Christian) converts to Islam while married to a Kitabiyya wife. The Hanafi position is that the marriage remains valid and unchanged because Islam permits a Muslim man to marry a Kitabiyya woman (as per Quran 5:5). Therefore, the conversion of the husband does not necessitate separation. The commentary provides two proofs: first, an athar that the companion Hani ibn Qubaysa converted and his four Christian wives were confirmed with him by Caliph Umar; second, the Quranic verse that explicitly allows marriage to chaste women from the People of the Book. This ruling is straightforward since the marriage was valid ab initio under Islamic law.

Key Terms
كتابية (kitabiyya): A woman from the People of the Book, i.e., Jewish or Christian.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the marriage when a man married to a Christian woman converts to Islam according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is dissolved immediately.
B) It remains valid and no new contract is needed.
C) The wife must convert within a certain period.
D) A new marriage contract is required.

Key Takeaway
A marriage to a Kitabiyya woman remains valid upon the husband's conversion to Islam because the Quran and Sunnah permit such unions.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Immediate Separation Upon Muslim Migration from Dar al-Harb
Ruling on immediate separation upon Muslim migration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a spouse's migration to Dar al-Islam as a Muslim immediately dissolves the marriage, and cite Quran 60:10 as evidence.

Core Idea
A spouse's migration to Dar al-Islam as a Muslim instantly dissolves the marriage—Quran 60:10 forbids holding to disbelieving spouses.

When one spouse embraces Islam and emigrates from enemy territory to the Muslim land, a critical legal question arises: does the marriage persist across the religious and territorial divide? The Hanafi school, guided by a clear Quranic command, rules that the marriage ends immediately upon entering Dar al-Islam. This lesson unpacks that ruling and the proof that supports it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the case involves one spouse (husband or wife) who has already converted to Islam and then physically migrates from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam.
The migration is a separate act after conversion; mere conversion without migration does not trigger this rule.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The ruling is that baynuna (irrevocable separation) occurs immediately upon the spouse's entry into Dar al-Islam. No waiting period is required.
The marriage is completely dissolved; the Muslim spouse is free to remarry.
3
Locate the Quranic proof
The primary evidence is Surah al-Mumtahana (60:10), which addresses believing women who emigrate and explicitly states that they are not lawful for disbelieving husbands, and vice versa.
The verse also commands Muslims not to 'hold to the marriage bonds of disbelieving women', which encompasses both genders by extension.
4
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The operative phrase 'wa la tumsiku bi 'isami al-kawafir' (hold not to marriage bonds with disbelieving women) indicates a general prohibition that, when combined with the migration context, demands immediate dissolution.
The imperative tone (لا تمسكوا) reinforces the obligation to sever the marital tie.
5
Note the cross-madhhab perspective
While the Hanafi school sticks to immediate dissolution, other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may allow a waiting period or consider the marriage still valid if the non-Muslim spouse later converts. Understand the Hanafi reliance on the apparent meaning of the verse.
This ikhtilaf stems from differing interpretations of the verse's scope and the role of post-migration conversion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا خرج احد الزوجين الينا من دار الحرب مسلما وقعت البينونة بينهما [ ۱۸۳۹] (۱۱۴) إذا میاں بیوی میں سے ایک دارالحرب سے ہماری طرف مسلمان ہو کر آئے تو بینونت واقع ہو جائے گی۔ بیوی شوہر میں سے ایک مسلمان ہو کر دار الحرب سے دار الاسلام آجائے تو دار الاسلام داخل ہوتے ہی جدائیگی واقع ہو جائے گی۔ اور بیوی نہیں رہے گی۔ يا أيها الذين آمنوا إذا جاءكم المؤمنات مهاجرات فامتحنوهن الله أعلم بإيمانهن فإن علمتموهن مؤمنات فلا ترجعوهن إلى الكفار لا هن حل لهم ولا هم يحلون لهن وآتوهم ما أنفقوا ولا جناح عليكم أن تنكحوهن إذا آتيتموهن أجورهن ولا تمسكوا بعصم الكوافر (ج ) ( آیت اسورة امتحیہ ۶۰) اس آیت میں ہے کہ عورت دار حاشیہ : (ج) اے ایمان والو اگر تمہارے پاس مومنہ عورتیں ہجرت کر کے آئیں تو ان کا امتحان لو۔ اور اللہ ان کے ایمان کو (باقی اگلے صفحہ پر )
And if one of the two spouses comes out to us from Dar al-Harb as a Muslim, baynuna (irrevocable separation) occurs between them. (114) If one of the husband and wife comes from Dar al-Harb to our side as a Muslim, then baynuna will occur. When one of them, husband or wife, becomes Muslim and comes from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam, upon entering Dar al-Islam, separation occurs immediately, and she will not remain a wife. 'O you who have believed, when the believing women come to you as emigrants, examine them. Allah is most knowing of their faith. And if you know them to be believers, then do not return them to the disbelievers; they are not lawful [wives] for them, nor are they lawful [husbands] for them. And give them what they have spent. And there is no blame upon you if you marry them when you have given them their due compensation. And hold not to marriage bonds with disbelieving women.' (Quran 60:10) In this verse it is that the woman [upon arrival]... Margin note (c): 'O you who have believed, if believing women come to you as emigrants, then examine them. And Allah is most knowing of their faith...' (continued on next page)
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This lesson addresses the scenario where one spouse (husband or wife) emigrates from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam having already converted to Islam before the journey. The Hanafi ruling is that the moment they enter Dar al-Islam, an irrevocable separation (baynuna) occurs between them, and they cannot remain married to a non-Muslim spouse still in Dar al-Harb. The primary evidence is Quran 60:10, which commands that believing women who migrate are not lawful for their disbelieving husbands, and conversely, Muslim men should not hold onto marriage bonds with disbelieving women. The verse indicates that migration and difference of religion at that point constitutes an insurmountable barrier. The commentary explains that separation occurs immediately upon entry into Dar al-Islam, because the spouse is now a Muslim and the other is not, and they cannot cohabit in Dar al-Islam due to religious differences. This is distinct from the previous cases where separation was delayed (like the woman in Dar al-Harb herself).

Key Terms
بينونة (baynuna): Irrevocable separation between spouses, making them strangers to each other.
مهاجرات (muhajirat): Female emigrants who left their homes in non-Muslim territory for Dar al-Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a husband from Dar al-Harb converts to Islam and migrates to Dar al-Islam, what happens to his marriage to his non-Muslim wife?
A) The marriage continues until she also converts
B) The marriage is immediately dissolved
C) The marriage is put on hold for three months
D) The marriage becomes invalid only if he remarries

Key Takeaway
Upon entering Dar al-Islam as a Muslim, the marriage is immediately dissolved due to difference of religion, as per the command in Quran 60:10.

beginner
6 min
Husband of Kitabiyya Converts: Marriage Remains Valid
Ruling with proof from Quran and athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a Kitabi husband converts and explain the dalil from Quran and athar.

Core Idea
A husband's conversion does not dissolve a valid marriage to a Kitabiyya; it continues.

A common question is what happens when a non-Muslim husband embraces Islam while his wife remains a Kitabiyya. Does the marriage need to be renewed or dissolved? The Hanafi school has a clear position, supported by the Quran and the practice of the Sahaba. This lesson explores that ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific scenario? A man married to a Kitabiyya woman converts to Islam. The ruling: the marriage remains valid and binding ('فهما على نكاحهما').
The act is the husband's conversion, not the wife's.
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs are cited: an athar from Umar ibn al-Khattab concerning Hani ibn Qubaysa, and Quran 5:5 which permits marrying chaste women from the People of the Book.
The athar is a practice of a Companion, which is a source in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does Quran 5:5 prove the ruling? The verse allows Muslim men to marry Kitabiyyat. If initial marriage is allowed, then conversion after marriage does not invalidate it; the same permission applies. The athar shows direct application by a Companion.
The verse is general ('على نكاحهما' is not explicitly in the verse but implies continuity).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require separation if the husband converts and the wife does not, arguing that conversion changes the husband's status. The Hanafi school disagrees.
The ikhtilaf is about whether the marriage continues or must be renewed.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) because of the clear athar and the general permission of the Quran. It is also more practical, preserving the family unit.
No explicit tarjih authority is cited in this passage, but it is the standard Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا اسلم زوج الكتابية فهما على نكاحهما. عن الحكم ان هاني بن قبيصة قدم المدينة فنزل على ابن عوف وتحته اربع نسوة نصرانيات فاسلم واقرهن عمر معه. والمحصنات من المؤمنات والمحصنات من الذين أوتوا الكتاب م قبلكم اذا اتيتموهن أجورهن.
And if the husband of a Kitabiyya converts to Islam, they remain upon their marriage. From al-Hakam that Hani ibn Qubaysa came to Madinah and stayed with Ibn Awf, and under him were four Christian women, so he converted and Umar kept them with him. And chaste women from the believers and chaste women from those who were given the Scripture before you, when you give them their due compensation.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This lesson presents a ruling with its proofs. The ruling: if a husband who is a Kitabi (Christian or Jew) converts to Islam, his marriage to his Kitabiyya wife remains valid. The Hanafi position cites an athar where Hani ibn Qubaysa had four Christian wives upon converting, and Umar ibn al-Khattab allowed him to keep them. Additionally, Quran 5:5 permits marrying chaste women from the People of the Book, implying that a Muslim man can remain married to a Kitabiyya. This ruling is consistent with the principle that a Muslim may marry a Kitabiyya initially, so conversion after the fact does not sever the tie.

Key Terms
كتابية (kitābiyya): A woman from the People of the Book (Jewish or Christian).
زوج الكتابية (zawj al-kitābiyya): The husband of a Kitabiyya woman, who is himself a Kitabi initially.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this lesson, what happens if a Kitabiyya's husband converts to Islam?
A) The marriage is immediately dissolved.
B) The marriage remains valid and they stay together.
C) The wife must also convert within three days.
D) The marriage becomes temporarily suspended until she converts.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that conversion of a Kitabi husband does not invalidate a valid marriage to a Kitabiyya; the marriage continues as before.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
6 min
Immediate Dissolution of Marriage Upon One Spouse's Emigration as Muslim
Ruling with Quranic evidence and athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when one spouse emigrates from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam as a Muslim, and explain the Quranic evidence (60:10) and the athar from Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
Separation occurs immediately when one spouse enters Dar al-Islam as a Muslim – difference of dar dissolves the marriage.

This lesson addresses a key scenario in Islamic family law: the fate of a marriage when one spouse converts to Islam and emigrates from non-Muslim territory. The Hanafi school, relying on Quran 60:10 and a Companion's statement, holds that the marriage is immediately dissolved. We will examine the ruling, its proof, and compare it with the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the case involves one spouse leaving Dar al-Harb and entering Dar al-Islam as a Muslim, while the other remains in Dar al-Harb as a non-Muslim.
The ruling applies whether the emigrant is the husband or the wife.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The marriage is immediately dissolved (baynuna) upon entry into Dar al-Islam. No waiting period or additional action is needed.
The dissolution is permanent; the spouses become irrevocably separated.
3
Locate the Quranic proof
Refer to Quran 60:10, which commands not to return believing women to disbelieving husbands and prohibits holding onto the marriage bonds of disbelieving women.
The verse is directly about emigrant believing women.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The verse explicitly forbids returning believing women to disbelieving husbands, indicating that the marriage ties are broken. The imperative 'do not hold onto the marriage bonds' implies immediate dissolution.
This is a qat'i dalalah according to Hanafi usul.
5
Note the athar from Ibn Abbas and Ata
Ibn Abbas said: 'If a Christian woman converts before her husband by an hour, she becomes forbidden to him.' Ata added that a new marriage and dower would be needed if they wish to reunite.
This supports that even a brief time difference ends the marriage.
6
Discuss the cross-madhhab dispute
The Shafi'i school holds that if the non-Muslim spouse converts within the idda, the marriage is restored. The Hanafi school rejects this, emphasizing the immediate and permanent effect of the difference of dar.
This is a thamarah al-khilaf with practical consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا خرج احد الزوجين الينا من دار الحرب مسلما وقعت البينونة بينهما. يا ايها الذين آمنوا اذا جاءكم المؤمنات مهاجرات فامتحنوهن الله اعلم بايمانهن فان علمتموهن مؤمنات فلا ترجعوهن الى الكفار لا هن حل لهم ولا هم يحلون لهن واتوهم ما انفقوا ولا جناح عليكم ان تنكحوهن اذا اتيتموهن أجورهن ولا تمسكوا بعصم الكوافر. عن ابن عباس اذا اسلمت النصرانية قبل زوجها بساعة حرمت عليه. وقال عطاء لا الا ان تشاء هي بنكاح جديد وصداق.
And if one of the two spouses comes out to us from Dar al-Harb as a Muslim, separation occurs between them. O you who believe, when believing women come to you as emigrants, examine them; Allah knows best their faith. Then if you know them to be believers, do not return them to the disbelievers; they are not lawful for them, nor are they lawful for them. And give them what they have spent. And there is no blame upon you if you marry them when you give them their due. And do not hold onto the marriage bonds of disbelieving women. From Ibn Abbas: If a Christian woman converts before her husband by an hour, she becomes forbidden to him. And Ata said: No, unless she desires it with a new marriage and a new dower.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This lesson deals with the scenario where one spouse leaves Dar al-Harb and arrives in Dar al-Islam as a Muslim. The ruling is that separation (baynuna) occurs immediately upon entering Dar al-Islam. The Hanafi evidence is primarily from Quran 60:10, which commands not to return believing emigrant women to their disbelieving husbands and prohibits holding onto the marriage bonds of disbelieving women. This implies that the marriage is dissolved. Additionally, an athar from Ibn Abbas states that if a Christian woman converts before her husband, she becomes forbidden to him immediately, even if he converts later during the waiting period. Ata's statement supports the view that if the husband converts in the idda, a new marriage is required. This establishes that difference of dar (dar al-harb vs. dar al-islam) dissolves the marriage.

Key Terms
بينونة (baynūna): Complete separation between spouses; the marriage is irrevocably dissolved.
دار الحرب (dār al-ḥarb): Territory under non-Muslim rule where Islamic law is not dominant.
عدة (ʿidda): Waiting period after separation; here, if husband converts during idda, it does not restore the marriage per Hanafi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens when a wife emigrates from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam as a Muslim, while her husband remains a non-Muslim in Dar al-Harb?
A) The marriage remains valid until the idda expires.
B) The marriage is immediately dissolved upon her entry into Dar al-Islam.
C) The husband can reclaim her if he converts within the idda.
D) She must wait for a divorce from her husband.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that when one spouse leaves Dar al-Harb for Dar al-Islam as a Muslim, the marriage is immediately and permanently dissolved, based on Quran 60:10 and the practice of Ibn Abbas.
